Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
The Four Principles of Shari'ah: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas
States the three primary usul and Qiyas as the fourth derived principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four principles of Shari'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain why Qiyas is considered derivative and not independent.

Core Idea
Qiyas is the fourth principle but derived from the three primary sources: Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'.

This passage introduces the foundational sources of Islamic law from a Hanafi perspective. The author deliberately uses the phrase 'usul al-shar'' to emphasize that these principles apply to both fiqh and theology. Understanding the hierarchy between the primary sources and Qiyas is crucial for correct legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three primary principles
Locate the first principles mentioned: Kitab (Quran), Sunnah, and Ijma'. Note that they are described as 'three' and are the foundation.
These three are agreed upon by all Sunni schools.
2
Understand the choice of 'shar'' over 'fiqh'
Read why the author said 'usul al-shar'' instead of 'usul al-fiqh'. The reason given is that these sources are also principles of kalam (theology).
This shows the interdisciplinary scope of these sources.
3
Locate Qiyas as the fourth principle
Find the statement that Qiyas is the fourth principle. Note the qualifying phrase 'al-mustanbit min hadhihi al-usul'.
This qualification restricts Qiyas to legal analogy derived from the three sources.
4
Distinguish Qiyas from the first three
The passage says Qiyas is 'asl min wajh wa far' min wajh' (a source in some respects, a branch in others). Understand that unlike the first three, Qiyas is not independent; it relies on them.
This distinction is key in Hanafi usul: the first three are 'asl min kull wajh' (original in every respect).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصنف ع ا اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ شریعت کے اصول یعنی ادلہ تین ہیں، کتاب اللہ ،سنت اور اجماع امت ،مصنف نے اصول الشرع کہا اصول الفقہ نہیں فرمایا، کیونکہ کتاب سنت اور اجماع جس طرح فقہ کے اصول ہیں ایسے ہی علم کلام کے بھی اصول ہیں اور لفظ شرع چونکہ فقہ اور علم کلام دونوں میں عام ہے، اس لئے اصول الشرع فرمایا تا کہ دونوں کو شامل ہو جائے۔ مذکورہ تین اصول کے بعد چوتھی اصل وہ قیاس ہے جو مذکورہ تین اصول و دلائل سے مستنبط ہو، المستنبط من هذه الاصول کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ کر دیا کہ یہاں مطلق قیاس مراد نہیں بلکہ قیاس شرعی مراد ہے۔ نیز یہاں الاصل الرابع کہہ کر قیاس کو پہلے تین اصول سے الگ بیان کیا، اس لئے کہ قیاس من وجہ اصل ہے، من وجہ فرع ہے برخلاف پہلے تین اصول کے کہ وہ من کل وجہ اصل ہیں۔
The author, may Allah have mercy on him, says that the principles of Shari'ah — i.e., the evidences — are three: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the Ummah. The author said 'usul al-shar' (principles of Shari'ah) and not 'usul al-fiqh' because the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma' are principles of both fiqh and kalam, and the word 'shar'' is common to both fiqh and kalam, so he said 'usul al-shar'' to include both. After the mentioned three principles, the fourth principle is analogy (qiyas) which is derived from the aforementioned three principles and evidences. The qualification 'al-mustanbit min hadhihi al-usul' indicates that what is meant here is not absolute analogy, but rather legal analogy (qiyas shar'i). Also, by calling it 'al-asl al-rabi'', Qiyas is separated from the first three principles because Qiyas is an original principle in some respects and a branch in others, unlike the first three principles which are original principles in every respect.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage clarifies the foundational sources of Islamic law according to the Hanafi school. The commentator explains that the author of the matn (likely al-Husami) deliberately used the term 'usul al-shar'' instead of 'usul al-fiqh' because the three primary sources — Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' — are also principles of theology (kalam). The commentator notes that Qiyas is the fourth principle but is derivative: it is an 'asl' in the sense that it is a source of law, but it is a 'far'' because it relies on the first three. This distinction underscores the hierarchy: the first three are independent and original, while Qiyas is dependent and secondary. The phrase 'al-mustanbit min hadhihi al-usul' restricts Qiyas to legal analogy, excluding non-legal analogies. This is standard Hanafi usul: the four sources are Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, with Qiyas being a valid source when no direct text is available.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): A source or principle of Shari'ah; in this passage, each of the four evidences (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas).
قیاس (qiyas): Legal analogy that derives a ruling for a new case from an original case (asl) based on a common effective cause ('illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author use the term 'usul al-shar'' instead of 'usul al-fiqh'?
A) Because the principles are for worship only.
B) To include both fiqh and kalam.
C) Because the author wrote a book on theology.
D) To emphasize that these are only for family law.

Key Takeaway
The four principles of Shari'ah are Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, with Qiyas being a derivative that must be based on the first three.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Two Types of Connection (Ittisal) Between Cause and Effect
Expounding the two types of causal connection in sabab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the strong connection ('illah-hukm) and the weak connection (sabab-musabbab), and state the direction of permissible isti'arah in each case.

Core Idea
The strength of the causal connection determines the direction of permissible metaphorical usage.

In Hanafi usul, not all causal connections are equal. The relationship between an 'illah (effective cause) and its hukm is reciprocal and strong, while the relationship between a pure sabab and its musabbab is one-sided. This difference governs when we can use one term to refer to the other (isti'arah). This lesson unpacks the two types as explained by the commentator on Al-Husami.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
The text distinguishes between the connection of hukm with 'illah (type 1) and the connection of the branch (far') with a pure sabab (type 2).
2
Analyze the strength
For type 1, the 'illah is placed specifically for the hukm; each implies the other. For type 2, the musabbab depends on the sabab but not vice versa.
3
Derive the isti'arah rule
From the strength: for type 1, isti'arah is bidirectional; for type 2, only from sabab to musabbab (except when musabbab is specific to sabab).
The exception is when the musabbab is exclusive to the sabab, e.g., wine is specific to grapes.
4
Apply to the example of milk and shira
Milk (ownership) and shira (purchase) have a strong 'illah-hukm connection, so either can be used to intend the other.

ان اشتريت عبد ا فهو حر - اگر میں غلام کو خریدوں تو وہ آزاد ہے، پس اس نے آدھا خریدا پھر اس کو بیچ دیا پھر دوسرا آدھا خریدا تو یہ دوسرا آدھا آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اگر ان ملکت عبداً فهو حر کہا پھر آدھا لے تو دوسرا آدھا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن جس صورت میں متکلم کا فائدہ ہو رہا ہے اور اس پر تخفیف ہورہی ہے اس میں قضاء اس کی بات نہیں مانی جائے گی یعنی قاضی اس کی بات تسلیم نہیں کرے گا، لہذا ملک بولکر شراء مراد لے رہا ہے تو دیا نہ وقضاء اس کی بات معتبر ہے اور اگر شراء بولکر ملک مراد لے رہا ہے تو چونکہ اس میں متکلم کا فائدہ ہے لہذا د یا نہ تو اس کی بات قبول ہوگی ،مگر قضاء معتبر نہ ہوگی ، اس وجہ سے نہیں کہ استعارہ بیچ نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے متہم بالکذب ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تنبیہ: ملک وشراء کے درمیان مذکور فرق اس وقت ہے جب اس نے عبداً نکرہ استعمال کیا ہو، اگر نکرہ نہ لائے بلکہ مفعول کو معین کر کے کہے ان اشتَرَيْتُ هَذَا الْعَبْدَ، يَا إِنْ مَلَكْتُ هَذَا الْعَبد تو دونوں صورتوں میں دوسرا آدھا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ وَالثَّانِي إِتِصالُ الْفَرْعِ بِمَا هُوَ سَبَبْ مَحْضٌ لَيْسَ بِعِلَّةٍ وُضِعَتْ لَهُ كَاِتِّصَالِ زَوَالِ مِلْكِ الْمُتْعَةِ بِالْفَاظِ الْعِتْقِ تَبْعًا لِزَوَالِ مِلْكِ الرَّقْبَةِ وَإِنَّهُ يُؤْجِبْ اِسْتِعَارَةَ الْاَصْلِ لِلْفَرْع وَالسَّبَبَ لِلْحُكُم دُونَ عَكْسِهِ لِأَنَّ اِتِّصَالَ الْفَرْعِ بِالْاَصْلِ فِي حَقِّ الْأَصْلِ فِي حُكْمِ الْعَدَمِ لِاسْتِغْنَائِهِ عَنِ الْفَرْعِ ترجمہ :- اتصال سبی کی دوسری قسم فرع (حکم ، مسبب ) کا اتصال ہے اس چیز کے ساتھ جو سبب محض ہے ایسی علت نہیں ہے جو فرع کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہو، جیسے ملک متعہ کے زوال کا اتصال عتق کے الفاظ سے ملک رقبہ کے زوال
So that the entire slave does not come into his ownership collectively. Then if he intended by one of the two [terms] the other, his intention will be acted upon in both places, but in the place where there is a reduction (benefit) for him, it will not be accepted in qada (judicial decision), but it will be accepted in din (conscience/moral obligation). Explanation: It was mentioned previously that the connection of sabab has two types; here these types are being explained. The first type is the connection of the hukm with the 'illah, i.e., the connection between 'illah and ma'lul. For example, milk (ownership) and shira (purchase): shira is the 'illah and milk is the ma'lul (hukm). The connection between 'illah and ma'lul is strong; therefore, isti'arah (metaphorical use) is permitted from both sides, i.e., one can intend the ma'lul by uttering the 'illah, and also intend the 'illah by uttering the ma'lul. As for sabab and musabbab, the connection is weak; therefore, isti'arah from both sides is not correct. The reason why the connection is strong in the first and not strong in the second is that in Shari'ah, 'illah is that which is placed for a hukm. Hence, if a hukm is not conceivable in a place, then the 'illah is also not legislated. For example, if milk is not conceivable in a place, then bay' is also not legislated. Thus, both the existence and obligatoriness of the hukm are attributed to the 'illah, meaning that the hukm both exists and is obligatory due to the 'illah. It became known that the connection between 'illah and ma'lul (hukm) is strong: whenever the 'illah exists, the hukm exists, and whenever the hukm exists, the 'illah exists. Because the 'illah is legislated only for the hukm, and the hukm is established only from the 'illah. So both are in need of each other, so the connection between them is strong. As for sabab and musabbab, this is not the case, because the musabbab is in need of the sabab, but the sabab does not need the musabbab. That is, for the existence of the musabbab, the sabab is necessary, but for the existence of the sabab, it is not necessary that the musabbab exist. So the need is from one side. Therefore, intending the musabbab by uttering the sabab is correct, but intending the sabab by uttering the musabbab is not correct. Because the reality of isti'arah is that the malzum (logical antecedent) is uttered to intend the lazim (logical consequent), not the lazim to intend the malzum. So when the musabbab is in need of the sabab and not the sabab in need of the musabbab, then the musabbab is the needer (muhtaj) and the sabab is the needed (muhtaj ilayh). The needer is the lazim, and the needed is the malzum. Therefore, it is correct to utter the malzum (i.e., the sabab) intending the lazim (i.e., the musabbab), and it is not correct to utter the musabbab intending the sabab. Except where the musabbab is specific to the sabab, then one can intend the musabbab by uttering the sabab, like the verse "Inni arani a'siru khamran" (I see myself pressing wine) where by khamr (wine) grapes are intended. So khamr is the musabbab and grapes are the sabab, and the musabbab (khamr) is uttered intending the sabab (grapes) because here the musabbab is specific to the sabab, i.e., wine is not made without grapes. Example of isti'arah from both sides: The author is branching out a ruling on this. As a preliminary, he says: If someone said, "If I buy a slave, he is free," then he bought half, then sold it, then bought the other half, then this second half becomes free. And if he said, "If I own a slave, he is free," then bought half and sold it, then bought the other half, then this second half does not become free. The difference between them is that in purchase, it is not necessary for the entire slave to be together; if he buys half by half, in custom he will still be called a buyer of the slave. But for ownership, it is necessary that the entire slave be together in his ownership. Therefore, if he bought the first half and sold it, then bought the second half, the entire slave does not come into his ownership collectively because the first half left his ownership, so in custom he will not be called the owner of the slave. This is the difference between purchase and ownership. After this preliminary, now understand the issue: If someone said "In ishtaraytu 'abdan fahuwa hurr" and intends ownership, or said "In malktu 'abdan fahuwa hurr" and intends purchase, then isti'arah from both sides is correct because between milk and shira there is a connection of 'illah and ma'lul. Therefore, his statement will be accepted in din and qada. But in the case where the speaker benefits and there is a reduction for him, in qada his statement will not be accepted, i.e., the judge will not accept it. So if he says milk intending purchase, then in both din and qada his statement is valid. But if he says purchase intending milk, then because there is a benefit for the speaker, it will be accepted in din but not in qada. This is not because the isti'arah is invalid, but because he is accused of lying. Note: The mentioned difference between milk and shira applies when he used 'abdan as indefinite; if he did not use indefinite but specified the object, saying "In ishtaraytu hadha al-'abda" or "In malktu hadha al-'abda", then in both cases the second half becomes free. And the second [type] is the connection of the branch (far') with that which is a pure sabab, not an 'illah placed for it, like the connection of the removal of milk al-mut'ah (right of enjoyment) with the words of 'itq (emancipation), following the removal of milk al-raqabah (ownership of the corpus). And this necessitates the isti'arah of the asl (origin) for the far' and of the sabab for the hukm, but not the reverse, because the connection of the far' with the asl, in respect of the asl, is like non-existent due to the asl's independence from the far'. Translation: The second type of ittisal of sabab is the connection of the far' (hukm, musabbab) with that which is a pure sabab, not an 'illah placed for it, like the connection of the removal of milk al-mut'ah with the words of 'itq, following the removal of milk al-raqabah. And it necessitates the isti'arah of the asl for the far' and of the sabab for the hukm, but not the reverse, because the connection of the far' with the asl, in respect of the asl, is like non-existent due to the asl's independence from the far'.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the two types of 'ittisal al-sabab' (connection of the cause) as used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that the first type is the connection between an 'illah (effective cause) and its hukm (ruling). This connection is strong because the 'illah is legislated specifically for the hukm; each implies the other. Therefore, metaphorical use (isti'arah) is permissible in both directions: one can utter the 'illah and intend the hukm, or utter the hukm and intend the 'illah. An example is the relationship between 'shira' (purchase) as 'illah and 'milk' (ownership) as hukm. In the scenario of a conditional emancipation, if someone says 'If I buy a slave, he is free,' the condition is satisfied by partial purchases because 'buying' applies even if the slave is not fully owned at once. However, if he says 'If I own a slave, he is free,' the condition requires full ownership at the moment of utterance; partial ownership followed by sale prevents the condition from being met. The second type of connection is between a pure sabab and its musabbab (effect), where the sabab is not an 'illah specifically placed for the musabbab. An example is the words of emancipation ('itq): when one says 'You are free,' the removal of ownership of the corpus (milk al-raqabah) occurs, and following that, the removal of the right of enjoyment (milk al-mut'ah). Here, the sabab (the words of 'itq) leads to the musabbab (removal of milk al-raqabah), and then secondarily to another musabbab (removal of milk al-mut'ah). This secondary effect is dependent on the first, but the sabab does not require the secondary effect. Consequently, isti'arah is only allowed from sabab to musabbab (uttering the cause intending the effect), not the reverse. The text emphasizes that when the musabbab is specific to the sabab (like wine being specific to grapes), the reverse isti'arah is possible. The author also discusses the judicial implications: when the speaker's intention differs from the literal meaning, his statement is accepted in din (conscience) and qada (court) except when he stands to benefit; in that case, the court does not accept it due to suspicion of lying. This entire discussion illustrates the nuanced Hanafi approach to legal language, where the strength of causal connections determines the scope of metaphorical interpretation.

Key Terms
اتصال السبی (Ittiṣāl al-sabab): The connection between a cause (sabab/ʿillah) and its effect (musabbab/ḥukm). Two types are distinguished: strong (illah-hukm) and weak (sabab-musabbab).
استعارہ (Istiʿārah): Metaphorical usage where one term is used to intend another due to a connection between them. Permissibility depends on the strength of the connection.
سبب محض (Sabab maḥḍ): A pure cause that is not an ʿillah specifically placed for a ruling; it brings about an effect but does not have a reciprocal relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main factor that determines whether isti'arah is permissible in both directions?
A) The strength of the causal connection.
B) The clarity of the terms.
C) The intention of the speaker.
D) The authority of the text.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the direction of permissible isti'arah depends on whether the causal connection is strong (illah-hukm) or weak (sabab-musabbab).

The Impossibility of Combining Haqiqah and Majaz in One Utterance
Explaining the rule that haqiqah and majaz cannot be intended simultaneously

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that haqiqah and majaz cannot be intended together in one utterance and explain the qiyas analogy that supports it.

Core Idea
A single word cannot carry both literal and figurative meanings simultaneously—just as a garment is either owned or borrowed.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational principle of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the impossibility of combining the literal (ḥaqīqa) and figurative (majāz) meanings of a word in a single utterance. The author uses a clear analogy to a garment that cannot be both owned and borrowed at the same time. Then, a practical case from Imam Muhammad's Al-Jamiʿ al-Kabīr demonstrates how this rule operates in legal interpretation, showing that when the literal meaning is intended, the figurative becomes void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Recognize the statement: it is impossible for one utterance to intend both haqiqah and majaz simultaneously. This is the central rule of the passage.
2
Understand the Analogy
Examine the qiyas jaliy: a garment on a wearer cannot be both owned and borrowed at the same time. Similarly, a word at a given instance must be either haqiqah or majaz.
The analogy highlights mutual exclusivity, not simultaneous possession.
3
Analyze the Applied Case
Work through the case from Al-Jamiʿ al-Kabīr: a free Arab (with no walaʿ) bequeaths one-third to his mawālī. The word 'mawālī' is literal for his direct freed slave (muʿtiq), but figurative for the freed slave's own clients. Since the literal meaning is intended, the figurative fails.
The testator has only one freed slave, so that slave takes half of the one-third; the remainder returns to the heirs.
4
Extract the Usul Principle
Conclude that when a text can bear both literal and figurative meanings, the literal is the default. The figurative is only valid if the literal is impossible. This prevents confusion in legal interpretation.
Hanafis prioritize haqiqah unless a qarīna (contextual indicator) redirects to majaz.

ایسا نہیں ہوسکتا ہے، پس حقیقی معنی مملوک کے مانند ہے اور مجازی معنی عاریت کے درجہ میں ہے۔ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي الْجَامِعِ لَوْاَنَّ عَرَبِيَا لَا وَلَاءَ عَلَيْهِ أَوْصَى بِثْلُثِ مَالِهِ لِمَوَالِيْهِ وَلَهُ مُعْتَقٌ وَاحِدٌ فَاسْتَحَقَ النِّصْفَ كَانَ النِّصْفُ الْبَاقِي مَرْدُودًا إِلَى الْوَرَثَةِ وَلَا يَكُونُ لِمَوَالِي مَوْلَاهُ لِاَنَّ الْحَقِيقَة أريدَتْ بِهَذَا اللَّفْظِ کا معتق مجازی معنی ہوئے۔ دوسری بات یہ سمجھ لیں کہ غلام کے مال میں آزاد کرنے والے کا جو حق ہوتا ہے، غلام کے مرنے کے بعد وہ ولاء کہلاتا ہے۔ اور یہ بھی سمجھ لیں کہ عربی حر الاصل ہوتا ہے، عربوں میں رقیت نہیں ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ عربوں میں دوہی باتیں تھیں یا اسلام یا قتل، پس عرب میں غلامی نہیں ہوتی ہے، تو ولاء بھی نہیں ہوگی، لہذا مصنف کی عبارت میں عربیا کے بعد لا ولا ع
And from the ruling of haqiqah and majaz is the impossibility of their combination as intended meanings from a single word, just as it is impossible for a single garment on a wearer to be both owned and borrowed at the same time. Translation: The ruling of haqiqah and majaz is that their combination is impossible as intended meanings from a single word, just as it is impossible for a single garment on a person to be both owned and borrowed at the same time. Explanation: The author states the ruling of haqiqah and majaz: that one word at one time cannot intend both its literal and figurative meanings; either the literal meaning is intended or the figurative, but not both. This is like a garment on a person: it is either owned or borrowed, not both simultaneously. So the literal meaning is like owned property, and the figurative meaning is like a borrowed item. Therefore, Muhammad said in al-Jami': If a free-born Arab man who has no wala' (client bond) bequeaths one-third of his property to his mawali (clients), and he has only one freed slave (mu'tiq), then that freed slave deserves half of the one-third. The remaining half of the one-third is returned to the heirs, and it will not go to the mawali of his mawali, because when the literal meaning was intended by this word, the figurative meaning became void. Explanation: Since the ruling of haqiqah and majaz is known that they cannot be combined, the author branches off a case from this. First understand that the word 'mawla' is used for both the manumitter and the manumitted. Its literal meaning is the direct manumitter or direct manumitted. Figurative meanings are the mawali of the manumitter or the mawali of the manumitted. Second, understand that the right of the manumitter over the property of the slave after the slave's death is called wala'. Also understand that an Arab is free-born; there is no slavery among Arabs because they had only two options: Islam or death. So there is no slavery among Arabs, hence no wala' either. Therefore, the author's phrase 'Arab... after which there is no wala''.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage establishes a key usul rule: a single utterance cannot simultaneously express both its literal (haqiqi) and figurative (majazi) meanings. The author uses an analogy: a garment on a person is either owned or borrowed, not both at once. Similarly, a word at a given instance must be understood either literally or figuratively; both cannot be intended together. This rule is then applied to a case from Imam Muhammad's Al-Jami' al-Kabir, a foundational text of the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah). The case involves a free-born Arab (who has no wala' relationship due to the absence of slavery among Arabs) who bequeaths one-third of his property to his 'mawali' (clients). Since he has only one freed slave (mu'tiq), that freed slave qualifies as a literal 'mawla' and thus takes half of the one-third (the maximum share for a single beneficiary in a will). The remaining half of the one-third is then distributed to the testator's other legal heirs, not to the freed slave's own mawali (the figurative 'mawali' of a mawla). This is because the testator intended the literal meaning of 'mawali' (his own direct clients), not the figurative extension (his clients' clients). Thus, the literal meaning prevails, and the figurative meaning is void. This example illustrates the central rule: haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined in one utterance.

Key Terms
حَقِيقَة (ḥaqīqa): The literal, original meaning for which a word was coined.
مَجَاز (majāz): Figurative meaning used when the literal meaning is not intended.
الاستحالة (al-istiḥāla): Impossibility; here referring to the logical impossibility of combining haqiqah and majaz in one utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Mabsut
B) Al-Jami' al-Kabir
C) Al-Hidayah
D) Al-Fiqh al-Akbar

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a single utterance can only intend either the literal or the figurative meaning of a word, not both; the literal takes precedence unless context forces the figurative.

Paying Kaffarah Before Hanth: The Cause vs. Condition Dispute
Discusses permissibility of paying kaffarah before oath violation in Shafi'i and Hanafi views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Shafi'i argument for prepaying kaffarah before hanth and apply the Hanafi response by analyzing the distinction between nafs wujub and wujub ada in financial versus bodily obligations.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is wajib only after hanth; the oath alone does not create a binding duty.

This passage examines a crucial usul distinction: whether the cause (sabab) of an obligation can precede its condition (shart). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that financial kaffarah can be paid before the oath is broken, analogizing to zakat before hawl. The Hanafis reject this, arguing that the obligation to pay kaffarah is entirely contingent on the act of breaking the oath (hanth). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify how different schools treat the separation of nafs wujub from wujub ada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
Determine the exact question: is it permissible to pay kaffarah for an oath before the oath is broken (hanth)?
The question is about timing, not validity.
2
State the Shafi'i Position and Proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the oath itself is the cause (sabab) of nafs wujub; hanth is only a condition for wujub ada. Financial obligations allow separation, as seen in zakat before hawl.
They cite analogy (qiyas) with zakat.
3
State the Hanafi Position and Proof
The Hanafis hold that the cause of kaffarah is hanth itself, not the oath. Therefore, no obligation exists before hanth, regardless of type.
This is based on the idea that the oath only creates a potential obligation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to the Shafi'i Analogy
The Hanafis point out that the Shafi'i position is inconsistent because they do not allow prepayment of bodily kaffarah. Also, the analogy with zakat is rejected because kaffarah is conditional on hanth, whereas zakat is not conditional on a future act.
The distinction between financial and bodily obligations is key.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi requires repeating kaffarah after hanth if paid early; Shafi'i considers financial kaffarah prepaid as valid and not requiring repetition.
This affects how a mufti advises someone who has paid early.

ورنہ روزہ سے کفارہ حانث ہونے سے پہلے ان کے نزدیک بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ والمالى يحتمل سے مصنف نے مالی اور بدنی کفارہ میں فرق بتا رہے ہیں ، یعنی امام شافعی کے بتارہے نزد یک مالی کفاره قبل الحنث جائز ہے اور بدنی کفارہ جائز نہیں ، کیوں؟ تو کہتے ہیں کہ واجب مالی میں نفس وجوب اور وجوب ادا میں فصل ہو سکتا ہے جیسے کسی نے ایک مہینہ کے وعدہ پر کوئی چیز خریدی تو شمن کا نفس وجوب تو عقد ہوتے ہی ہو گیا لیکن وجوب ثابت ہو جائے اور وجوب ادا ابھی نہ ثابت ہو، اور نفس وجوب ثابت ہو جانے کے بعد واجب کو وجوب ادا کے ثابت ہونے سے پہلے ادا کرنا جائز ہے، جیسے کہ مالک نصاب کے لئے حولان حول سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کرنا جائز ہے، اور مشتری کے لئے شمن مؤجل کو میعاد پوری ہونے سے پہلے ادا کرنا جائز ہے، لیکن جو بدنی واجب ہے اس میں نفس وجوب اور وجوب ادا میں فصل نہیں ہوسکتا ہے، بلکہ وجوب ادا ہی کا نام نفس وجوب ہے، لہذا کفارہ بدنی میں وجوب ادا حانث ہونے کے بعد ہے تو نفس وجوب بھی حانث ہونے کے بعد ہی ہوگا کیونکہ واجب بدنی میں وجوب ادا ہی نفس وجوب ہے، فلما تاخر الاداء سے مصنف یہی سمجھا رہے ہیں، کہ جب وجوب ادا مؤخر ہو گیا تو نفس وجوب بھی پہلے باقی نہیں رہا بلکہ وہ بھی مؤخر ہو گیا، اور جب مؤخر ہو گیا تو حانث ہونے سے پہلے بدنی کفارہ ادا نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک حانث ہونے سے پہلے کفارہ کالی دے سکتا ہے، کفارہ بدنی نہیں ادا کر سکتا ہے، اور احناف کے نزدیک چونکہ کفارہ کا سبب یمین نہیں ہے بلکہ حانث ہونا ہے تو کفارہ حانث ہونے کے بعد ہی واجب ہوگا ، چاہے کفارہ مالی ہو یا بدنی، اگر کوئی پہلے ادا کر دے تو اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا حانث ہونے کے بعد اعادہ ضروری ہے۔
He permits [kaffarah before hanth] – the second derived issue is mentioned: if someone swears 'by Allah, I will not do such and such', and before becoming a breaker of the oath (hanth) he pays the financial kaffarah, i.e., frees a slave or feeds ten poor people, it is permissible, and after becoming hanth he does not need to pay kaffarah again, because according to Imam Shafi'i the cause of the very obligation (nafs wujub) of kaffarah is the oath (yamin), i.e., upon taking the oath, the nafs wujub of kaffarah is established; therefore kaffarah is attributed to the oath and called 'kaffarah yamin'. And becoming hanth is a condition for the obligation of payment (wujub ada) of kaffarah. Hence, according to Shafi'i principle, after the cause contracts before the existence of the condition, it is valid to perform the obligation, just as upon owning the nisab before the passing of a year (hawalan hawl) it is valid to pay zakat – no repetition is required. Similarly, the oath is the cause of nafs wujub, and hanth is the condition for wujub ada, so after the cause (yamin) occurs, before the condition (hanth) if one gives kaffarah, it is valid. But according to Imam Shafi'i, this condition applies only to financial kaffarah (freeing a slave, feeding ten poor); as for fasting kaffarah, it is not allowed before hanth even in his view. 'And financial [obligations] can bear' – the author explains the difference between financial and bodily kaffarah: Shafi'i allows financial kaffarah before hanth but not bodily kaffarah. Why? They say: in financial obligations, nafs wujub and wujub ada can be separated, e.g., if someone buys something on a one-month promise, the nafs wujub of the price occurs at the contract, but wujub ada after a month – here separation occurred. This shows that absence of wujub ada in financial matters does not indicate absence of nafs wujub; rather, it is possible that nafs wujub is established while wujub ada is not yet established, and after nafs wujub it is permissible to pay before wujub ada, like paying zakat for nisab owner before hawl, or a buyer paying a deferred price before the term. But in bodily obligations (badani), there cannot be separation between nafs wujub and wujub ada; rather, wujub ada is the same as nafs wujub. Therefore, in bodily kaffarah, since wujub ada occurs after hanth, nafs wujub also occurs after hanth, because in bodily obligations, wujub ada is nafs wujub. So the author explains: when wujub ada is deferred, nafs wujub does not remain before but is also deferred, and when deferred, bodily kaffarah cannot be paid before hanth. In any case, according to Imam Shafi'i, one can give financial kaffarah before hanth but not bodily kaffarah. According to the Hanafis, since the cause of kaffarah is not the oath but the hanth itself, kaffarah becomes wajib only after hanth, whether financial or bodily. If anyone pays before, it is not valid; after hanth, repetition is necessary.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage discusses a second derived issue (far'i mas'ala) flowing from the previous discussion on ta'liq. It concerns paying kaffarah for a broken oath before the oath is actually broken (hanth). The Shafi'i position distinguishes between financial kaffarah (freeing a slave, feeding poor) and bodily kaffarah (fasting). They argue that the oath (yamin) is the cause of the obligation (sabab al-wujub), and hanth is only a condition for the payment obligation (shart al-ada). Therefore, financial kaffarah – like zakat before hawl – can be paid before hanth because in financial obligations, the existence of the obligation (nafs wujub) can precede the obligation to pay (wujub ada). This separation is not possible in bodily obligations, where the obligation to pay is the same as the existence of the obligation. The Hanafi position is that the cause of kaffarah is the hanth itself, not the oath. Hence, kaffarah becomes wajib only after hanth occurs. Paying before hanth is invalid regardless of the type. This difference reflects the usul principle of whether the oath itself generates the obligation or merely creates a potential for it. The text sides with the Hanafi position, which is consistent with the earlier view that a deferred cause is not yet effective.

Key Terms
حانث (hanth): A person who breaks his oath by doing the prohibited act.
نفس وجوب (nafs wujub): The intrinsic legal obligation itself, independent of the time of performance.
وجوب ادا (wujub ada): The obligation to actually pay/perform the duty at a specific time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Shafi'i view on paying kaffarah before hanth?
A) It is invalid for all types.
B) It is valid for financial but not bodily kaffarah.
C) It is valid for both financial and bodily kaffarah.
D) It is valid only if the oath is conditional.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the cause of kaffarah is the breaking of the oath (hanth), not the oath itself; therefore prepayment is invalid and must be repeated after the oath is broken.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Refuting Shafi'i's Premises on Wasf as Condition
Refuting Imam Shafi'i's first two premises on wasf as condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a wasf into its three types (ittifaqi, sharti, 'illi) and evaluate whether its absence negates the ruling, applying the Hanafi principle of multiple causes.

Core Idea
Absence of a description does not necessarily negate the ruling — only exclusive causation or condition on the cause does.

This passage presents the Hanafi response to Imam al-Shafi'i's first two premises in the debate on whether descriptions (awsaf) function as conditions. The Hanafis argue that descriptions are of three types, and even when they are causes, their absence does not void the ruling because multiple causes can exist. This lesson dissects the Hanafi argument and its practical application in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The central dispute is whether the absence of a description (wasf) in a legal text necessarily implies the absence of the ruling. Imam al-Shafi'i treats descriptions as conditions; the Hanafis disagree.
2
Learn the Three Categories of Wasf
The text classifies wasf into three types: (1) wasf ittifaqi (coincidental, no effect), (2) wasf bi ma'na al-shart (conditional effect, but condition affects cause not ruling), (3) wasf bi ma'na al-'illa (causal, but ruling can have multiple causes).
Memorize the three categories with Quranic examples from the text.
3
Apply the Principle of Multiple Causes
The Hanafi key argument: A ruling can have multiple 'illas. Therefore, the absence of one 'illa does not necessitate absence of the ruling, as another 'illa may suffice. This is demonstrated with the verses on zina and theft.
Example: The hadd punishment for zina is established by the act, not exclusively by the description 'zani'.
4
Understand the Second Premise Refutation
Even if we accept that wasf is a condition (shart), it enters upon the cause (sabab), not the ruling directly. The condition prevents the cause from connecting to its subject, so absence of condition does not negate the ruling, only prevents the cause from taking effect.
Example: Conditional divorce – the divorce does not occur until the condition is fulfilled, but the ruling (divorce) is not negated by the condition's absence; it is merely suspended.

Source Text

وَإِنَّا نَقُولُ بِأَنَّ أَقْصَى دَرَجَاتِ الْوَصف إِذَا كَانَ مُؤْثِرًا أَنْ يَكُوْنَ عِلَّةً لِلْحُكُم كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى الزَّانِي وَالسَّارِقُ وَلَا أَثَرَ لِلْعِلَّةٍ فِي النَّفَى بِلَا خِلَافٍ ترجمہ : اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وصف کے درجات میں اعلی درجہ جب کہ وہ مؤثر ہو یہ ہے کہ وہ حکم کے لئے علت ہو یسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول " الزاني والسارق " میں اور علت کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہے نفی میں بغیر کسی اختلاف کے۔ تشریح:- کچھ باتیں بطور تمہید کے سمجھ لیں ، امام شافعی اللہ نے جو بات کہی وہ پانچ مقدمات سے مرکب ہے (۱) مقدمہ اولی انہوں نے وصف کو شرط کے ساتھ لاحق کیا (۲) مقدمہ تانی تعلیق بالشرط مانع حکم ہے، مانع انعقاد سبب نہیں ہے، (۳) مقدمہ ثالثہ طلاق اور عناق کو ملک پر معلق کرنا باطل ہے (۴) مقدمہ رابعہ کفارہ مالی قبل الحنث جائز ہے (۵) مقدمہ خامسہ امام شافعی یے نے واجب مالی اور واجب بدنی میں فرق کیا ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک یہ پانچوں مقدمات باطل ہیں ،مصنف عالی ترتیب وار ہر ایک کی تردید کرینگے، پہلے مقدمہ اولی کی تردید ہے۔ حضرت والا ! آپ نے وصف کو شرط کا درجہ دیا، اور یوں فرمایا کہ جیسے شرط کے انتفاء سے حکم کا انتفاء ہوتا ہے، ایسے ہی وصف کے انتفاء سے بھی حکم کا انتفاء ہوگا، تو وصف کو مطلق شرط کا درجہ دے دینا درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وصف تین طرح کا ہوتا ہے، (۱) بھی وصف اتفاقی ہوتا ہے جس کا وجود و عدم برابر ہوتا ہے جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے، وربائبكم التي في حجورکم مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی نے عورت سے نکاح کیا اور اس منکوحہ کی پہلے شوہر سے ایک بیٹی ہے، تو اگر شوہر نے منکوحہ سے دخول کیا ہے تو یہ ربیبہ مرد پر حرام ہو گی ، چاہے اس کی پرورش میں ہو یا نہ ہو تو معلوم ہوا کہ فی حجور کم وصف اتفاقی اور وصف عادی ہے یعنی لوگوں کی عادت ہے کہ وہ ربائب کو ان کی ماں کے ساتھ رکھتے ہیں، تو یہاں ماں کی پرورش میں ہونا نہ ہونا دونوں برابر ہیں، پرورش میں ہونے پر جواز کا مدار نہیں ہے، جواز کا مدار دخول اور عدم دخول پر ہے (۲) وصف بھی شرط کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے، جیسے من فتياتكم المومنات ، جس سے آپ نے استدلال کیا ہے (۳) وصف کبھی علت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے، اور یہ وصف کا اعلی درجہ ہے جیسے الزانية والزانی فاجلدوا اور جیسے السارق والسارقة فاقطعو ا میں وصف زنا اور وصف سرقہ وجوب حد اور قطع ید میں مؤثر ہے کیونکہ حکم یعنی وجوب جلد اور قطع ید اسم مشتق یعنی زانی اور سارق پر مرتب ہے، اور حکم جب اسم مشتق پر مرتب ہو تو اسم مشتق کا ماخذ اور مصدر اس حکم کی علت ہوتا ہے ، اور یہ بات متفقہ ہے کہ جب تک حکم کا علت کے ساتھ اختصاص نہ ہو تو علت کا انتفاء حکم کے انتفاء کو مستلزم نہیں ہے، یعنی علت نہ ہو اور حکم ہوایسا ہوسکتا ہے، کیونکہ ایک حکم کی متعدد علتیں ہو سکتی ہیں، لہذا ایک علت اگر نہ رہی تو دوسری علت سے حکم ثابت ہوگا۔ تو جب وصف کے اعلی درجہ میں وصف کے عدم سے حکم کا عدم نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو جو ادنی اور اوسط درجہ ہے اس میں وصف کے عدم سے حکم کا عدم کیسے ہوگا ؟ لہذا وصف کو مطلقا شرط کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
وَلَوْ كَانَ شَرْطًا فَالشَّرْطُ دَاخِلٌ عَلَى السَّبَبِ دُونَ الْحُكْمِ فَمَنَعَهُ مِنْ اِبْصَالِهِ بِمَحَلِّهِ وَبِدُونِ الْاِتِّصَالِ بِالْمَحَلَّ لَا يَنْعَقِدُ سَبَبًا وَلِهَذَا لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُطَلِّقُ فَعَلَّقَ الطَّلَاقَ بِالشَّرْط لَا يَحْنَثُ مَالَمْ يُوْجَدِ الشَّرْطُ ترجمہ : ۔ اور اگر وصف شرط ہو تو شرط سبب پر داخل ہوتی ہے نہ کہ حکم، پر پس وہ شرط سبب کو روک دیگی سبب کو اس سے محل میں متصل ہونے سے، اور محل میں اتصال کے بغیر وہ سب منعقد نہیں ہوگا ، اور اسی وجہ سے اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ طلاق نہیں دے گا پھر طلاق کو شرط پر معلق کیا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہو گا جب تک شرط نہ پائی جائے۔ تشریح:- یہ دوسرے مقدمہ کی تردید ہے، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر ہم مان بھی لیں کہ وصف شرط کے ساتھ لاحق ہے تو ہم یہ بات تسلیم نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ وصف کا عدم حکم کے عدم پر دلالت کرتا ہے، کیونکہ جب شرط کا عدم حکم کے عدم
And we say: The highest degree of description, when it is effective, is that it is the cause for the ruling, as in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'The adulterer and the thief' — and there is no effect of the cause in negation, without dispute. Translation: And we say that the highest degree among the degrees of description, when it is effective, is that it is the cause for the ruling, as in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'The adulterer and the thief', and the cause has no effect in negation, without any dispute. Explanation: Understand some things by way of introduction. Whatever Imam Shafi'i said is composed of five premises: (1) The first premise: They attached the description to the condition. (2) The second premise: Suspension by condition prevents the ruling, but does not prevent the cause from occurring. (3) The third premise: Suspending divorce and manumission on ownership is invalid. (4) The fourth premise: Wealth expiation before the oath is broken is permissible. (5) The fifth premise: Imam Shafi'i distinguished between wealth obligation and bodily obligation. In our view, all five premises are invalid. The author will refute each in order. First is the refutation of the first premise. O venerable one! You gave the description the status of a condition, and you said that just as the absence of a condition necessitates the absence of the ruling, similarly the absence of the description will also necessitate the absence of the ruling. So giving the description the absolute status of a condition is not correct. Because description is of three types: (1) A coincidental description, whose existence and non-existence are equal, as in Allah's saying: 'And your stepdaughters who are in your care.' The issue is that a man married a woman, and that married woman has a daughter from a previous husband. If the husband has had intercourse with the married woman, this stepdaughter becomes forbidden to the man, whether she is in his care or not. So it becomes known that 'in your care' is a coincidental and customary description — it is people's custom that they keep stepdaughters with their mothers. Here, being in the mother's care or not are equal; permissibility does not depend on being in care; permissibility depends on intercourse or its lack. (2) Sometimes description is in the meaning of condition, as in 'from among your believing maidens', from which you argued. (3) Sometimes description is in the meaning of cause, and this is the highest degree of description, as in 'The adulteress and the adulterer, flog them' and 'The thief and the thief, cut off their hands' — the description of adultery and theft are effective in the obligation of hadd and cutting of the hand, because the ruling (obligation of flogging and cutting) is attached to the derived noun (adulterer, thief). And when the ruling is attached to a derived noun, the source and origin of the derived noun is the cause for that ruling. And it is agreed that as long as the ruling is not exclusive to a single cause, the absence of the cause does not necessitate the absence of the ruling, meaning it is possible that the cause is absent but the ruling exists, because a ruling can have multiple causes. Therefore, if one cause is absent, another cause can establish the ruling. So when in the highest degree of description, the absence of description does not necessitate the absence of the ruling, then how can it be that in the lower and middle degrees, the absence of description necessitates the absence of the ruling? Hence, absolutely attaching description to condition is not correct. And if it were a condition: The condition enters upon the cause, not upon the ruling; it prevents it from connecting to its subject, and without connection to the subject, it does not become a cause. Therefore, if someone swore that he would not divorce, and then suspended divorce on a condition, he does not become guilty of perjury until the condition occurs. Explanation: This is the refutation of the second premise. The gist is that even if we accept that description is attached to condition, we do not accept that the absence of description indicates the absence of the ruling, because when the absence of condition
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi refutation of Imam Shafi'i's first two premises regarding the legal nature of descriptions (wasf). The author first defines three types of wasf: coincidental (ittifaqi), conditional (sharti), and causal ('illi). The highest degree is when the description is the cause ('illa) for the ruling, as in the Quranic verses 'The adulterer and the thief' where the act of adultery or theft is the cause for the prescribed punishment. The key argument is that even at this highest level, the absence of the cause does not necessarily negate the ruling, because a ruling can have multiple causes. For example, a hadd punishment could be established through different means. Therefore, it is incorrect to treat all descriptions as conditions whose absence would void the ruling. The second part addresses the second premise: even if we consider wasf as a condition, the condition affects the cause, not the ruling itself. It prevents the cause from connecting to its subject, so the cause does not become efficacious. An example is given of a conditional divorce where the condition must occur for the divorce to take effect. The refutation is that the absence of the condition does not negate the ruling directly; it only prevents the cause from operating. Thus, the absence of wasf does not indicate the absence of the ruling.

Key Terms
وصف اتفاقي (wasf ittifaqi): A coincidental description that has no effect on the ruling; its presence or absence is irrelevant.
علة (illa): The legal cause or effective reason behind a ruling.
شرط (shart): A condition on which the existence of a ruling depends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the absence of the description 'in your care' not affect the prohibition of marriage with a stepdaughter?
A) Because the description is a condition.
B) Because the description is a coincidental attribute (wasf ittifaqi).
C) Because the cause of prohibition is intercourse, not custody.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a description (wasf) does not automatically function as a condition; it may be coincidental, conditional, or causal, and only an exclusive cause would necessitate negation upon absence.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Grammatical Conjunction Does Not Imply Legal Conjunction
Refutes the claim that grammatical conjunction implies legal conjunction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish complete from incomplete sentences in legal texts and apply the Hanafi principle that only incomplete sentences require shared rulings.

Core Idea
Grammatical conjunction does not automatically create legal partnership; only incomplete sentences share rulings.

Some scholars, notably Imam Malik, argue that when two sentences are linked by a conjunction like 'and' (waw), they must share the same legal ruling. They use this to derive that zakah is not obligatory on a child because prayer is not. The Hanafi school refutes this by distinguishing between complete and incomplete sentences. This lesson unpacks that refutation, showing that only incomplete sentences require partnership in ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
State the claim being refuted: grammatical conjunction (qiran fi al-nazm) obligates legal conjunction (qiran fi al-hukm).
This is attributed to Imam Malik and some others.
2
Examine the Maliki Proof
Look at the verse 'And establish prayer and give zakah' (2:43). The Maliki argument: since prayer is not obligatory on a child, zakah also is not obligatory on a child because of the conjunction.
They treat the two commands as a single unit of obligation.
3
Understand the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi response: partnership (musharaka) in ruling only applies when the second sentence is incomplete (jumla nāqiṣa) and needs the first to complete its meaning. A complete sentence (jumla kāmila) stands independent.
The command 'give zakah' is a complete sentence; it does not borrow its obligation from prayer.
4
Apply the Principle to the Divorce Example
Consider the statement: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and my slave is free.' Here the second part 'and my slave is free' is incomplete as a conditional (qāṣir) because it lacks a condition. So it borrows the condition from the first part, making manumission also conditioned on entry.
This shows that only when the second sentence is deficient does conjunction imply shared ruling.
5
Conclude the Practical Difference
The practical result (thamarah al-khilaf): according to the Hanafi view, zakah is obligatory on a child who possesses wealth, because the command is independent. According to the Maliki view, it would not be.
This illustrates the importance of the complete/incomplete distinction in usul.

And among them (the invalid arguments) is what some of them said: that conjunction in wording obligates conjunction in ruling, like the statement of some of them regarding the saying of Allah the Exalted 'And establish prayer and give zakah' that the conjunction obligates that zakah is not obligatory upon a child. They said because the conjunction requires partnership, and they made a qiyas (analogy) with an incomplete sentence when it is conjoined to a complete sentence. And this is invalid, because partnership is only necessary in the incomplete sentence due to its need for that by which it becomes complete. So when it is complete by itself, partnership is not necessary except in that which it needs. And for this reason we said concerning the statement of a man to his wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and my slave is free' that the manumission is attached to the condition because it is incomplete with respect to ta'liq (conditional suspension). Translation: And among these invalid arguments is that which some people said: that conjunction in wording obligates conjunction in ruling, like the statement of some of them regarding the saying of Allah the Exalted 'And establish prayer and give zakah' that the conjunction obligates that zakah is not obligatory upon a child. They said because the conjunction requires partnership, and they made an analogy with an incomplete sentence when it is conjoined to a complete sentence. And this analogy is invalid, because partnership is only necessary in an incomplete sentence due to its need for that by which it becomes complete. So when a sentence is complete by itself, partnership is not necessary except in that which it needs. And for this reason we said concerning the statement of a man to his wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and my slave is free' that the manumission is attached to the condition because it is incomplete with respect to ta'liq. Commentary: This is explaining an invalid argument, whose proponent is Imam Malik. He says that conjunction in wording (qiran fi al-nazm) obligates conjunction in ruling (qiran fi al-hukm), meaning that when two statements are joined by a conjunction (waw), this is evidence that they share the same ruling. For example, in the verse 'And establish prayer and give zakah', the conjunction suggests that since prayer is obligatory on the sane adult, zakah should also be obligatory, but they use this to argue that zakah is not obligatory on a child because prayer is not obligatory on a child. The Hanafi refutation: partnership (musharaka) in ruling is only required when the second sentence is incomplete, needing the first to complete it. Complete sentences, like the independent command 'give zakah', are complete in themselves, so they do not require the same ruling as the previous command. The example of divorce: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and my slave is free' — here the phrase 'and my slave is free' is incomplete as a conditional statement, so it borrows the condition from the first part (entry into the house). This is because it is 'qasir' (deficient) in the context of ta'liq. Thus, only in cases of structural dependence does conjunction imply legal sharing. This refutes Imam Malik's general claim.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes a claim that grammatical conjunction (al-qirān fī al-naẓm) necessarily implies legal conjunction (al-qirān fī al-ḥukm). According to this claim, when two sentences are joined by wa (and), they must share the same legal ruling. Proponents, attributed here to Imam Malik, use this to argue that since prayer (ṣalāh) is not obligatory on a child, zakah (zakāh) also becomes non-obligatory on a child because both are joined in the verse 'And establish prayer and give zakah'. The Hanafi refutation distinguishes between complete and incomplete sentences. Partnership (mushāraka) in ruling is only required when the second sentence is incomplete (jumla nāqiṣa) and depends on the first for completion. A complete sentence (jumla kāmila) stands on its own and does not require the same ruling. The Hanafi example: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and my slave is free' — here 'and my slave is free' is incomplete (qāṣir) in terms of taʿlīq (conditional suspension), so it needs the condition from the first part. Thus, the manumission is also conditioned on entry. This shows that only structurally dependent sentences, not independent commands, participate in the ruling of the first sentence. Therefore, the Maliki analogy is invalid (fāsid) in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
قران في النظم (qirān fī al-naẓm): Grammatical conjunction; joining two linguistic units with a conjunction (e.g., waw).
جملة ناقصة (jumla nāqiṣa): An incomplete sentence that depends on another for full meaning, especially in conditional contexts.
جملة كاملة (jumla kāmila): A complete sentence that is self-sufficient in conveying its meaning.
تعليق (taʿlīq): Conditional suspension of a legal effect, e.g., divorce or manumission upon a condition.
قاصر (qāṣir): Deficient or incomplete in a specific legal context, needing supplementation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi refutation, why is the Maliki analogy from the verse 'And establish prayer and give zakah' to the non-obligation of zakah on a child invalid?
A) Because the conjunction only applies to prayer, not zakah.
B) Because 'give zakah' is a complete sentence and does not need partnership with the previous command.
C) Because children are not addressed by the verse at all.
D) Because zakah is not mentioned in the verse.

Key Takeaway
Grammatical conjunction only implies legal sharing when the second sentence is structurally dependent on the first.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Transfer of the Cause to the Final Part of Prayer Time
Explaining the transfer of the cause to the final part of prayer time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of sabab transfer to the final part of prayer time and evaluate the opposing view of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
The cause of prayer obligation transfers to the minimal final part; hypothetical power suffices.

In this lesson, we explore a key usul principle from the Hanafi school: how the sabab (cause) for an obligatory act is determined when the time is limited. The passage from Al-Fayd al-Hijazi explains that the sabab does not extend over the entire time nor a fixed fraction, but rather transfers to the final part connected to actual performance. This principle has significant implications for when prayer becomes obligatory, especially in edge cases where time is narrow.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the problem: How to determine the sabab (cause) for prayer obligation when the entire time is not the cause and no fixed fraction is specified.
The sabab must be a part of time that is connected to the actual performance (ada).
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, the sabab transfers to the final part of time, which is the measure of takbirat al-tahrima (the initial takbir).
This is the minimal amount of time needed to initiate prayer.
3
Trace the reasoning
The sabab must be attached to the musabbab (effect). Since the entire time cannot be the cause, the minimal part that is directly connected to the act (ada) is chosen.
No proof exists for making any other part the cause.
4
Examine the objection
Imam Zufar argues that the sabab should transfer until there remains time for four rak'ahs, otherwise it would be an unbearable burden (taklif ma la yutaq).
Zufar's view is based on the idea that obligation requires actual ability to complete the prayer.
5
Resolve with tawahhum
Abu Hanifa responds that actual power (haqiqiyya qudra) is not required; hypothetical power (tawahhum qudra) suffices, as Allah could extend the time.
Thus, even if only a moment remains, the obligation arises because hypothetical power is sufficient.

الفيضُ الحجازي
۹۶
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
سبیت کو منتقل کرنا ضروری ٹھہرا اور پورے وقت کے بعد ایسا کوئی معین حصہ جیسے خمس ، ربع وغیرہ بھی نہیں تھا کہ جس کی طرف ہم سب کو منتقل کرتے ، اور کہتے کہ یہ چوتھائی حصہ یا وقت کا تہائی حصہ سبب ہے، کیوں کہ پورے وقت میں نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، لہذا جب کوئی معین حصہ بھی نہیں ہے اور پورے وقت کو بھی سبب نہیں بنا سکتے تو ادنی مقدار پر اکتفاء کرنا ضروری ہوا اور ادنی مقدار وہ جزء ہے جس کے ساتھ ادا متصل ہے کیونکہ یہ جز ءادا سے ملا ہوا ہے اور اصل سبب میں یہ ہے کہ وہ مسبب سے ملا ہوا ہو۔ ولم يجز تقديرة :- سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے کہ آپ ادا سے متصل جزء کو سبب قرار دے رہے ہیں، تو صرف ادا سے متصل جزء کو سبب قرار دینے کے بجائے ادا سے پہلے گزرے ہوئے تمام اجزاء کو سبب قرار دیں تو کیا حرج ہے؟
اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ادا سے پہلے گذرے ہوئے تمام اسباب کو سبب قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ دلیل کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ پورا وقت سبب ہو جیسے قضا میں ہوتا ہے، یا وہ ادنی جزء سبب ہو کیونکہ یہ ادا سے ملا ہوا ہے، اور اصل سبب میں یہ ہے کہ وہ مسبب سے ملا ہوا ہو ، اور ان دو کے علاوہ کو سبب بنانے کی کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، لہذا ادا اور سے پہلے کے تمام اجزاء کو سبب بنانے میں قلیل ( جزء متصل بالا دا) سے بغیر دلیل کے اعراض و تجاوز لازم آ رہا ہے جو جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر کوئی دلیل ہوتی تو گزرے ہوئے اجزا کو سبب بنا سکتے تھے ،مگر کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، لہذا اقلیل یعنی جزء متصل بالا داء سے تجاوز نہ کریں گے۔
ثم كذلك - مصنف االلہ کہتے ہیں کہ سبیت پہلے جزء سے منتقل ہوتی رہے گی یہاں تک کہ ہمارے نزد یک آخری جزء تک جو تحریمہ کی مقدار ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جب چار رکعت کے بقدر وقت باقی رہ جائے ، وہاں تک سبیت منتقل ہوگی ، اب اس کے بعد سبیت آگے منتقل نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ اگر چار رکعت کے بقدر وقت باقی نہیں رہا اور آپ نے وقت کو سبب بنا کر چار رکعت واجب کر دی تو یہ بندہ پر تکلیف مالا يطاق ہے ، اور احناف کے نزدیک ادا شروع کرنے سے متصل جو آخری جزء ہے جو تحریمہ کی مقدار ہے وہاں تک سبیت منتقل ہوگی، کیونکہ یہ آخری جزء ہے اس کے بعد کوئی جزء نہیں جس کی طرف سبیت کو منتقل کیا جا سکے۔ سوال: - احناف تحریمہ کی مقدار آخری جزء کو سبب قرار دے رہے ہیں ،جس میں صرف تحریمہ کے بقدر وقت ہے، پوری نماز پڑھ سکے اتنا وقت نہیں ہے، تو کیا اس سے تکلیف مالا يطاق لازم نہیں آئے گی ؟ جواب: - امام ابو حنیفہ عالی کے نزدیک ادا واجب ہونے کے لئے حقیقہ قدرت شرط نہیں ہے، تو ہم قدرت کافی ہے، پس تحریمہ کے بقدر جو آخری جزء ہے اس میں اگر چہ بندہ ادا پر حقیقۂ قدرت نہیں رکھتا ہے کیونکہ وقت ہی

الفيضُ الحجازي شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي نہیں ہے ، مگر تو ہم قدرت ضرور ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ اللہ تعالی وقت کو لمبا کر دے اور بندہ ادا پر قادر ہو جائے تو خلاصہ
کلام یہ کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ادا و ا جب ہونے کے لئے تو ہم کافی ہے لہذا آخری جز ء سبب ہو جائے گا۔ فَيُعْتَبَرُ حَالُهُ فِي الْإِسْلَامِ وَالْبُلُوغِ وَالْعَقْلِ وَالْجُنُونِ وَالسَّفَرِ وَالْا قَامَةِ وَالْحَيْضِ وَالطُّهُرِ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْءِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ صِفَةُ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْءِ فَإِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْءُ صَحِيحًا كَمَافِى الْفَجْرِ وَجَبَ كَامِلاً فَإِذَا اعْتَرَضَ الْفَسَادُ بِطُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ بَطَلَ الْفَرْضُ وَإِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْجُزْهُ فَاسِدًا كَمَا فِي الْعَصْرِ يَسْتَانِفُ فِي وَقْتِ الْإِحْمِرَارِ وَ جَبَ نَاقِصَّافَيَتَأْذَى بِصِفَةِ النُّقْصَانِ ترجمہ: پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا مکلف کے حال کا اس جزء کے وقت ، مسلمان ہونے میں ، بالغ ہونے میں ، عاقل ہونے میں، مجنون ہونے میں ، مسافر اور مقیم ہونے میں، حائضہ ہونے میں اور حیض سے پاک ہونے میں، اور اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس جزء کی صفت کا پس اگر وہ جزء صیح ہے جیسا کہ فجر میں تو نماز کامل واجب ہوگی پس اگر فساد پیش آ گیا طلوع شمس کی وجہ سے تو فرض باطل ہو جائے گا، اور اگر وہ جزء فاسد ( ناقص ) ہو جیسا کہ عصر میں درانحالیکہ وہ عصر کی نماز شروع کرے احمرار کے وقت تو عصر کی نماز ناقص واجب ہوگی پس ادا ہو جائے گی وہ نقصان کی صفت کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح:- جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک آخری جزء سبب بنا جو تحریمہ کی مقدار ہے تو اسی جزء میں مکلف کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا، لہذا اتنا وقت باقی رہ گیا جس میں صرف تحریمہ کی گنجائش ہے اور اس وقت میں کا فر مسلمان ہو گیا یا بچہ بالغ ہو گیا یا مجنون کا جنون ختم ہو گیا، یا مقیم مسافر ہو گیا، یا مسافر مقیم ہو گیا، یا عورت حیض سے پاک ہوگئی تو ان سب پر نماز فرض ہو جائے گی ، اگر اس وقت عاقل مجنون ہو گیا یا عورت کو حیض آگیا تو نماز ساقط ہو جائے گی، اس وقت میں مقیم مسافر ہو گیا تو قصر کرے گا اور مسافر مقیم ہو گیا تو پوری نماز پڑھے گا۔ اور مامور بہ کے کامل اور ناقص ہونے میں بھی اس جزء کا دخل ہوگا ، اگر یہ آخری جزء کامل ہے تو نماز کامل واجب ہوگی جیسے فجر کا پورا وقت کامل ہے، کسی نے آخری جزء میں نماز شروع کی اور دورانِ نماز سورج طلوع ہو گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ آخری جزء کے کامل ہونے کی وجہ سے کامل واجب ہوئی ، اور صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ادا ئیگی درست نہیں۔۔ اور اگر آخری جزء ناقص ہے تو واجب بھی ناقص ہوگا، جیسے عصر ناقص واجب ہوئی اور ادائیگی بھی ناقص ہو رہی ہے پس ناقص واجب کی صفت نقصان کے ساتھ ادا ئیگی درست ہے۔
وَلَا يَلْزَمْ عَلَى هَذَا مَا إِذَ ابْتَدَأَ الْعَصْرَ فِي اَوَلِ وَقْتِهِ ثُمَّ مَدَّهُ إِلَى أَنْ غَرَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi: Urdu commentary on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. It became necessary to transfer the sabab (cause), and after the entire time there was no specific portion like one-fifth or one-quarter to which we could transfer the cause and say this one-quarter or one-third of the time is the cause, because one can pray in the entire time. So when there is no specific portion and we cannot make the entire time the cause, it became necessary to suffice with the minimal amount, and the minimal amount is that part (juz') which is connected to the actual performance (ada), because it is attached to the ada, and in the original cause, it is that it be attached to the effect (musabbab). 'Wa lam yajuz taqdirah': This is the answer to an assumed question: You are making the part connected to ada the cause, so why not make all the previous parts that have passed the cause instead of only the part connected to ada? He answers that it is not correct to make all the passed parts the cause, because the requirement of the proof is either that the entire time be the cause as in qada, or the minimal part because it is connected to ada, and in the original cause it must be connected to the effect. There is no proof for making anything other than these two a cause. So making all the previous parts a cause entails abandoning and exceeding the minimal part (the part connected to ada) without proof, which is not permissible. Yes, if there were proof, we could make the passed parts a cause, but there is no proof, so we will not exceed the minimal part, i.e., the part connected to ada. 'Thumma kathalik': The author says that the sabab will keep transferring from the first part until, according to us (Hanafis), the final part which is the measure of takbirat al-tahrima, and according to Imam Zufar, until there remains time equivalent to four rak'ahs, then the sabab will transfer up to that point, after which it will not transfer further because if four rak'ahs' time does not remain and you make the time a cause making four rak'ahs obligatory, that would be an unbearable burden (taklif ma la yutaq). According to Hanafis, the final part that is connected to starting the ada and is the measure of takbirat al-tahrima is where the sabab transfers, because it is the final part after which there is no part to which the sabab could be transferred. Question: Hanafis make the final part of the measure of takbirat al-tahrima the cause, in which there is only time for takbirat al-tahrima, not enough time to pray the whole prayer. Would that not entail an unbearable burden? Answer: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, actual power (haqiqiyya qudra) is not a condition for the obligation of ada; sufficient power (tawahhum qudra) is enough. So in the final part which is the measure of takbirat al-tahrima, even though the person does not have actual power to perform the ada because there is no time, still there is power based on tawahhum, in the manner that Allah could lengthen the time and the person would be able to perform. So the conclusion is that according to Imam Sahib, tawahhum is sufficient for the obligation of ada, therefore the final part becomes the cause. 'Fa yu'tabaru haluhu fi al-Islami wa al-bulughi wa al-'aqli wa al-jununi wa al-safari wa al-iqamati wa al-haydi wa al-tuhri 'inda dhalika al-juz'i wa yu'tabaru sifat dhalika al-juz'i fa in kana dhalika al-juz'u sahihan kama fi al-fajri wajaba kamilan fa idha i'tarada al-fasadu bi tulu'i al-shamsi batala al-fardu wa in kana dhalika al-juz'u fasidan kama fi al-'asri yasta'naf fi waqti al-ihmirari wajaba naqisan fa yata'adhdha bi sifati al-nuqsan. Translation: So consideration will be given to the condition of the responsible person at the time of that part regarding Islam, puberty, reason, insanity, travel, residence, menstruation, and purity, and consideration will be given to the quality of that part. If that part is sound (sahih) like in Fajr, the prayer becomes obligatory completely (kamil); then if corruption occurs due to sunrise, the fard becomes void. If that part is unsound (fasid) like in 'Asr (when one starts at the time of redness), it becomes obligatory incomplete (naqis); so it will be performed with the quality of deficiency. Commentary: When according to Imam Sahib the final part which is the measure of takbirat al-tahrima becomes the cause, then at that part the condition of the responsible person is considered. So if at that remaining time which only allows takbirat al-tahrima, a disbeliever becomes Muslim, a child becomes pubescent, an insane person regains sanity, a resident becomes a traveler, a traveler becomes a resident, or a woman becomes pure from menstruation, then prayer becomes obligatory upon all of them. If at that time a sane person becomes insane or a woman's menstruation begins, the prayer is dropped. If at that time a resident becomes a traveler, he will shorten the prayer; if a traveler becomes a resident, he will pray complete. And regarding the completeness or incompleteness of the commanded act, that part also plays a role. If this final part is complete (sahih), then the prayer becomes obligatory completely, like the entire time of Fajr is complete. If someone starts prayer at the final part and during it the sun rises, the prayer becomes void, because due to the final part being complete, the obligation was complete, and performing it with the quality of deficiency is not valid. If the final part is incomplete (fasid), then the obligation is also incomplete, like 'Asr becomes obligatory incomplete, and its performance is also incomplete, so it is valid to perform an incomplete obligation with the quality of deficiency. 'Wa la yalzam 'ala hadha ma idha btada' al-'asra fi awwal waqtihi thumma maddahu ila an gharabat al-shamsu': And it does not follow from this that if one starts 'Asr at its beginning time and then extends it until the sun sets...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Husami discusses the usul principle of how the sabab (cause) for an obligatory act (here, prayer) is determined when the time is limited. The author argues that the sabab cannot be the entire time because that would be impractical, nor a fixed fraction, but rather the minimal part connected to the actual performance (ada). This part is the final moment that allows the initiation of prayer (takbirat al-tahrima according to Hanafis, or four rak'ahs according to Imam Zufar). The passage then explains that at this final part, the condition of the person (Islam, puberty, sanity, travel, menstruation) is considered for the obligation. Additionally, the quality of this final part (whether it is 'sound' or 'unsound' based on the time's length) determines whether the obligation is complete or incomplete, affecting the validity if the time expires during prayer. The commentary addresses an objection about unbearable burden by citing Imam Abu Hanifa's position that tawahhum (hypothetical) power suffices for obligation. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, with Imam Zufar's differing view noted. The passage ends with a note that starting 'Asr early and extending until sunset does not invalidate the prayer, though the text is incomplete.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The legal cause that triggers the obligation of prayer; it is the minimal part of time connected to the actual performance (ada).
جزء (juz'): A part or portion of time; the final part that is the cause is the measure of takbirat al-tahrima.
تحریمہ (tahrima): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer; its time is a minimal moment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The time to perform four rak'ahs
B) The time to perform one rak'ah
C) The time to say the takbirat al-tahrima
D) The time to recite Surah al-Fatihah

Key Takeaway
The sabab for prayer obligation transfers to the final minimal part (takbirat al-tahrima); hypothetical power (tawahhum) suffices for the obligation to arise.
