الفيضُ الحجازي
۲۰۶
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہا کہتے ہیں کہ جو گدھا چارہ اور بھوسہ کھاتا ہے اس کا جھوٹا پاک ہے۔ اور سور حمار میں قیاس بھی متعارض ہیں، کیونکہ اگر پسینہ پر قیاس کرتے ہیں تو جھوٹا پاک ہونا چاہیے، اس لئے کہ گدھے کا پسینہ پاک ہے، اور اگر گدھی کے دودھ پر قیاس کرتے ہیں تو جھوٹا ناپاک ہوگا، نیز گدھے کے جھوٹے کو کتے کے جھوٹے پر قیاس کر کے ناپاک بھی نہیں کہہ سکتے ، کیونکہ گدھے کی ضرورت اکثر پڑتی ہے اور کتے میں ضرورت نہیں ہے، اور بلی کے جھوٹے پر قیاس کر کے پاک بھی نہیں کہہ سکتے کیونکہ گدھے کے مقابلہ میں بلی میں ضرورت زیادہ ہے، اب اگر سور حمارکوسور ہرہ پر قیاس کر کے پاک کہتے ہیں یا سور کلب پر قیاس کر کے ناپاک کہتے ہیں تو یہ قیاس کا اثبات بغیر علت مشترکہ کے ہوگا ، اور یہ باطل ہے کیونکہ قیاس بغیر علت کے ابتداء کسی حکم کو ثابت کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے۔
بہر حال جب سور حمار میں دلائل متعارض ہیں تو تقریر الاصول واجب ہوگا یعنی ورود دلائل سے پہلے کی حالت کا اعتبار ہوگا، اور سور حمار دلائل سے پہلے اصلاً پاک تھا، کیونکہ پانی اپنی خلقت کے اعتبار سے پاک ہے، لہذا تعارض کی وجہ سے وہ ناپاک نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ گدھے کا لعاب مل جانے کی وجہ سے نجاست کا شک پیدا ہو گیا ، اور اصل کے لحاظ سے پانی کی طہارت یقینی ہے، تو یقین شک سے زائل نہ ہوگا، لہذا اگر اس کے علاوہ پانی نہ ہو تو اس سے وضو کرنا ضروری ہے،۔۔لیکن اس پانی سے محدث کا حدث بھی زائل نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ آدمی کا حدث یقینی چیز ہے، اور پانی کی طہارت مشکوک ہے اور شک سے یقین زائل نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا اس سے حدث زائل نہ ہوگا، حدث زائل کرنے کے لئے اس پانی سے وضو کر نے کے ساتھ تم بھی ضروری ہے، سور حمار کو بوجہ دلائل کے متعارض ہونے کے اور حکم کے مشتبہ ہونے کے مشکوک کہا جاتا ہے۔ وَأَمَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ التَّعَارُضُ بَيْنَ الْقِيَاسَيْنِ لَمْ يَسْقُطَا بِالتَّعَارْضِ لِيَجِبَ الْعَمَلُ بِالْحَالِ بَلْ يَعْمَلُ الْمُجْتَهِدُ بِأَيْهِمَا شَاءَ بِشَهَادَةِ قَلْبِهِ لِاَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ حُجَةٌ يُعْمَلُ بِهِ أَصَابَ الْمُجْتَهدُ الْحَقَ بهِ أَوْأَخْطَأَ فَكَانَ الْعَمَلُ بِأَحَدِهِمَا وَهُوَ حَجَةٌ اِطْمَأَنَ قَلْبُهُ إِلَيْهَا بِنُورِ الْفِرَاسَةِ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْعَمَلِ بِالْحَالِ ثُمَّ التَّعَارُضُ إِنَّمَا يَتَحَقَّقُ بَيْنَ الْحُجَّتَيْنِ بِايْجَابِ كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا ضِدَّ مَا يُوجِبُهُ الْأُخْرَىٰ فِيْ وَقْتِ وَاحِدٍ فِي مَحِلٌ وَاحِدٍ مَعَ تَسَاوِيْهِمَا فِي الْقُوَةِ- ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال جب تعارض واقع ہو دو قیاسوں کے درمیان تو وہ دونوں ساقط نہ ہوں گے تعارض کی وجہ سے کہ استصحاب حال پر عمل کرنا واجب ہو، بلکہ مجتہد ان دونوں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے اپنے قلب کی شہادت سے ، اس لئے کہ قیاس ایسی حجت ہے جس پر عمل کیا جاتا ہے، مجتہد اس قیاس کی وجہ سے حق کو پالیوے یا خطا کرے، پس ان دو قیاسوں میں سے ایک پر عمل کرنا جب کہ ان میں سے ایک عمل کے حق میں ) ایسی حجت ہے جس کی طرف مجتہد کا دل نور فراست سے مطمئن ہوا ہے۔ استصحاب حال پر عمل کرنے سے اولی ہے۔ پھر تعارض متحقق ہوتا ہے دو حجتوں کے درمیان ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے ثابت کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کی ضد کو جس کو دوسری حجت ثابت کرتی ہے، ایک ہی وقت میں، ایک ہی محل میں، ان دونوں حجتوں کے قوت میں برابر ہونے کے ساتھ۔
تشریح : ۔ جب دو قیاسوں میں تعارض واقع ہو تو دونوں قیاس ساقط نہ ہوں گے، جیسے دو آیتوں یا دوسنتوں میں تعارض کی صورت میں دونوں جنتیں ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں، کیونکہ اگر قیاس ساقط ہو گئے تو اس مسئلہ کا حکم معلوم کرنے کے لئے سوائے استصحاب حال کے اور کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، استصحاب حال کا مطلب ہے شی کو اس کی پہلی حالت پر باقی رکھنا جیسے پانی کے پاک اور ناپاک ہونے میں شک ہے اور کوئی بتانے والا بھی نہیں ہے، تو استصحاب حال سے پانی پاک ہوگا کیونکہ اصل وضع میں پانی پاک ہے، اور یہ استصحاب حال ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے، اور قیاس حجت ہے، لہذا اب مجتہد کو اختیار ہوگا کہ دو قیاسوں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے مگر تحری کر کے دل جس پر مطمئن ہو اس پر عمل کرے، یہ تحری ہمارے نزدیک شرط ہے، امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر تحری کے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے، ان کے نزدیک تحری شرط نہیں ہے، اسی لئے امام شافعی کے ایک مسئلہ میں ایک ہی وقت میں کئی کئی قول ہو جاتے ہیں، اور ہمارے اگر ایک مسئلہ میں دو قول ہوں گے تو الگ الگ زمانوں کے اعتبار سے ہوں گے، لہذا ایک صحیح اور ایک فاسد ہوگا۔
مصنف دو قیاسوں میں سے ایک پر عمل کرنے اور استصحاب حال کی طرف رجوع نہ کرنے کی دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس میں مجتہد چاہے حق کو پالے یا خطا کرے بہر صورت قیاس حجت ہے، اور استصحاب حال حجت نہیں ہے، تو غیر حجت کے مقابلہ میں حجت پر عمل کرنا بغیر تحری کے بھی اولی ہے، پھر جب مجتہد تحری کرلے اور نور فراست سے اس کا قلب مطمئن ہو جائے تو پھر قیاس پر عمل اور بھی اولی ہوگا، لہذا تعارض قیاس کی صورت میں قیاس پر ہی عمل ہوگا ، پھر اس سوال کا جواب کہ دو آیتوں یا دو حدیثوں میں تعارض کے وقت دونوں حجتیں کیوں ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں؟ یہ ہے کہ آیتوں اور سنتوں کے بعد دلیل شرعی یعنی قیاس موجود ہے جس کی طرف رجوع ہوسکتا ہے، اور قیاس کے بعد کوئی دلیل شرعی نہیں ہے، سوائے استصحاب کے جو ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں، اور رہا یہ سوال کہ ماقبل
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi. Page 206. Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) says: The mouthful of a donkey that eats fodder and straw is pure. And regarding the donkey's mouthful, the analogies are conflicting: because if one analogizes to sweat, then the mouthful should be pure, because the donkey's sweat is pure; and if one analogizes to the donkey's milk, then the mouthful would be impure. Also, one cannot say the donkey's mouthful is impure by analogy to the dog's mouthful, because the donkey is often needed and the dog is not; and one cannot say it is pure by analogy to the cat's mouthful, because the cat is needed more than the donkey. Now if one says it is pure by analogy to the mouthful of a [؟] or impure by analogy to the dog's mouthful, then this would be affirming an analogy without a common effective cause, and that is invalid because analogy without a cause cannot initially prove a ruling. In any case, when the evidences regarding the donkey's mouthful are conflicting, then the presumption of the principle (taqrir al-asl) becomes necessary, i.e., the state before the arrival of evidences is considered. And the donkey's mouthful before evidences was originally pure, because water by its nature is pure. Therefore, due to conflict it will not become impure, because the donkey's saliva mixing raises doubt of impurity, and according to the principle, the water's purity is certain, and certainty is not removed by doubt. Hence, if there is no other water, performing wudu with it is necessary. However, the state of being in need of ablution (hadath) will not be removed by this water, because a person's hadath is certain, and the water's purity is doubtful, and certainty is not removed by doubt. So to remove hadath, along with performing wudu with this water, tayammum is also necessary. The donkey's mouthful is called mashkuk (doubtful) because of the conflict of evidences and the ambiguity of the ruling. And as for when conflict occurs between two analogies, they are not dropped due to conflict so that acting upon the current state (istishab al-hal) becomes obligatory; rather, the mujtahid acts upon whichever he wishes by the testimony of his heart, because an analogy is a proof that is acted upon, whether the mujtahid attains the truth through it or errs. So acting upon one of them — it being a proof whose heart is tranquil towards it by the light of perspicacity — is more appropriate than acting upon the current state. Then conflict is realized between two proofs by each of them necessitating the opposite of what the other necessitates at the same time, in the same subject matter, with them being equal in strength. Translation: And in any case, when conflict occurs between two analogies, they are not invalidated due to conflict, so that acting upon the current state (istishab al-hal) becomes obligatory; rather, the mujtahid acts upon whichever he wishes by the testimony of his heart, because an analogy is a proof that is acted upon, whether the mujtahid attains the truth through it or errs. So acting upon one of them — when it is a proof towards which the mujtahid's heart is tranquil due to the light of perspicacity — is more appropriate than acting upon the current state. Then conflict is realized between two proofs by each of them necessitating the opposite of what the other necessitates, at the same time, in the same locus, with them being equal in strength. Explanation: When conflict occurs between two analogies, both analogies are not dropped, unlike when two verses or two sunnahs conflict, wherein both proofs are dropped. Because if the analogies were dropped, then for determining the ruling of this issue there would be no proof except istishab al-hal. Istishab al-hal means to keep a thing in its original state, such as when there is doubt about water's purity or impurity and no informant exists; then by istishab al-hal the water would be pure because water originally is pure. And this istishab al-hal is not a proof in our view, whereas analogy is a proof. Therefore, the mujtahid has the choice to act on whichever of the two analogies he wishes, but he must exercise taharri (seeking) so that his heart is tranquil towards it. This taharri is a condition in our view. Imam al-Shafi'i says that one may act on whichever he wishes without taharri; in his view, taharri is not a condition. For this reason, Imam al-Shafi'i may have multiple statements on one issue at the same time, whereas if we have two statements on one issue, they are based on different times, so one is correct and one is invalid. The author is giving the reason for acting on one of the two analogies and not resorting to istishab al-hal. He says that in analogy, whether the mujtahid attains the truth or errs, in any case analogy is a proof, and istishab al-hal is not a proof. So acting upon a proof over a non-proof is more appropriate even without taharri. Then when the mujtahid performs taharri and his heart becomes tranquil by the light of perspicacity, then acting on the analogy is even more appropriate. Therefore, in the case of conflicting analogies, one acts upon the analogy. Then the answer to the question: why are both proofs dropped when two verses or two hadiths conflict? It is because after verses and sunnahs, there is a legal proof (i.e., analogy) to which one can resort, and after analogy there is no legal proof except istishab, which in our view is not a proof. Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Husami addresses the important usul principle of ta'arud al-qiyasayn (conflict of analogies). The author begins with a concrete example: the ruling on the mouthful (su'r) of a donkey. He presents conflicting analogies: comparing it to sweat (pure), to milk (impure), to a dog's mouthful (impure) but with a distinction due to necessity, and to a cat's mouthful (pure again with a distinction). Because these analogies lack a common effective cause (illa) that can be consistently applied, they are not valid qiyas. The correct approach when evidences conflict is to revert to the original principle (taqrir al-asl): water is inherently pure, and certainty is not overridden by doubt. Thus, water mixed with a donkey's mouthful is considered pure but its purity is doubtful; therefore, one must perform both wudu and tayammum to remove the certainty of hadath. This is known as the case of mashkuk (doubtful water). Then the author transitions to the general rule: when two analogies conflict (valid analogies, unlike the previous invalid ones), they are not dropped. Instead, the mujtahid must choose one based on taharri (seeking tranquility of the heart) because qiyas is a proof (hujja) and istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) is not a proof in the Hanafi school. The commentary emphasizes that conflicting textual proofs (Quran or Sunnah) are treated differently: they are both dropped and one resorts to qiyas. But after qiyas, there is no further proof except istishab, which is insufficient. The author also highlights a key difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is: Shafi'is do not require taharri when choosing between conflicting analogies — they allow free choice. This explains why Imam al-Shafi'i sometimes has multiple contradictory positions on a single issue, whereas in the Hanafi school, only one opinion is correct at any given time.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'āruḍ): Conflict between two proofs (qiyas, texts) where each necessitates opposite rulings on the same issue at the same time.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause (illa).
استصحاب حال (istiṣḥāb al-ḥāl): Presumption that a state continues unchanged (e.g., purity) when there is doubt without evidence of change.
تحری (taḥarrī): The mujtahid's inner effort to find which conflicting proof his heart is tranquil towards, using the light of perspicacity (nur al-firasa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a mujtahid do when two valid analogies (qiyas) conflict on a single issue?
A) Drop both analogies and act on istishab al-hal.
B) Choose one of the analogies without any further condition.
C) Choose one analogy after performing taharri (seeking inner conviction).
D) Refer to the later rulings in the madhhab.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conflicting analogies are not dropped; the mujtahid must exercise taharri to choose one, because qiyas is a proof and istishab is not.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Conflicting Qiyas and the Role of Istishab
Usul rule explaining conflict resolution between qiyas and the role of istishab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for resolving conflicting qiyas and explain why taharrī is required and why istishab is not a proof in such cases.

Core Idea
When two qiyas conflict, the mujtahid must choose by taharrī, not by istishab, because qiyas is a proof and istishab is not.

This passage confronts a fundamental problem in usul al-fiqh: what happens when two valid analogies yield opposite rulings? The Hanafi school teaches that neither analogy is discarded—unlike contradictory texts—because the only alternative, istishab (presumption of continuity), is not a valid proof. Instead, the mujtahid must exert careful deliberation (taharrī) to determine the stronger analogy, and then act on it. This lesson unpacks that rule and the underlying dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over the role of taharrī.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of ta'arud in Usul al-Fiqh
Differentiate between conflict of texts (nusus) and conflict of analogies (qiyas). In texts, both drop when equal; in qiyas, neither drops because no higher authority exists.
This distinction is key to Hanafi methodology.
2
Define istishab and its Hanafi status
Istishab means presuming the original state when in doubt. Hanafis do not consider it a shar'i proof (hujja). It is only used in absence of any other proof out of necessity.
Know the precise Hanafi position: istishab is not a hujja.
3
Explain the requirement of taharrī
Taharrī is the careful deliberation by the mujtahid to choose the qiyas that his heart becomes tranquil with. It is a condition (shart) in the Hanafi school.
Taharrī ensures consistency and prevents arbitrary choice.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i position and the thamarah al-khilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i does not require taharrī, allowing the mujtahid to choose arbitrarily. This leads to multiple simultaneous rulings on the same issue, whereas Hanafis have one ruling per time period.
The dispute has practical consequences for fatwa consistency.
5
Apply the rule to a sample scenario
Example: Two qiyas on the purity of a liquid. One says it is najis (analogy to water), the other says it is pure (analogy to solid). The Hanafi mujtahid performs taharrī and chooses the more convincing analogy, not defaulting to istishab.
This shows the rule in action.

سے کہ استصحاب حال پر عمل کرنا واجب ہو، بلکہ مجتہد ان دونوں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے اپنے قلب کی شہادت سے ، اس لئے کہ قیاس ایسی حجت ہے جس پر عمل کیا جاتا ہے، مجتہد اس قیاس کی وجہ سے حق کو پالیے یا خطا کرے، پس ان دو قیاسوں میں سے ایک پر عمل کرنا جب کہ ان میں سے ایک عمل کے حق میں ) ایسی حجت ہے جس کی طرف مجتہد کا دل نور فراست سے مطمئن ہوا ہے۔ استصحاب حال پر عمل کرنے سے اولی ہے۔

تشریح : ۔ جب دو قیاسوں میں تعارض واقع ہو تو دونوں قیاس ساقط نہ ہوں گے، جیسے دو آیتوں یا دوسنتوں میں تعارض کی صورت میں دونوں جنتیں ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں، کیونکہ اگر قیاس ساقط ہو گئے تو اس مسئلہ کا حکم معلوم کرنے کے لئے سوائے استصحاب حال کے اور کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، استصحاب حال کا مطلب ہے شی کو اس کی پہلی حالت پر باقی رکھنا جیسے پانی کے پاک اور ناپاک ہونے میں شک ہے اور کوئی بتانے والا بھی نہیں ہے، تو استصحاب حال سے پانی پاک ہوگا کیونکہ اصل وضع میں پانی پاک ہے، اور یہ استصحاب حال ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے، اور قیاس حجت ہے، لہذا اب مجتہد کو اختیار ہوگا کہ دو قیاسوں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے مگر تحری کر کے دل جس پر مطمئن ہو اس پر عمل کرے، یہ تحری ہمارے نزدیک شرط ہے، امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر تحری کے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے، ان کے نزدیک تحری شرط نہیں ہے، اسی لئے امام شافعی کے ایک مسئلہ میں ایک ہی وقت میں کئی کئی قول ہو جاتے ہیں، اور ہمارے اگر ایک مسئلہ میں دو قول ہوں گے تو الگ الگ زمانوں کے اعتبار سے ہوں گے، لہذا ایک صحیح اور ایک فاسد ہوگا۔

مصنف دو قیاسوں میں سے ایک پر عمل کرنے اور استصحاب حال کی طرف رجوع نہ کرنے کی دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس میں مجتہد چاہے حق کو پالے یا خطا کرے بہر صورت قیاس حجت ہے، اور استصحاب حال حجت نہیں ہے، تو غیر حجت کے مقابلہ میں حجت پر عمل کرنا بغیر تحری کے بھی اولی ہے، پھر جب مجتہد تحری کرلے اور نور فراست سے اس کا قلب مطمئن ہو جائے تو پھر قیاس پر عمل اور بھی اولی ہوگا، لہذا تعارض قیاس کی صورت میں قیاس پر ہی عمل ہوگا ، پھر اس سوال کا جواب کہ دو آیتوں یا دو حدیثوں میں تعارض کے وقت دونوں حجتیں کیوں ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں؟ یہ ہے کہ آیتوں اور سنتوں کے بعد دلیل شرعی یعنی قیاس موجود ہے جس کی طرف رجوع ہوسکتا ہے، اور قیاس کے بعد کوئی دلیل شرعی نہیں ہے، سوائے استصحاب کے جو ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں، اور رہا یہ سوال کہ ماقبل میں سور حمار میں تعارض کے وقت تو آپ نے استصحاب حال پر عمل کیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ ضرورۃ کیا گیا ہے۔
That acting on istishab (presumption of continuity) is not obligatory; rather, the mujtahid may act on whichever of the two [qiyas] he wishes, with the testimony of his heart, because qiyas is a proof upon which action is taken, whether the mujtahid reaches the truth or errs through that qiyas. So acting on one of the two qiyas, when one of them in right of action is a proof toward which the mujtahid's heart has become tranquil by the light of insight, is better than acting on istishab. 

Explanation: When two qiyas conflict, neither falls, unlike the case of two verses or two sunnahs where both proofs fall. Because if the qiyas fell, there would be no proof to know the ruling of this issue except istishab. Istishab means to keep a thing on its original state, like when there is doubt about water being pure or impure and there is no informer, then by istishab the water is pure because the original state is purity. This istishab is not a proof in our view, and qiyas is a proof. So the mujtahid now has the choice to act on whichever of the two qiyas he wishes, but after exerting judgment (taharrī) and acting on which his heart is tranquil. This taharrī is a condition in our view. Imam Shafi'i says that he may act without taharrī; in his view taharrī is not a condition. Therefore, Imam Shafi'i may have multiple statements on one issue at the same time, whereas if we have two statements on an issue, they are according to separate times, so one is correct and the other is invalid. 

The author is providing the proof for acting on one of the two qiyas and not resorting to istishab. He says: In qiyas, whether the mujtahid reaches the truth or errs, qiyas is a proof. Istishab is not a proof. So acting on a proof in contrast to a non-proof is better even without taharrī. Then when the mujtahid does taharrī and his heart becomes tranquil by the light of insight, then acting on qiyas is even more excellent. Therefore, in case of conflicting qiyas, action is taken on qiyas. Then the answer to the question: why do both proofs fall when two verses or two hadith conflict? It is that after verses and sunnahs, there exists a shar'i proof, i.e. qiyas, to which one can resort, and after qiyas there is no shar'i proof except istishab, which is not a proof in our view. As for the question that earlier in the case of the donkey [where there was conflict] you acted on istishab, the answer is that it was done out of necessity.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the ta'arud (conflict) of two qiyas. The author first establishes that when two analogies conflict, both are not dropped; the mujtahid has discretion to choose one based on his heart's inclination, because qiyas is a valid proof even if it leads to error. The commentary explains that unlike verses and hadith where both proofs fall due to no higher authority, qiyas remains because the only alternative is istishab (presumption of continuity), which Hanafis do not consider a proof. Istishab is defined as maintaining the original state in doubt, e.g., water remains pure if its purity is unknown. The Hanafi view is that istishab is not a hujja, so qiyas must be used. The mujtahid must perform taharrī (careful deliberation) to satisfy his heart; this is a condition (shart) for Hanafis. Imam Shafi'i does not require taharrī, which leads to multiple contradictory statements from him. The author also addresses an objection: in the case of the donkey (a hypothetical or narrated case), acting on istishab was allowed due to necessity. Thus the rule is that in ta'arud of qiyas, action is based on the stronger qiyas after taharrī, not on istishab.

Key Terms
الاستصحاب (al-istishāb): Presumption of continuity: keeping a thing on its original state when there is doubt about its change.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical deduction from a revealed text to a new case.
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Exertion of judgment to determine the correct ruling when proofs conflict.
التعارض (al-taʿāruḍ): Conflict between two proofs that require opposite rulings on the same case at the same time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two qiyas conflict, what does the Hanafi school require before choosing one?
A) Arbitrary choice without conditions
B) Taharrī (careful deliberation) until the heart is tranquil
C) Always prefer the one supported by a hadith
D) Abandon both and resort to istishab

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when two qiyas conflict, the mujtahid must perform taharrī to choose the stronger analogy, rather than resorting to istishab, which is not a valid proof.

The Authority of Tabi'un's Fatwa in Hanafi Usul
Concluding discussion on qiyas and presenting ikhtilaf on taqlid of Tabi'un

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on taqlid of a Tabi'i when their fatwa conflicts with a Companion's fatwa, and evaluate the evidence cited for each position.

Core Idea
A Tabi'i's fatwa is like qiyas: not discarded but weighed; whether taqlid of a Tabi'i is allowed is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This lesson completes the discussion on qiyas and moves to the authority of the Tabi'i (successor) in the presence of a conflicting Companion's fatwa. In Hanafi usul, the opinions of the Companions are treated like qiyas—they are not invalidated by conflict but are selected by evidence. Similarly, the fatwa of a Tabi'i, when prevalent during the Companion era, generates an internal school dispute: should a mujtahid follow it? We examine the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Recall the role of Companion sayings
The passage first states that conflicting sayings of Companions are like qiyas: one is preferred, not discarded. Understand that this is the baseline principle.
Companion sayings are not authoritative like Quran/Sunnah but are considered as evidence to be weighed.
2
Identify the issue regarding the Tabi'i
When a Tabi'i's fatwa is prevalent during the time of Companions and conflicts with a Companion's fatwa, what is the ruling on following the Tabi'i? This is the central question.
3
State the two positions within the Hanafi school
Some Hanafi scholars permit taqlid of the Tabi'i; others do not. This is an internal ikhtilaf.
The text mentions 'some of our mashayikh' for each view.
4
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's two narrations
First narration: 'I will not follow a Tabi'i because he is also a man like us' (equality). Second narration: 'I will follow him because the Companions used to refer to their sayings' (authority).
These narrations represent the two poles of the dispute.
5
Apply the example
The example of 'Ali (RA) allowing a son's testimony for his father, and Qadi Shurayh (a Tabi'i) ruling it impermissible, illustrates how the two views lead to different outcomes.
This example shows the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قیاس کے قائم مقام ہوگا ، اور پہلے آپ پڑھ چکے ہیں کہ جب دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہوتا ہے، تو قیاس باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے، بلکہ کسی ایک قیاس کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، اسی طرح اقوال صحابہ جب بمنزلہ قیاس ہیں، تو یہ اقوال ساقط نہ ہوں گے بلکہ مجتہد کسی ایک قول کو دلائل سے ترجیح دے گا ، اور عمل کرے گا۔ واما التابعی - اگر کسی تابعی کا فتوی دور صحابہ میں مروج ہو اور وہ صحابی کے فتوی سے مزاحم ہو جائے تو اس تابعی کی تقلید کے بارے میں دو قول ہیں، ہمارے بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک تابعی کی تقلید جائز ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے، جیسے حضرت علی کے نزدیک بیٹے کی شہادت باپ کے حق میں جائز تھی اور قاضی شریح جو تابعی ہیں ان کا فتوی عدم جواز کا تھا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ سے بھی اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں ، پہلی روایت ہے کہ امام صاحب نے کہا کہ میں تابعی کی تقلید نہیں کرونگا، اس لئے کہ وہ بھی ہماری طرح رجال ہیں، اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ میں ان کی تقلید کرونگا، کیونکہ صحابہ ان کے اقوال کی طرف رجوع کرتے تھے۔
It will be in place of qiyas, and you have already read that when two qiyas conflict, qiyas is not invalidated, rather preference is given to one qiyas. Similarly, when the sayings of the Companions are like qiyas, these sayings will not be discarded, but the mujtahid will prefer one saying based on evidence and act upon it. As for the Tabi'i - if a Tabi'i's fatwa is prevalent during the time of the Companions and it conflicts with a Companion's fatwa, then regarding following that Tabi'i there are two sayings: according to some of our scholars, following a Tabi'i is permissible, and according to some it is not permissible. For example, according to 'Ali, the testimony of a son in favor of his father was permissible, while Qadi Shurayh, who is a Tabi'i, gave a fatwa of impermissibility. From Imam Abu Hanifa there are also two narrations on this: the first narration is that the Imam said, 'I will not follow a Tabi'i because he is also a man like us.' The second narration is that 'I will follow him because the Companions used to refer to their sayings.'
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion on qiyas and then addresses the status of the fatwa of a Tabi'i (a successor of the Companions) in the presence of a contrary Companion's fatwa. The author first establishes that conflicting sayings of Companions are not discarded; rather, a mujtahid weighs them. Then he addresses the Tabi'i. There is disagreement among Hanafi scholars: some permit taqlid of a Tabi'i, others do not. Imam Abu Hanifa himself has two narrations. The example given is from 'Ali (RA) allowing a son's testimony for his father, while Qadi Shurayh (a Tabi'i) held it impermissible. This illustrates that the ruling depends on the strength of evidence, not merely the status of the narrator.

Key Terms
تابعی (Tabi'i): A Muslim who met a Companion and learned from them, but did not see the Prophet ﷺ.
تقلید (taqlid): Following the legal opinion of a mujtahid without knowing the evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Tabi'un lack knowledge
B) Because they are also men like us
C) Because their opinions are not preserved
D) Because Companions did not follow them

Key Takeaway
The authority of a Tabi'i's fatwa in Hanafi usul is debated; it remains a valid source but with internal disagreement that requires evidence-based preference.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Definition and First Two Conditions of Qiyas
Definition and first two negative conditions of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas linguistically and technically, and identify the two negative conditions that must be met for qiyas to be valid.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires that the original case is neither text-specifically exceptional nor itself contrary to analogy.

In this passage from a Hanafi usul commentary, the author opens the chapter on qiyas by defining it and then explaining its conditions. He begins by giving the linguistic and technical definitions, emphasizing that qiyas is an estimation of a branch case from an original due to a shared cause. He then states the first two conditions, which are negative: the original must not be specific to its ruling by a separate text, and it must not be a ruling that deviates from the general principles of qiyas. Understanding these conditions is crucial to ensure that qiyas is applied correctly.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic and technical definitions
Note that linguistically, qiyas means estimation or measurement, e.g., measuring a sandal to another. Technically, it is applying the ruling of an original (asl) to a branch (far') due to a shared effective cause (illah).
2
Understand the scope of the chapter
The passage outlines five topics: definition (nafs), condition (shart), pillar (rukn), ruling (hukm), and rebuttal (daf'). Our focus is on definition and the first two conditions.
3
Identify the first negative condition
The ruling of the original must not be specific to it by another text. If it is, it is exceptional and cannot be extended. Example: acceptance of Khuzayma's sole testimony was a special honor, so it cannot be used as a basis for qiyas.
4
Identify the second negative condition
The ruling of the original must not be itself an exception from qiyas. If a ruling contradicts the principles of analogy, it cannot be a basis. Example: obligation of purification due to loud laughter in prayer is a ruling established contrary to qiyas (since laughter normally nullifies purity, but here it obligates purification).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْقِيَاسِ وَهُوَ يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى بَيَانِ نَفْسِ الْقِيَاسِ وَشَرْطِهِ وَرُكْنِهِ وَحُكْمِهِ وَدَفْعِهِ أَمَا الْاوَل فَالْقِيَاسُ هُوَ التَّقْدِيرُ لُغَةٌ يُقَالُ قِسِ النَّعْلَ بِالنَّعْلِ أَى قَدِّرْهُ بِهِ وَاجْعَلْهُ نَظِيْرَ الْأَخَرِ وَالْفُقَهَاءُ إِذَا أَخَذُواحُكُمَ الْفَرْعِ مِنَ الْأَصْلِ سَمَوَاذْلِكَ قِيَاسًا لِتَقْدِيرِهِمْ الْفَرْعَ بِالْاَصْلِ فِي الْحُكْمِ وَالْعِلَةِ یعنی علل مؤثرہ پر شوافع کے اعتراضات اور اس کے جوابات، سب سے پہلے قیاس کی لغوی اور اصطلاحی تعریف کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کے لغوی معنی ہے اندازہ کرنا، ناپنا، جیسے کہا جاتا ہے قیس الفعل بالفعل ایک خَزَيْمَةَ وَحْدَهُ كَانَ حُكْمًا ثَبَتَ بِالنَّصِّ اِخْتِصَاصُهُ بِهِ كَرَامَةً لَهُ وَأَنْ لَا يَكُون الأَصْلُ مَعْدُوْلًا بِهِ عَنِ الْقِيَاسِ كَايْجَابِ الطَّهَارَةِ بِالْقَهْقَهُةِ فِي الصلوة ترجمہ: اور بہر حال قیاس کی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل (مقیس علیہ ) اپنے حکم کے ساتھ کسی دوسری نص کے سبب سے مخصوص نہ ہو، جیسے تنہا خزیمہ کی شہادت کا قبول ہونا ایسا حکم ہے کہ ثابت ہے نص سے اس حکم کا ان کے ساتھ خاص ہونا ان کی کرامت و اعزاز کے پیش نظر اور (دوسری شرط یہ کہ اصل قیاس سے ہٹی ہوئی نہ ہو، جیسے نماز میں قہقہہ کی وجہ سے طہارت کا واجب ہونا۔ تشریح:- مصنف اللہ قیاس کی شرطیں بیان کر رہے ہیں ، قیاس کی چار شرطیں ہیں ، دو عدمی اور دو وجودی ہیں، پہلے عدمی شرطوں کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، عدمی میں پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ کا جو حکم ہے وہ کسی نص سے اصل کے ساتھ مخصوص نہ ہو، کیونکہ جب اصل کا حکم اصل کے ساتھ مخصوص ہو گا تو اس حکم کو دوسری جگہ متعدی نہیں کر سکتے ، پھر اس اصل پر دوسرے کو قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ، جیسے تنہا حضرت خزیمہ جس کی شہادت کا قبول ہونا یہ بطور اعزاز کے تھے حدیث سے حضرت خزیمہ مال کی خصوصیت ہے، لہذا اس پر کسی دوسرے کو چاہے وہ خلفاء راشدین ہی کیوں نہ ہوں قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ حضرت خزیمہ کا قصہ یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی ا يہ تم نے ایک عرابی سے گھوڑ اخریدا، اور اس کو ساتھ لیکر چلے تا کہ اس کو قیمت دیدیں ، آپ سالی سیستم تیز چلنے لگے وہ آہستہ چل رہا تھا، وہ پیچھے اور لوگوں سے بھاؤ تاؤ کرنے لگا، اور انہیں پتہ نہیں تھا کہ حضور صلی نیا دینی گھوڑا خرید چکے ہیں، پھر وہ اعرابی آواز دیکر کہنے لگا کہ حضور صلی اینم اگر آپ خریدتے ہوں تو بتائیں ورنہ میں نے بیچ دیا، حضور صلی نا ہی تم اس کی آواز سنکر ٹھہر گئے ، اور فرمایا یہ کیا کہہ رہے ہو، میں تو خرید چکا ہوں، تو وہ اعرابی کہنے لگا گواہ لاؤ، حضرت خزیمہ پینے سے موجود تھے، انہوں نے کہا میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ آپ سی تم نے خریدا ہے، آپ مسی ہی تم نے فرمایا ، خزیمہ تم کیسے گواہی دیتے ہو؟ تم تو خریدتے وقت تھے نہیں ؟ انہوں نے کہا چونکہ آپ کہہ رہے ہیں اس لئے مجھے یقین ہے کہ آپ نے خریدا ہے ، آپ مالی ستایلی ایمن نے ان کو اعزازی سرٹیفکیٹ عطا کیا من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه ، جس کی شہادت خزیمہ دیں وہ تنہا کافی ہیں، آپ صلی یا یہ تم نے ان کی گواہی دو آدمیوں کے برابر قراردی، تو تنہا حضرت خزیمہ کی شہادت کا قبول ہونا یہ حکم دوسری نص یعنی من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه ، سے حضرت خزیمہ اللہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے، لہذا اس پر دوسرے کو قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ وان لا يكون الاصل : - دوسری عدمی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ خلاف قیاس نہ ہو، کیونکہ جب اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ خلاف قیاس ہوگا تو اس پر دوسرے کو کیسے قیاس کر سکتے ہیں، جیسے رکوع سجدے والی
Chapter of Qiyas. It includes explanation of the essence of qiyas, its condition, its pillar, its ruling, and its rebuttal. As for the first, qiyas linguistically is estimation; it is said: 'Measure the sandal by the sandal,' i.e., estimate it by it and make it like the other. The jurists, when they take the ruling of the branch from the original, they call that qiyas, because they estimated the branch by the original in ruling and cause. Translation: This is the chapter of qiyas, and it includes the explanation of the essence of qiyas, its condition, its pillar, its ruling, and its rebuttal. So the first: qiyas is estimation linguistically; it is said 'qis al-na'la bi al-na'li' i.e., measure it with it and make it similar to the other. And when the jurists take the ruling of the branch from the original, they name that qiyas, due to their estimation of the branch with the original in ruling and cause. Commentary: The author is beginning the chapter of qiyas; he will specially explain five things: (1) definition of qiyas, (2) condition of qiyas, (3) pillar of qiyas, (4) ruling of qiyas, (5) rebuttal of qiyas i.e., the objections of the Shafi'is on effective causes and their answers. First he gives the linguistic and technical definition of qiyas: qiyas linguistically means estimation, measuring, as it is said 'qis al-na'la bi al-na'li' i.e., estimate one sandal with the other, make it like the other. And the author gives the technical definition: when the jurists establish the ruling of the original (maqis 'alayh) for the branch (maqis), due to a common cause between them, then taking and establishing the ruling for the branch from the original is called qiyas, because they estimated the branch with the original in ruling and cause, compared them, so they measured the branch by the original in ruling and cause. So the correspondence between the linguistic and technical meanings becomes clear. As for its condition: that the original not be specific to its ruling by another text, like the acceptance of the testimony of Khuzayma alone; it was a ruling established by text, its specificity to him as an honor for him. And that the original not be turned away from qiyas, like the obligation of purification due to laughter in prayer. Translation: And as for the condition of qiyas, it is that the original (maqis 'alayh) not be specific to its ruling by another text, like the acceptance of the sole testimony of Khuzayma; such a ruling is established by text, its specificity to him due to his honor and veneration. And the second condition: that the original not be turned away from qiyas, like the obligation of purification by loud laughter in prayer. Commentary: The author is explaining the conditions of qiyas. Qiyas has four conditions: two negative and two positive. First he explains the negative conditions. The first negative condition: the ruling of the original (maqis 'alayh) must not be specific to the original by a text, because when the ruling of the original is specific to it, the ruling cannot be transferred to another place; and then one cannot make qiyas on that original. For example, the acceptance of the sole testimony of Hadrat Khuzayma; this was a special honor from the hadith, a specificity of Hadrat Khuzayma may Allah be pleased with him. Therefore one cannot make qiyas on anyone else, even if they be the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The story of Hadrat Khuzayma: The Prophet (peace be upon him) bought a horse from a Bedouin and took it with him to give the price. The Prophet rode fast, the Bedouin walked slowly, and he started bargaining with other people who did not know that the Prophet had already bought the horse. Then the Bedouin called out saying: O Prophet of Allah, if you have bought it tell me, otherwise I have sold it. The Prophet stopped upon hearing his voice and said: What are you saying? I have already bought it. The Bedouin said: Bring a witness. Hadrat Khuzayma was present drinking, and he said: I bear witness that you have bought it. The Prophet said: O Khuzayma, how can you bear witness? You were not present at the time of purchase. He said: Because you are saying it, I am certain that you bought it. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave him an honorary certificate: 'Whoever has Khuzayma as a witness is sufficient.' The Prophet made his testimony equivalent to two men. So the acceptance of the sole testimony of Hadrat Khuzayma is a ruling specific to him by another text, i.e., 'man shahida lahu khuzaymatun fahuwa hasbuhu', so one cannot make qiyas on anyone else. 'And that the original not be' - the second negative condition: that the original (maqis 'alayh) should not be contrary to qiyas, because when the original is contrary to qiyas, how can one make qiyas on another? For example, the case of bowing and prostration...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Qiyas (analogical deduction) from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary. The author first states that the chapter covers five topics: (1) the nature of qiyas, (2) its conditions, (3) its pillar (components), (4) its ruling, and (5) the rebuttal of objections against it. He then gives the linguistic and technical definitions of qiyas. Linguistically, qiyas means ‘estimation’ or ‘measurement’, as when one measures a sandal against another. Technically, according to the Hanafi jurists, qiyas is applying a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far‘) due to a shared effective cause (illah). The author then explains the first two conditions of qiyas, which are negative. First, the original case must not have its ruling restricted to it by another text; otherwise the ruling is exceptional and cannot be extended. The example given is the acceptance of the sole testimony of the Companion Khuzayma ibn Thabit, which was a special honor from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and cannot be generalised. The second negative condition is that the ruling of the original must not be itself an exception from qiyas, i.e., it must not be a ruling that contradicts the general principles of qiyas. The example is the obligation of ablution due to loud laughter in prayer, which is a God-given ruling that is not based on analogy. These conditions ensure that qiyas is applied only when the original is a suitable basis for extension.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Linguistically: estimation; technically: deriving the ruling of a branch from the original due to a common cause.
الأصل (al-asl): The original case (maqis 'alayh) whose ruling is established by text or ijma, and from which the ruling is transferred to the branch.
الفرع (al-far'): The branch case (maqis) whose ruling is sought and is derived from the asl through qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a ruling that cannot be used as a basis for qiyas because it is specific to a particular person?
A) Obligation of zakat on wealth
B) Acceptance of Khuzayma's sole testimony
C) Prohibition of interest
D) Obligation of five daily prayers

Key Takeaway
For qiyas to be valid, the original ruling must be generalisable, meaning it must not be text-specifically exceptional nor itself an exception to the principles of analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Four Conditions for Valid Qiyas
Systematic explanation of qiyas conditions with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four conditions for valid qiyas: two negative (no takhsis, no khilaf al-qiyas) and two positive (shar'i ruling extends to a similar branch with no text).

Core Idea
Qiyas is only valid when the original ruling is not a unique exception and not itself contrary to analogy.

Analogical reasoning (qiyas) is a cornerstone of Hanafi jurisprudence, but it cannot be applied arbitrarily. This lesson unpacks the four conditions that must be met for a qiyas to be valid: two negative conditions (the original must not be text-specified or contrary to qiyas) and two positive conditions (the ruling must be shar'i and the branch must be a genuine similar with no text). Understanding these conditions prevents misuse of qiyas and ensures sound legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first negative condition: no takhsis
Check whether the original ruling (ḥukm al-aṣl) is specified to a particular person or case by a text. If it is, it cannot be extended via qiyas. Example: Khuzaymah's sole testimony being accepted is specific to him due to a hadith.
Takhṣīṣ makes the ruling non-transferable.
2
Identify the second negative condition: not khilāf al-qiyās
Check whether the original ruling itself is an exception to the general principle. If it is established by text as a deviation from the norm, it cannot be used as an original. Example: loud laughter breaking wudu in prayer is contrary to qiyas.
Khilāf al-qiyās rulings are anomalies and cannot be analogized.
3
Apply the first positive condition: the ruling must be shar‘ī and extendable
The ruling must be a shar‘ī (legal) ruling, not a linguistic label or other non-legal matter. It must be transferable to a branch that is similar (naẓīr).
The branch must be genuinely similar; similarity in excuse or severity is not enough.
4
Apply the second positive condition: no text on the branch
Ensure there is no existing text (naṣṣ) that already governs the branch case. If there is, qiyas cannot be used to alter it.
Example: requiring faith in expiation slaves is text-based, so qiyas cannot change it.

الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال قیاس کی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل (مقیس علیہ ) اپنے حکم کے ساتھ کسی دوسری نص کے سبب سے مخصوص نہ ہو، جیسے تنہا خزیمہ کی شہادت کا قبول ہونا ایسا حکم ہے کہ ثابت ہے نص سے اس حکم کا ان کے ساتھ خاص ہونا ان کی کرامت و اعزاز کے پیش نظر اور (دوسری شرط یہ کہ اصل قیاس سے ہٹی ہوئی نہ ہو، جیسے نماز میں قہقہہ کی وجہ سے طہارت کا واجب ہونا۔ تشریح:- مصنف اللہ قیاس کی شرطیں بیان کر رہے ہیں ، قیاس کی چار شرطیں ہیں ، دو عدمی اور دو وجودی ہیں، پہلے عدمی شرطوں کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، عدمی میں پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ کا جو حکم ہے وہ کسی نص سے اصل کے ساتھ مخصوص نہ ہو، کیونکہ جب اصل کا حکم اصل کے ساتھ مخصوص ہو گا تو اس حکم کو دوسری جگہ متعدی نہیں کر سکتے ، پھر اس اصل پر دوسرے کو قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ، جیسے تنہا حضرت خزیمہ جس کی شہادت کا قبول ہونا یہ بطور اعزاز کے تھے حدیث سے حضرت خزیمہ مال کی خصوصیت ہے، لہذا اس پر کسی دوسرے کو چاہے وہ خلفاء راشدین ہی کیوں نہ ہوں
۱
قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ حضرت خزیمہ کا قصہ یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ایک اعرابی سے گھوڑا خریدا، اور اس کو ساتھ لیکر چلے تا کہ اس کو قیمت دیدیں ، آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تیز چلنے لگے وہ آہستہ چل رہا تھا، وہ پیچھے اور لوگوں سے بھاؤ تاؤ کرنے لگا، اور انہیں پتہ نہیں تھا کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم گھوڑا خرید چکے ہیں، پھر وہ اعرابی آواز دیکر کہنے لگا کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اگر آپ خریدتے ہوں تو بتائیں ورنہ میں نے بیچ دیا، حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کی آواز سنکر ٹھہر گئے ، اور فرمایا یہ کیا کہہ رہے ہو، میں تو خرید چکا ہوں، تو وہ اعرابی کہنے لگا گواہ لاؤ، حضرت خزیمہ پاس سے موجود تھے، انہوں نے کہا میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ آپ نے خریدا ہے، آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ، خزیمہ تم کیسے گواہی دیتے ہو؟ تم تو خریدتے وقت تھے نہیں ؟ انہوں نے کہا چونکہ آپ کہہ رہے ہیں اس لئے مجھے یقین ہے کہ آپ نے خریدا ہے ، آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ان کو اعزازی سرٹیفکیٹ عطا کیا من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه ، جس کی شہادت خزیمہ دیں وہ تنہا کافی ہیں، آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ان کی گواہی دو آدمیوں کے برابر قراردی، تو تنہا حضرت خزیمہ کی شہادت کا قبول ہونا یہ حکم دوسری نص یعنی من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه ، سے حضرت خزیمہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے، لہذا اس پر دوسرے کو قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ وان لا يكون الاصل : - دوسری عدمی شرط یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ خلاف قیاس نہ ہو، کیونکہ جب اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ خلاف قیاس ہوگا تو اس پر دوسرے کو کیسے قیاس کر سکتے ہیں، جیسے رکوع سجدے والی نماز میں قہقہہ مار کر ہنسنے سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے، تو قہقہہ سے وضو کا ٹوٹنا خلاف قیاس ہے، کیونکہ وضو نجاست سے ٹوٹتا ہے اور قہقہہ میں کوئی نجاست کا خروج نہیں ہے، لہذا قہقہہ سے نماز میں وضو نہیں ٹوٹنا چاہیے جیسے نماز کے علاوہ میں قہقہہ سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹتا لیکن حدیث کی وجہ سے نماز میں قہقہہ کو خلاف قیاس ناقض وضو قرار دیا، لہذا اس پر نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت کو قیاس نہیں کر سکتے کیونکہ مقیس علیہ یعنی صلاۃ میں قہقہہ کا ناقض وضو ہونا خلاف قیاس ہے۔
وَاَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ الثَّابِتُ بِالنَّصَ بِعَيْنِهِ إِلَى فَرْعِ هُوَ نَظِيْرُهُ وَلَا نَصَ فِيْهِ فَلَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لا ثُبَاتِ اِسْمِ الْخَمْرِ لِسَائِرِ الْأَشْرِبَةِ لِاَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِحُكُم شَرْعِي وَلَا لِصِحَّةِ ظِهَارِ الذِّمِّي لِكَوْنِهِ تَغْيِيراً لِلْحُرْمَةِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ فِي الْأَصْلِ إِلَى إِطْلَاقِهَا فِى الْفَرْعِ عَنِ الْغَايَةِ وَلَا لِتَعْدِيَةِ الْحُكْمِ مِنَ النَّاسِي فِي الْفِطْرِ إِلَى الْمُكْرَهِ وَالْخَاطِيْ لِاَنَّ عُذْرَهُمَا دُونَ عُذْرِهِ فَكَانَ تَعْدِيَتُهُ إِلَى مَا لَيْسَ بِنَظِيْرِهِ وَلَا لِشَرْطِ الْإِيْمَانِ فِي رَقَبَهِ كَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِينِ وَالظِّهَارِ وَفِي مَصْرَفِ الصَّدَقَاتِ لأَنه تَعْدِيَةٌ إلى مَا فِيْهِ نَصٌ بِتَغْيِيرِهِ .
ترجمہ: اور ( تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ حکم شرعی جو ثابت ہو نص سے بعینہ اس فرع کی جانب متعدی ہو جو اس کی نظیر ہے، اور اس میں کوئی نص نہ ہو، پس تعلیل درست نہ ہوگی خمر کا نام ثابت کرنے کے لئے تمام شرابوں کے لئے ، اسلئے کہ یہ حکم شرعی نہیں ہے، اور نہیں ہے ( درست قیاس کرنا) ذمی کے ظہار کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے ، قیاس کے تبدیل کرنے والا ہونے کی وجہ سے اس حرمت کو جو ختم ہو جاتی ہے کفارہ سے اصل (مسلمان ) میں ،فرع ( ذمی ) میں اس حرمت کے غایت سے اطلاق کی طرف ( یعنی غایت سے اطلاق کی طرف تبدیل کرنے والا ہونے کی وجہ سے ) اور نہیں ہے ( درست قیاس کرنا ) روزہ ٹوٹنے میں ناسی سے حکم کو متعدی کرنے کے لئے مکرہ اور خاطی کی طرف ، اس لئے که ان دونوں کا عذر ناسی سے کم درجہ کا عذر ہے ، پس ناسی کے حکم کو متعدی کرنا ( مکرہ اور خاطی کی طرف ) ایسی چیز کی طرف حکم کو متعدی کرنا ہے جو ناسی کی نظیر نہیں ہے، اور نہیں ہے ( درست قیاس کرنا ) ایمان کی شرط کے لئے کفارہ یمین و ظہار کے رقبہ میں اور صدقات کے مصرف میں ، کیونکہ یہ قیاس تغییر حکم کے ساتھ ایسی چیز کی طرف حکم کو متعدی کرنا ہے جس میں نص موجود ہے۔ تشریح:- تیسری شرط اور دو وجودی شرطوں میں پہلی شرط بیان کر رہے ہیں، یہ کہنے کو تو ایک شرط ہے مگر حقیقت
Translation: And nevertheless, the condition for qiyas is that the original (maqis 'alayh) is not specified with its ruling due to another text, like the acceptance of the testimony of Khuzaymah alone — such a ruling is established by text that this ruling is specific to him due to his honor and esteem. And (the second condition) is that the original is not contrary to qiyas, like the obligation of purification due to loud laughter in prayer. Explanation: The author is explaining the conditions of qiyas. Qiyas has four conditions: two negative and two positive. First, he mentions the negative conditions. The first negative condition is that the original, i.e., maqis 'alayh, its ruling is not specified to the original by any text, because when the ruling of the original is specific to the original, then we cannot transfer that ruling to another place, nor can we make qiyas on that original. For example, the acceptance of the testimony of Hadrat Khuzaymah alone — this was a honorific, from the hadith, the specificity of Hadrat Khuzaymah's [property?]. Therefore, no one else, even if they are the Rightly Guided Caliphs, can be analogized to him. The story of Hadrat Khuzaymah: The Prophet purchased a horse from a Bedouin and took it with him to pay the price. The Prophet walked quickly, the Bedouin walked slowly, and he began bargaining with others behind, not knowing that the Prophet had already bought the horse. Then the Bedouin called out saying: O Prophet, if you have bought, tell me, otherwise I sold it. The Prophet heard his voice, stopped, and said: What are you saying? I have already bought. The Bedouin said: Bring a witness. Hadrat Khuzaymah was present and said: I bear witness that you bought it. The Prophet said: Khuzaymah, how can you bear witness? You were not present at the time of purchase? He said: Because you are saying so, I am certain that you bought it. The Prophet granted him an honorary certificate: 'Whoever has Khuzaymah as witness, it is sufficient for him.' The Prophet made his testimony equal to two men. So the acceptance of the testimony of Khuzaymah alone is a ruling specified by another text, i.e., 'Whoever has Khuzaymah as witness, it is sufficient for him', specific to Hadrat Khuzaymah. Therefore, no one else can be analogized to him. 'And that the original be not [contrary to qiyas]': The second negative condition is that the original, i.e., maqis 'alayh, is not contrary to qiyas, because if the original is contrary to qiyas, how can we analogize another to it? For example, in prayer that has bowing and prostration, loud laughter breaks wudu. That loud laughter breaks wudu is contrary to qiyas, because wudu is broken by impurity, and there is no impurity in loud laughter. So loud laughter should not break wudu in prayer, just as outside prayer it does not break wudu. But due to a hadith, loud laughter in prayer was declared a breaker of wudu contrary to qiyas. Therefore, we cannot analogize to it the funeral prayer or the prostration of recitation, because the original, i.e., the prayer with bowing and prostration, loud laughter being a breaker of wudu is contrary to qiyas. 'And that the shar'i ruling established by a specific text extends to a branch that is its similar and in which there is no text, so that the ta'lil (causal reasoning) is not correct for establishing the name of khamr for all other intoxicating beverages, because it is not a shar'i ruling; nor for the validity of dhihar of a dhimmi, because it is a alteration of the unlimited prohibition by expiation in the original to its unrestrictedness in the branch without the [limiting] purpose; nor for extending the ruling from the forgetful one who breaks fast to the coerced and the errant, because their excuse is less than his excuse, so extending it to what is not its similar; nor for the condition of faith in the slave of expiation for an oath and dhihar and in the dispensation of charity, because it is an extension to something about which there is a text with alteration.' Translation: And (the third condition is that the shar'i ruling established by a specific text extends to the branch that is its similar and in which there is no text; so ta'lil will not be correct for establishing the name of khamr for all other intoxicating beverages, because it is not a shar'i ruling; nor (is correct qiyas) for the validity of dhihar of a dhimmi, because it alters the prohibition that ends with expiation in the original to its unrestriction in the branch without the purpose; nor (is correct qiyas) for extending the ruling from the forgetful in breaking fast to the coerced and the errant, because both their excuses are less than his, so his extension to what is not his similar; nor (is correct qiyas) for the condition of faith in the slave of expiation for oath and dhihar and in the dispensation of charity, because this qiyas is an extension with alteration of the ruling to something about which a text exists. Explanation: The third condition and the first of the two positive conditions is being explained; it is one condition in word but in reality...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author states that qiyas has four conditions: two negative (adamī) and two positive (wujūdī). The first negative condition is that the original ruling (ḥukm al-aṣl) should not be specific to the original case due to a text. If a ruling is established by a text specifically for a particular person or situation, it cannot be extended via qiyas to others. The example given is the acceptance of the sole testimony of Sayyidunā Khuzaymah (radiyallāhu ‘anhu), derived from the prophetic saying, 'Whoever has Khuzaymah as a witness, it is sufficient for him.' This privilege is unique to Khuzaymah due to his special virtue, and no one else, not even the Rightly Guided Caliphs, can be analogized to him. The second negative condition is that the original should not be itself contrary to qiyas (khilāf al-qiyās). If a ruling is an exception established by text against the general principle, it cannot serve as an original for further analogy. The example is that loud laughter (qahqaha) during a prayer that includes bowing and prostration breaks wudu. This is contrary to the general principle that wudu is only broken by the exit of impurities, and laughter does not involve that. It is established solely by a hadith as an exception. Therefore, one cannot analogize the funeral prayer or prostration of recitation to this, because the original itself is khilāf al-qiyās. The first positive condition is that the ruling must be a shar‘ī (legal) ruling established by a specific text, and it must be extendable to a branch (far‘) that is similar (naẓīr) to the original and has no textual ruling. Several invalid applications are then listed to illustrate violations of this condition: (1) Trying to apply the name 'khamr' (wine) to all intoxicating drinks by qiyas, because 'khamr' is a name, not a shar‘ī ruling. (2) Trying to validate the ẓihār of a dhimmī (non-Muslim subject) by qiyas on the ẓihār of a Muslim, because in the original (Muslim) the marital prohibition is removed by expiation, but in the dhimmī the prohibition would be unrestricted without the purpose (ghāyah) of lifting the prohibition. (3) Extending the ruling of a forgetful person (nāsī) who breaks the fast to a coerced person (mukrah) or an errant person (khāṭi’), because their excuses are weaker, so they are not similar. (4) Requiring faith (īmān) in the slave for expiation (kaffārah) for oath and ẓihār and for the recipients of charity (ṣadaqāt), because there is already a text on these matters, so qiyas would alter the ruling. The passage ends mid-sentence but clearly presents the conditions systematically.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a similar branch due to a common effective cause.
اصل (aṣl): The original case (maqīs ‘alayh) that possesses a known ruling from text or consensus.
فرع (far‘): The branch case to which the ruling is extended via qiyas.
نص (naṣṣ): A clear text from Quran or Sunnah that gives a ruling.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification of a general text to a particular case or person.
خلاف القياس (khilāf al-qiyās): A ruling that is established as an exception to the general principle of qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid original (aṣl) for qiyas according to the Hanafi conditions discussed?
A) The acceptance of the sole testimony of Khuzaymah, since it is a ruling from the Prophet.
B) The breaking of wudu by loud laughter in prayer, as it is established by hadith.
C) The obligation of zakat on gold, as it is a shar‘ī ruling not specific to a person and not contrary to qiyas.
D) The condition of faith in the expiation slave, because it is a ruling from the text.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is only valid when the original ruling is not a unique exception, not itself contrary to analogy, is a shar'i ruling, and extends to a similar branch with no existing text.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Third Condition of Valid Qiyas
Stating the third condition with four illustrations of invalid qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the third condition of qiyas (transfer of a legal ruling to a true analogue) and identify which of the four invalid analogies fails and why.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires a legal ruling, a true analogue, and no text on the branch — anything less is invalid.

This passage from Al-Husami's matn presents a crucial filter in analogical reasoning: the ruling being transferred must be a legal ruling (not linguistic), and the branch must be a perfect analogue (nazir) without an independent text. Four concrete examples show how qiyas fails when these conditions are violated, helping you distinguish valid from invalid analogy in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition
The third condition requires that the hukm shar'i (legal ruling) established by text be transferred exactly to a branch that is its analogue (nazir) and for which no text exists. Any change in the ruling or lack of full equivalence nullifies the qiyas.
The ruling must be 'bi-aynihi' (exactly itself) — no alteration of its nature.
2
Analyze the first example: name of khamr
The attempted qiyas: other intoxicants are like khamr in intoxication, so they should be called khamr. Hanafis reject this because the name 'khamr' is a linguistic ruling, not a legal one. Qiyas only operates on legal rulings.
This also involves a cross-madhhab dispute (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i).
3
Analyze the second example: zihar of a dhimmi
For a Muslim, zihar creates a prohibition that ends with expiation. For a dhimmi, qiyas would apply, but the prohibition would become absolute (no expiation). This changes the ruling, so it fails the exact transfer condition.
The nature of the ruling is altered — not identical.
4
Analyze the third example: forgetful to coerced/errant
The forgetful (nasi) who breaks his fast has a strong excuse; his fast remains valid. The coerced (mukrah) and errant (khati') have weaker excuses. Their cases are not analogues (nazir) to the nasi, so qiyas is invalid.
The branch must be equal in the effective cause ('illa).
5
Analyze the fourth example: faith condition in expiation
There is an explicit text requiring faith in the slave for expiation of oath and zihar. Qiyas cannot operate when a text governs the branch directly. Additionally, the transfer would change the ruling by dropping the faith condition.
Two violations: existing text and change of ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاَنْ يَتَعَدَّى الْحُكْمُ الشَّرْعِيُّ الثَّابِتُ بِالنَّصَ بِعَيْنِهِ إِلَى فَرْعِ هُوَ نَظِيْرُهُ وَلَا نَصَ فِيْهِ فَلَا يَسْتَقِيمُ التَّعْلِيلُ لِإثْبَاتِ اِسْمِ الْخَمْرِ لِسَائِرِ الْأَشْرِبَةِ لِاَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِحُكُمٍ شَرْعِيٍّ وَلَا لِصِحَّةِ ظِهَارِ الذِّمِّيِّ لِكَوْنِهِ تَغْيِيراً لِلْحُرْمَةِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ فِي الْأَصْلِ إِلَى إِطْلَاقِهَا فِى الْفَرْعِ عَنِ الْغَايَةِ وَلَا لِتَعْدِيَةِ الْحُكْمِ مِنَ النَّاسِي فِي الْفِطِر إِلَى الْمُكْرَهِ وَالْخَاطِيْ لِاَنَّ عُذْرَهُمَا دُونَ عُذْرِهِ فَكَانَ تَعْدِيَتُهُ إِلَى مَا لَيْسَ بِنَظِيْرِهِ وَلَا لِشَرْطِ الْإِيْمَانِ فِي رَقَبَهِ كَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِينِ وَالظِّهَارِ وَفِي مَصْرَفِ الصَّدَقَاتِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعْدِيَةٌ إلى مَا فِيْهِ نَصٌّ بِتَغْيِيْرِه
And that the legal ruling established by a text (nass) be transferred exactly to a branch that is its analogue and for which there is no text. Therefore, analogical reasoning (ta'lil) is not valid for establishing the name of khamr for all other intoxicating drinks, because it is not a legal ruling. Nor is it valid for the validity of zihar of a dhimmi, because it would be a change from the prohibition that is terminated by expiation in the original [case of a Muslim] to an absolute release from the restriction in the branch. Nor is it valid for transferring the ruling from the forgetful person who breaks his fast to the one under compulsion or the one who errs, because the excuse of the latter two is weaker than his excuse; so transferring his ruling to what is not its analogue [occurs]. Nor is it valid for the condition of faith in the slave for the expiation of an oath and zihar and in the recipients of charity, because it is a transfer to something for which there is a text, along with a change.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from Al-Husami's matn states the third condition for valid qiyas (analogical reasoning): The legal ruling (hukm shar'i) established by a text (nass) must be transferred exactly (bi-aynihi) to a branch (far') that is analogous (nazir) to the original (asl), and there must be no independent text governing the branch. The author then provides four examples where qiyas fails due to violation of one aspect of this condition.

First example: Extending the name 'khamr' to all intoxicating drinks. The Shafi'is argue that since khamr intoxicates, any intoxicating drink should be treated the same. The Hanafis respond that the ruling that khamr is haram and entails hadd is a legal ruling, but the name 'khamr' itself is a linguistic (lughawi) classification, not a legal ruling. Therefore, analogizing other drinks to khamr in name is invalid because the condition requires a legal ruling.

Second example: The validity of zihar (a form of divorce) by a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject). A Muslim's zihar is valid and renders his wife prohibited until he performs expiation (kaffarah). The Shafi'is analogize the dhimmi's zihar to the Muslim's. The Hanafis reject this because in the Muslim's case, the prohibition (hurmah) is limited and ends with expiation (muntahiyah bi al-kaffarah). In the dhimmi's case, if qiyas were applied, the prohibition would become absolute (mutlaq) without the possibility of expiation (since dhimmi is not required to perform kaffarah). This changes the very nature of the ruling, violating the condition of exact transfer (bi-aynihi).

Third example: Transferring the ruling of a forgetful person (nasi) who breaks his fast to one who is coerced (mukrah) or errs (khati'). The forgetful person's fast is not invalidated because he has a strong excuse (forgetfulness). The coerced and the errant have weaker excuses (compulsion and mistake). So their cases are not analogous (not nazir); the transfer would be to something not a proper analogue, violating the condition that the far' must be a nazir.

Fourth example: The condition of faith (iman) in the slave for expiation of an oath or zihar, and for the recipients of charity. Some might analogize from cases where faith is not a condition. However, there is an explicit text (nass) requiring faith in the slave (e.g., Quran 4:92) and in the recipients (e.g., Quran 9:60 for zakat). Qiyas cannot operate when there is a text on the branch, and also the transfer would change the ruling (since the text specifies faith). Thus this qiyas invalid due to both the existence of a text and the change in ruling.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a branch (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
حكم شرعي (hukm shar‘i): A legal ruling from the Lawgiver concerning the actions of the mukallaf, such as obligation, prohibition, etc.
نظير (nazir): Analogue; the branch must be equal in effective cause and overall similarity to the original, not inferior.
تعليل (ta'lil): Analogical reasoning or justification; the process of identifying an 'illa to transfer a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to analogize other intoxicating drinks to khamr for the purpose of establishing the name 'khamr'?
A) Because there is a text on other intoxicants
B) Because the name 'khamr' is a linguistic ruling, not a legal ruling
C) Because other intoxicants are not intoxicating
D) Because the analogy would change the ruling

Key Takeaway
For qiyas to be valid, the ruling transferred must be a legal ruling, the branch must be a perfect analogue, and no text may govern the branch; violation of any element invalidates the analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
First Condition of Qiyas: Ruling Must Be Shari'
Explaining the first condition with a Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over intoxicants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a Shari' ruling from a linguistic ruling, and apply the first condition of qiyas to invalidate analogies based on linguistic meanings.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires the original ruling to be Shari'; analogies based on linguistic meanings are invalid.

We begin with the first condition of valid qiyas in Hanafi usul: the ruling of the original case must be a Shari' ruling, not a linguistic or customary one. The Hanafis use this condition to reject the Shafi'i analogy of other intoxicants to wine, arguing that 'covering the intellect' is a linguistic attribute, not a legal ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
Read the opening lines: the ruling of the asl must be a Shari' hukm, not a lughawi hukm. This means the ruling must be established by the Lawgiver (Allah or His Messenger), not derived from language or custom.
Note: A linguistic meaning (like 'covering the intellect') is not a legal ruling; it is a definition.
2
Understand the Shafi'i analogy
Shafi'is analogize other intoxicants to khamr: since khamr intoxicates and covers the intellect, other intoxicants share this attribute, so they should carry the same ruling (prohibition and hadd penalty). The attribute is intoxication (mukhamara).
3
Apply the Hanafi critique
Hanafis argue that 'covering the intellect' is a linguistic meaning (the literal definition of khamr), not a Shari' ruling. The Shari' ruling on khamr (prohibition and hadd) is specific to the substance called khamr. Since the attribute is linguistic, the first condition fails, and qiyas is invalid.
This critique illustrates the strict Hanafi requirement that the illah (effective cause) must be a Shari' attribute, not merely a linguistic one.
