الفيض الحجازي شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي

الطعام بالطعام الاسواء بسواء اس میں نص کا حکم طعام کو طعام کے بدلہ کمی بیشی سے بیچنا جائز نہ ہونا ہے ، اور اس کی علت قدر و جنس ہے، مگر یہ نص اس علت پر صراحہ مشتمل نہیں ہے بلکہ اشارہ مشتمل ہے، وہ اس طرح کہ سواء بسواء فرمایا اور برابری بغیر کیل کے نہیں ہوتی ہے، پس اس سے علت نکلی قدر اور طعام کا طعام سے مقابلہ ہے یہ دلیل ہے جنس کے علت ہونے کی تو علت قدر اور جنس ہوئی ، غرض رکن قیاس وہ وصف ہے جس کو اصل کے حکم پر علامت قرار دیا گیا ہو اور یہ وصف فرع میں بھی ہے اس لئے فرع کو بھی حکم میں اصل کی نظیر بنایا گیا ہو، یعنی اصل کا حکم فرع میں بھی متعدی کیا گیا ہو، اس سے یہ بات مفہوم ہوئی کہ قیاس کے چار رکن ہیں (۱) اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ (۲) فرع یعنی مقیس (۳) حکم (۴) اور وصف جامع ، ان میں چونکہ وصف جامع بنیادی رکن ہے، اس لئے مصنف نے صرف اسی کا ذکر کیا، مصنف نے علت کو علامت سے تعبیر کیا جس کے لئے لفظ لائے علما اس لئے کہ احکام شرعیہ کی علمیتیں محض علامت اور نشانیاں ہیں ، مثبت احکام نہیں ہیں، مثبت در حقیقت اللہ تعالی ہیں۔

وهو الوصف الصالح:- مصنف سے فرماتے ہیں کہ وصف میں دوباتیں پایا جانا ضروری ہے (۱) پہلی بات یہ کہ وہ وصف صالح ہو یعنی وصف میں یہ صلاحیت ہو کہ حکم کو اس کی طرف منسوب کیا جا سکے (۲) وصف مُعدل ہو یعنی وصف کی عدالت ثابت ہو ، پہلی شرط قیاس پر جواز عمل کے لئے ہے اور شرط ثانی قیاس پر وجوب عمل کے لئے ہے مثل شاہد کے کہ اس میں اہلیت و عدالت شرط ہے، اس میں اہلیت ہے تو اس کی گواہی پر عمل جائز ہے اور اہلیت کے ساتھ عدالت بھی ہے تو شہادت پر عمل واجب ہے، اسی طرح یہاں ہے، وصف صالح ہے تو قیاس پر عمل جائز ہے اور اگر معدن ہے تو قیاس پر عمل واجب ہے۔

مصنف ای معدن کے معنی بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ مُعدل وہ ہے جس کی عدالت ثابت ہو اور عدالت سے مراد تاثیر ہے یعنی اس وصف کی تاثیر ثابت ہو چکی ہو، پھر تاثیر چار قسم کی ہیں (۱) عین وصف کا اثر عین حکم میں ظاہر ہو جیسے سور ہرہ کا نا پاک نہ ہونا حکم ہے اور طواف علت ہے، تو بعینہ اس وصف کا اثر بعینہ اس حکم میں ظاہر ہوا، یہ پہلی قسم متفق علیہ ہے، امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک تاثیر اسی میں منحصر ہے ، باقی تین قسموں میں ان کے نزدیک تاثیر کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، (۲) عین وصف کا اثر جنس حکم میں ظاہر ہو یعنی عین وصف جنسی حکم کی علت ہو جیسے صغر ولایت مال کی علت ہے احناف و شوافع کے نزدیک اور ولایت مال کا ہم جنس ہے ولایت نکاح ، تو صفر کو ولایت نکاح کے لئے بھی علت قرار دیا یعنی عین علت کو جنسِ حکم کے لئے علت بنایا۔ (۳) جنس وصف کا اثر عین حکم میں ظاہر ہو یعنی جنس وصف کو عین حکم کی علت قرار دیں جیسے جنون اسقاط صلوۃ کے لئے علت ہے نص سے، اور اغماء جنون کا ہم جنس ہے، تو اغماء کو بھی استقاط صلوۃ کی علت بنا دیا یعنی جنسِ وصف کو عین حکم کی علت بنایا۔ (۴) جنس وصف کا اثر جنس حکم میں ظاہر ہو یعنی جنس وصف کو جنس حکم کی علت بنایا جائے جیسے مشقت سفر دور رکعت کے سقوط کی علت ہے ،نص سے، اور مشقت حیض کے ہم جنس ہے اور دور رکعت کا سقوط پوری نماز کے سقوط کے ہم جنس ہے تو اس مجانست کی وجہ سے حیض کو پوری نماز کے سقوط کے لئے علت قرار دینا درست ہے، تو یہاں جنس وصف جنس حکم کی علت بنا تو ان چاروں قسموں میں وصف کی تاثیر ظاہر ہورہی ہے۔

ونعنى بصلاح الوصف- وصف کے صالح ہونے سے یہ مراد ہے کہ وہ وصف حکم کے موافق اور مناسب ہو ، اور حکم کو اس وصف کی طرف منسوب کرنا صحیح ہو، جیسے دو کا فرمیاں بیوی میں سے ایک نے اسلام قبول کرلیا، تو دونوں میں فرقت ہو جائے گی مگر اس کا سبب کیا ؟ امام شافعی سے کہتے ہیں کہ اس کا سبب دو میں سے ایک کا اسلام ہے، اسلام کی وجہ سے فرقت ہو گئی۔ مگر احناف کہتے ہیں کہ اسلام سبب نہیں بلکہ دوسرے کا اسلام قبول کرنے سے انکار یہ سبب ہے فرقت کا، کیونکہ فرقت حکم ہے، اسلام اس کا سبب بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے، کیونکہ اسلام تو حقوق کی محافظت کے لئے آیا ہے نہ کہ فرقت کے لئے ۔

بہر حال وصف حکم کے موافق ہو یعنی وہ وصف ان علتوں کے موافق ہو جو رسول اللہ مایا یہ امن اور سلف سے منقول ہوں اگر موافق ہے تو وہ وصف صالح کہا جائے گا جیسے ولایت نکاح کی علت احناف کے نزدیک صفر ہے، اور شوافع کے نزدیک بکارت ہے ، لہذا ہمارے نزدیک صغیرہ پر ولایت ہوگی چاہے باکرہ ہو یا نشیبہ اور امام شافعی علانیہ کے نزدیک باکرہ پر ولایت ہوگی چاہیے صغیرہ ہو یا بالغہ ۔۔ ہم نے کہا کہ ولی ثیبہ صغیرہ کا جبر نکاح کرسکتا ہے، کیونکہ صغیرہ ہے، لہذا یہ باکرہ صغیرہ کے مشابہ ہوگئی ، اور باکرہ صغیرہ میں بالا تفاق ولایت ہے، لہذا ثیبہ صغیرہ پر بھی ولایت ہوگی کیونکہ علت صفر ہے، اور صغر اليسا وصف ہے جس کی طرف حکم منسوب ہو سکتا ہے، اس کی تاثیر ہے ولایت نکاح میں، اور یہ علت اس علت کے موافق ہے جس کو رسول اللہ صلی یا تم نے بیان کیا ہے ، حضور مان ہی یہ تم نے سور ہرہ کے ناپاک نہ ہونے کی علت طواف کو قرار دیا، تو اسی طرح ولایت نکاح کی علت صغر اس کے موافق ہے، کیونکہ دونوں ایک جنس کے تحت داخل ہیں ، یعنی جیسے طواف عدم نجاست کی علت ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے، کیونکہ بلی بار بار آنے جانے والی ہے اس سے بچنا مشکل ہے، اس ضرورت کی وجہ سے طواف کو علت قرار دیا ، پس اسی طرح صفر بھی ولایت کی علت بن رہا ہے ضرورت کی وجہ سے، اور وہ ضرورت اس عورت کا عاجز اور نا تجربہ کار ہونا ہے، پس یہ علت رسول اللہ لیہ السلام کی نص میں بیان کردہ علت کے موافق ہو گئی۔

ولا يصح العمل :- مصنف علا اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ وصف جامع اگر حکم کے موافق نہ ہوتو اس کو علت بنانا درست نہ ہوگا، پھر اس پر عمل نہ کیا جائے گا یعنی نہ اس کو اصل میں علت قرار دیں گے نہ اس کے ذریعہ فرع میں حکم
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi, Urdu commentary on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami.

'Food for food, equal for equal': In this [hadith], the ruling of the text is that selling food for food with excess or deficit is not permissible. And its cause ('illah) is measure (qadr) and genus (jins). But this text does not explicitly contain this cause; rather it contains an indication. That is: He said 'equal for equal', and equality does not occur without measurement. So from this, the cause is derived: measure, and 'food for food' is evidence that genus is the cause. So the cause becomes measure and genus. In short, the pillar of qiyas is that attribute (wasf) which has been designated as a sign of the ruling of the original case (asl), and this attribute is also present in the new case (far'), so that the new case is made analogous to the original in ruling, i.e., the ruling of the original is extended to the new case. From this, it is understood that qiyas has four pillars: (1) asl (the original case), (2) far' (the new case), (3) hukm (the ruling), (4) and wasf jami' (the connecting attribute). Since the connecting attribute is the fundamental pillar, the author mentioned only it. The author called the 'illah a 'sign', for which scholars used the word because the 'illahs of legal rulings are mere signs and indicators, not positive rulings; the positive rulings are truly from Allah.

'Wa huwa al-wasf al-salih': The author says that two things must be found in the attribute: (1) That the attribute is salih, i.e., it has the capacity that the ruling can be attributed to it; (2) That the attribute is mu'addal, i.e., its justice is established. The first condition is for the permissibility of acting upon qiyas, and the second condition is for the obligation of acting upon qiyas, like a witness where eligibility and justice are conditions. If he has eligibility, acting upon his testimony is permissible; if with eligibility there is also justice, acting upon his testimony is obligatory. Similarly here: if the attribute is salih, acting upon qiyas is permissible; if it is mu'addal, acting upon qiyas is obligatory.

The author explains the meaning of mu'addal: mu'addal is that whose justice is established, and by justice is meant effectiveness (ta'thir), i.e., the effectiveness of the attribute has been established. Then effectiveness is of four types: (1) The exact attribute's effect appears in the exact ruling, like the cat's saliva not being impure is the ruling, and tawaf is the cause. So exactly the effect of that attribute appears in exactly that ruling. This first type is agreed upon. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, effectiveness is confined to this; the remaining three types are not considered effective by him. (2) The exact attribute's effect appears in the genus of the ruling, i.e., the exact attribute is the cause for a genus of ruling, like minority (sighar) is the cause for guardianship of property according to Hanafis and Shafi'is, and guardianship of property is of the same genus as guardianship of marriage. So minority is also made a cause for guardianship of marriage, i.e., the exact cause is made a cause for the genus of ruling. (3) The genus of the attribute's effect appears in the exact ruling, i.e., the genus of the attribute is made the cause for the exact ruling, like insanity is the cause for dropping prayer according to text, and unconsciousness (ighma') is the same genus as insanity. So unconsciousness is also made a cause for dropping prayer, i.e., the genus of attribute is made the cause for the exact ruling. (4) The genus of attribute's effect appears in the genus of ruling, i.e., the genus of attribute is made the cause for the genus of ruling, like hardship of travel is the cause for dropping two rak'at according to text, and hardship of menstruation is of the same genus, and dropping two rak'at is of the same genus as dropping the entire prayer. So due to this similarity, making menstruation a cause for dropping the entire prayer is correct. So here the genus of attribute is made the cause for the genus of ruling. In all these four types, the effectiveness of the attribute is manifest.

'Wa na'ni bi salah al-wasf': By the attribute being salih, we mean that the attribute is suitable and appropriate for the ruling, and it is correct to attribute the ruling to that attribute. For example, two spouses, one of whom accepts Islam: then separation occurs between them. But what is its cause? It is said from Imam al-Shafi'i that its cause is one of the two accepting Islam; separation occurs because of Islam. But the Hanafis say that Islam is not the cause; rather the refusal of the other to accept Islam is the cause of separation. Because separation is a ruling, Islam does not have the capacity to be its cause, because Islam came to protect rights, not to cause separation.

Nevertheless, the attribute should be suitable for the ruling, i.e., it should conform to those causes that have been transmitted from the Messenger of Allah and the early generations. If it conforms, then that attribute is called salih. For example, the cause of guardianship of marriage according to the Hanafis is minority (sighar), and according to the Shafi'is it is virginity (bukarah). Therefore, according to us, there is guardianship over a minor girl whether she is a virgin or non-virgin, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i, there is guardianship over a virgin whether she is minor or adult. We said that a guardian can force a non-virgin minor into marriage because she is minor, so she becomes similar to a virgin minor, and in a virgin minor there is consensus on guardianship. Hence there is guardianship over a non-virgin minor as well, because the cause is minority, and minority is an attribute to which the ruling can be attributed; its effectiveness is in guardianship of marriage. And this cause conforms to the cause that the Messenger of Allah explained. The Prophet made tawaf the cause for cat's saliva not being impure; similarly, the cause of guardianship of marriage, i.e., minority, conforms to that because both fall under the same genus. Just as tawaf is the cause for the absence of impurity due to necessity, because a cat frequently comes and goes, it is difficult to avoid it; due to this necessity, tawaf was made the cause. Similarly, minority becomes the cause for guardianship due to necessity, and that necessity is the woman's helplessness and inexperience. So this cause conforms to the cause mentioned in the text of the Messenger of Allah.

'Wa la yasihhu al-'amal': The author says that if the connecting attribute is not suitable for the ruling, then making it a cause is not correct, and acting upon it will not be done, i.e., it will not be considered a cause in the original, nor will the ruling be extended through it to the new case.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the conditions and types of the 'illah (cause) in qiyas from a Hanafi usul perspective. The commentator begins by illustrating how a ruling is derived from a textual indication using the hadith 'food for food, equal for equal' — the prohibition of riba fadl in food items, where the cause (measure and genus) is not explicitly stated but derived from the requirement of equality which necessitates measurement. This establishes that the 'illah is a sign (علامت) for the ruling, not the legislator itself.

The author then introduces two essential conditions for a valid 'illah: (1) it must be salih (suitable), meaning it has the capacity to be attributed to the ruling, and (2) it must be mu'addal (just/adjudged effective), meaning its effectiveness (ta'thir) is established. The distinction is crucial: a salih attribute allows permissibility to act on qiyas, while a mu'addal attribute makes acting obligatory. This is likened to a witness: eligibility (اهلیت) makes testimony acceptable, but adding justice (عدالت) makes it binding.

The commentator then explains the four types of ta'thir (effectiveness) of the 'illah: (1) same attribute affecting same ruling (e.g., cat's saliva impurity ruling linked to cat's tawaf), agreed upon; (2) same attribute affecting genus of ruling (e.g., minority as cause for both guardianship of property and marriage); (3) genus of attribute affecting same ruling (e.g., insanity causing prayer dropping, extended to unconsciousness); (4) genus of attribute affecting genus of ruling (e.g., hardship of travel causing reduction of prayer, extended to hardship of menstruation causing full prayer dropping). Imam al-Shafi'i only accepts the first type, while Hanafis accept all four based on istihsan and broader reasoning.

Next, the attribute's suitability (صالح) is defined as being appropriate and conforming to established causes from Shariah and the Salaf. A dispute is presented regarding spouses converting to Islam: Imam al-Shafi'i says the cause of separation is Islam itself, but Hanafis argue Islam cannot be a cause for separation (which is a punitive ruling) because Islam is for preservation of rights. The Hanafi position is that the cause is the refusal of the other spouse to accept Islam.

Finally, the author gives a comparative example of guardianship in marriage: Hanafis hold minority (صغر) as the cause, Shafi'is hold virginity (بکارت). The commentator argues that even a non-virgin minor can be forced into marriage because minority is the effective cause, and it conforms to the prophetic analogy of the cat (necessity) — both involve necessity (helplessness of the minor or frequent presence of the cat). If the attribute is not suitable, acting upon it is invalid.

Key Terms
وصف صالح (wasf salih): An attribute that is suitable and appropriate for being the cause of a legal ruling, meaning it can be attributed to the ruling and conforms to established Shariah causes.
وصف معَدل (wasf mu'addal): An attribute whose effectiveness (ta'thir) is established, i.e., it has been proven to have an effect in the Shariah (by text or consensus). This makes acting on qiyas obligatory.
تاثیر (ta'thir): The effectiveness of an attribute in producing a ruling; the attribute must have a discernible effect that is acknowledged by the Shariah, either explicitly or through indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the difference between an attribute being salih and being mu'addal?
A) Salih allows qiyas; mu'addal makes qiyas obligatory.
B) Salih is for ibadah; mu'addal is for mu'amalat.
C) Salih is for Quranic rulings; mu'addal is for hadith rulings.
D) Salih is for explicit texts; mu'addal is for implicit texts.

Key Takeaway
An attribute that is both suitable (salih) and effective (mu'addal) is required for obligatory qiyas in the Hanafi school; effectiveness can be of four types, with the Hanafi school accepting all four unlike the Shafi'i school which restricts to direct correspondence.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Suitability of a Description as a Legal Cause (Salahah al-Wasf)
Explains the fourth type of effect and the definition of suitability (salahah) as a condition for a valid cause in qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define salahah and apply the condition of suitability to evaluate whether a description can serve as a cause in Hanafi qiyas, using the marital separation dispute and the guardianship example.

Core Idea
A description is suitable only if it agrees with transmitted causes and can properly be attributed to the ruling; otherwise qiyas is invalid.

In Hanafi usul, not every description that fits the ruling is acceptable as a cause. It must also be 'suitable' (salih)—meaning it is appropriate for the ruling and aligns with the causes from the Quran, Sunnah, or Salaf. This passage introduces the fourth type of effect and defines suitability, then applies it to real disputes and analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth type of effect
Recognize that making a genus of description the cause for a genus of ruling is one of the four types of effect (ta'thir). Example: hardship as the genus cause for reduction of prayer.
The text illustrates with travel and menstruation.
2
Define salahah (suitability)
A description is suitable if it is appropriate for the ruling and can be correctly attributed to it, and if it agrees with causes from the Prophet and Salaf.
The definition is explicitly given: 'و نعني بصلاح الوصف'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on marital separation
Understand why the Hanafis reject Islam as the cause for separation. Islam is for preserving rights, not separation. The cause is the other spouse's refusal, which is suitable because it leads to discord.
The text states: 'اسلام سبب نہیں بلکہ دوسرے کا اسلام قبول کرنے سے انکار'.
4
Examine the guardianship analogy
See how the Hanafis use minor age as the cause for guardianship, analogous to the cat's circling in the hadith. Both involve necessity (mashaqqa) as the basis.
The comparison: 'جیسے طواف عدم نجاست کی علت ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے'.
5
Apply the condition of agreement with transmitted causes
If a description is not in agreement with transmitted causes, it cannot be used as a cause. Action upon it is invalid.
The author says: 'ولا يصح العمل'.

جنس وصف کو جنس حکم کی علت بنایا جائے جیسے مشقت سفر دور رکعت کے سقوط کی علت ہے ،نص سے، اور مشقت حیض کے ہم جنس ہے اور دور رکعت کا سقوط پوری نماز کے سقوط کے ہم جنس ہے تو اس مجانست کی وجہ سے حیض کو پوری نماز کے سقوط کے لئے علت قرار دینا درست ہے، تو یہاں جنس وصف جنس حکم کی علت بنا تو ان چاروں قسموں میں وصف کی تاثیر ظاہر ہورہی ہے۔ ونعنى بصلاح الوصف- وصف کے صالح ہونے سے یہ مراد ہے کہ وہ وصف حکم کے موافق اور مناسب ہو ، اور حکم کو اس وصف کی طرف منسوب کرنا صحیح ہو، جیسے دو کا فرمیاں بیوی میں سے ایک نے اسلام قبول کرلیا، تو دونوں میں فرقت ہو جائے گی مگر اس کا سبب کیا ؟ امام شافعی سے کہتے ہیں کہ اس کا سبب دو میں سے ایک کا اسلام ہے، اسلام کی وجہ سے فرقت ہو گئی۔ مگر احناف کہتے ہیں کہ اسلام سبب نہیں بلکہ دوسرے کا اسلام قبول کرنے سے انکار یہ سبب ہے فرقت کا، کیونکہ فرقت حکم ہے، اسلام اس کا سبب بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے، کیونکہ اسلام تو حقوق کی محافظت کے لئے آیا ہے نہ کہ فرقت کے لئے ۔ بهر حال وصف حکم کے موافق ہو یعنی وہ وصف ان علتوں کے موافق ہو جو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور سلف سے منقول ہوں اگر موافق ہے تو وہ وصف صالح کہا جائے گا جیسے ولایت نکاح کی علت احناف کے نزدیک صغر ہے، اور شافعی کے نزدیک بکارت ہے ، لہذا ہمارے نزدیک صغیرہ پر ولایت ہوگی چاہے باکرہ ہو یا ثیبہ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک باکرہ پر ولایت ہوگی چاہے صغیرہ ہو یا بالغہ ۔۔ ہم نے کہا کہ ولی ثیبہ صغیرہ کا جبر نکاح کرسکتا ہے، کیونکہ صغیرہ ہے، لہذا یہ باکرہ صغیرہ کے مشابہ ہوگئی ، اور باکرہ صغیرہ میں بالاتفاق ولایت ہے، لہذا ثیبہ صغیرہ پر بھی ولایت ہوگی کیونکہ علت صغر ہے، اور صغر وہ وصف ہے جس کی طرف حکم منسوب ہو سکتا ہے، اس کی تاثیر ہے ولایت نکاح میں، اور یہ علت اس علت کے موافق ہے جس کو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بیان کیا ہے ، حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے سؤر الهرة کے ناپاک نہ ہونے کی علت طواف کو قرار دیا، تو اسی طرح ولایت نکاح کی علت صغر اس کے موافق ہے، کیونکہ دونوں ایک جنس کے تحت داخل ہیں ، یعنی جیسے طواف عدم نجاست کی علت ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے، کیونکہ بلی بار بار آنے جانے والی ہے اس سے بچنا مشکل ہے، اس ضرورت کی وجہ سے طواف کو علت قرار دیا ، پس اسی طرح صغر بھی ولایت کی علت بن رہا ہے ضرورت کی وجہ سے، اور وہ ضرورت اس عورت کا عاجز اور نا تجربہ کار ہونا ہے، پس یہ علت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی نص میں بیان کردہ علت کے موافق ہو گئی۔ ولا يصح العمل :- مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ وصف جامع اگر حکم کے موافق نہ ہو تو اس کو علت بنانا درست نہ ہوگا، پھر اس پر عمل نہ کیا جائے گا یعنی نہ اس کو اصل میں علت قرار دیں گے نہ اس کے ذریعہ فرع میں حکم متعدی کریں گے، کیونکہ وصف امر شرعی ہے، کیونکہ ہماری گفتگو ان علل شرعیہ سے ہیں جو مثبت حکم ہیں، لہذا وہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور سلف سے منقول علتوں کے موافق ہو، تو اس کو علت قرار دینگے۔
The genus of description is made the cause of the genus of ruling, such as the hardship of travel being the cause for the fall of two rak'ahs, from the text, and the hardship of menstruation is of the same genus as hardship, and the falling of two rak'ahs is of the same genus as the falling of the entire prayer, so due to this similarity, making menstruation the cause for the falling of the entire prayer is correct. So here the genus of description is made the cause of the genus of ruling, thus in all four types the effect of the description is apparent. And by suitability of the description we mean that the description is in agreement and appropriate for the ruling, and that attributing the ruling to that description is correct. For example, from a couple, if one accepts Islam, then separation occurs between them, but what is its cause? Imam al-Shafi'i says its cause is the Islam of one of them; due to Islam separation occurred. But the Hanafis say that Islam is not the cause, rather the other's refusal to accept Islam is the cause of separation, because separation is a ruling, and Islam is not capable of being its cause, because Islam came for the preservation of rights, not for separation. Nevertheless, the description is in agreement with the ruling, i.e., it is in agreement with the causes transmitted from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and the Salaf. If it is in agreement, then that description is called suitable. For example, the cause of guardianship in marriage according to the Hanafis is minor age, and according to al-Shafi'i it is virginity. Thus according to us, there is guardianship over a minor girl whether she is virgin or non-virgin, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i, there is guardianship over a virgin whether she is minor or adult. We said that a guardian can contract a forced marriage for a non-virgin minor because she is a minor, so she is similar to a virgin minor, and in a virgin minor there is guardianship by consensus, so there will be guardianship over a non-virgin minor as well because the cause is minor age, and minor age is a description to which the ruling can be attributed; its effect is in guardianship of marriage. And this cause is in agreement with the cause that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ stated: the Prophet ﷺ made the circling of the cat the cause for its saliva not being impure. Similarly, the cause of guardianship in marriage, minor age, is in agreement with it, because both fall under one genus. That is, just as circling is the cause for non-impurity due to necessity, because the cat comes and goes frequently and it is difficult to avoid, so due to this necessity circling was made the cause. Likewise, minor age is becoming the cause for guardianship due to necessity, and that necessity is the woman's being incapable and inexperienced. So this cause became in agreement with the cause mentioned in the text of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And the author says: 'Action is not correct' – if the comprehensive description is not in agreement with the ruling, then making it a cause is not correct, and action upon it will not be taken, meaning we will neither make it a cause in the original nor transmit the ruling to the branch through it, because the description is a sharia matter, because our discussion is about sharia causes that establish rulings. Therefore, it must be in agreement with the causes transmitted from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and the Salaf, then we will make it a cause.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth type of effect (ta'thir) in qiyas: making a genus of description the cause for a genus of ruling. It then defines salahah (suitability): a description is suitable if it is appropriate for the ruling and can be properly attributed to it. The text provides a key dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the cause of marital separation when one spouse converts to Islam. The Shafi'i position is that the very act of conversion causes separation. The Hanafi position, grounded in suitability, is that Islam cannot be the cause because it is meant to preserve rights, not sever them. Instead, the cause is the other spouse's refusal to convert. The text then illustrates suitability with the example of guardianship (wilayah) in marriage: Hanafis take minor age (sighar) as the cause, Shafi'is take virginity (bikarah). The passage then reconciles the Hanafi position by showing that minor age is a suitable cause because it is analogous to the cause stated in the hadith about the cat's saliva: necessity (hardship) justifies making the circling of the cat a cause for purity. Similarly, the necessity of the minor's incapacity justifies guardianship. Finally, the author states that if a description is not in agreement with transmitted causes, it cannot be used as a cause. This reinforces the Hanafi method of requiring suitability as a condition for accepting a cause in qiyas.

Key Terms
صلاح (salahah): Suitability of a description to be a legal cause; it must be in agreement with the ruling and with causes transmitted from the Prophet and Salaf.
تاثیر (ta'thir): The effect of a description in influencing a ruling; here classified into four types of connecting genus of description to genus of ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What example does the text use to justify that minor age is a suitable cause for guardianship?
A) The cat's saliva hadith
B) The hardship of travel
C) The conversion to Islam
D) The desire to preserve property

Key Takeaway
A description is a valid cause only if it is suitable—i.e., appropriate for the ruling and consistent with the causes found in the Revelation and the practice of the Salaf.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Condition of 'Adalah for a Valid 'Illah and Its Impact
Establishes necessity of 'adalah for 'illah and its impact on istihsan prioritization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirement of 'adalah for a valid 'illah after mulayamah and apply the criterion of effect strength to prioritize between qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
No 'illah without effect: suitability alone is insufficient until its legal effect is proven elsewhere.

In Hanafi usul, establishing a valid cause ('illah) for analogy requires more than just suitability (mulayamah). The text introduces an additional condition: 'adalah, meaning that the description's legal effect must be witnessed in another instance through nass or ijma. This lesson unpacks this condition, its rationale, and how it influences the prioritization of istihsan (hidden analogy) over explicit qiyas based on the strength of the effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for a valid 'illah
The text states that after mulayamah (suitability) is established, acting on the description is not obligatory until 'adalah is also confirmed. 'Adalah here means the effect (athar) of the description has appeared in another place via nass or ijma.
Mulayamah alone is necessary but not sufficient; 'adalah is the second condition.
2
Understand the rationale for 'adalah
The text argues that a description may be rejected by the Lawgiver despite being suitable. Its correctness is known by the appearance of its effect elsewhere, just as a witness's truthfulness is known by the effect of his religion in restraining him from sins.
The witness analogy (tamthil) clarifies that internal evidence (effect) confirms validity.
3
Examine the illustrative example: minority and guardianship
The example of 'minority' (sighr) is given: its effect in guardianship of property (wilayat al-mal) is established by ijma, which then validates using it as 'illah for guardianship in marriage.
The effect must be proven independently, not merely assumed from suitability.
4
Apply the effect criterion to istihsan vs qiyas
Because the 'illah becomes valid by its effect, the school prioritizes istihsan (hidden analogy) over explicit qiyas when its effect is strong. Conversely, explicit qiyas is given preference over istihsan when istihsan's effect is apparent but its inner rot is hidden.
The criterion is strength and correctness of effect, not mere visibility.
5
Recognize the inter-school dispute
The Hanafi position is contrasted with Imam al-Shafi'i, who accepts mere suitability (munasabah/ihalah) as sufficient for 'illah, without requiring a proven effect elsewhere.
This leads to differences in which analogies are accepted in each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ الْمُلَايَمَةُ لَمْ يَجِبْ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ إِلَّا بَعْدَ الْعَدَالَةِ عِنْدَنَا وَهِيَ الْأَثَرُ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الرَّدَّ مَعَ قِيَامِ الْمُلَايَمَةِ فَيَتَعَرَّفُ صِحَّتُهُ بِظُهُورِ أَثَرِهِ فِي مَوْضِعٍ مِنَ الْمَوَاضِعِ كَأَثَرِ الصِّغْرِ فِي وِلَايَةِ الْمَالِ وَهُوَ نَظِيرُ صِدْقِ الشَّاهِدِ يُتَعَرَّفُ بِظُهُورِ أَثَرِ دِينِهِ فِي مَنْعِهِ عَنْ تَعَاطِي مَحْظُورِ دِينِهِ وَلَمَّا صَارَتِ الْعِلَّةُ عِنْدَنَا عِلَّةً بِالْأَثَرِ قَدَّمْنَا عَلَى الْقِيَاسِ الْإِسْتِحْسَانَ الَّذِي هُوَ الْقِيَاسُ الْخَفِيُّ إِذَا قَوِيَ أَثَرُهُ وَقَدَّمْنَا الْقِيَاسَ لِصِحَّةِ أَثَرِهِ الْبَاطِنِ عَلَى الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ الَّذِي ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ وَخَفِيَ فَسَادُهُ لِأَنَّ الْعِبْرَةَ لِقُوَّةِ الْأَثَرِ وَصِحَّتِهِ دُونَ الظُّهُورِ
And when suitability is established, acting upon it is not obligatory except after 'adalah according to us, and it is the effect, because it may be rejected despite the presence of suitability. So its correctness is known by the appearance of its effect in some place, like the effect of minority in guardianship of property. And this is analogous to the truthfulness of a witness, which is known by the appearance of the effect of his religion in preventing him from engaging in what his religion prohibits. And since the 'illah according to us becomes an 'illah by (virtue of) effect, we give precedence of istihsan, which is qiyas khafi, over qiyas when its effect is strong; and we give precedence of qiyas, due to the validity of its inner effect, over istihsan whose effect has become apparent but whose invalidity is hidden, because consideration is given to the strength of the effect and its validity, not to its appearance.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi usul rule regarding the conditions for a valid 'illah (cause) in qiyas. It begins by stating the Hanafi position: when a description (wasf) is found to be suitable (mulayim) for the ruling, it is not yet binding to use it as a cause until 'adalah is established. 'Adalah here means the effect (athar) of that description has been witnessed in another instance through explicit text (nass) or consensus (ijma). Without 'adalah, the description could still be rejected by the Lawgiver despite its suitability. The correctness of the description is recognized by the appearance of its effect elsewhere. The example given is the description of 'minority' (sighr) in guardianship of property (wilayat al-mal) — it is established by ijma that a minor is unable to manage property, so guardianship is given to the guardian. This effect (inability) is then extended to guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah), proving the validity of minority as a cause. The analogy of a witness (shahid) is drawn: a witness's truthfulness is known by the effect of his religion in refraining from sins, not by mere claim. The passage then draws a methodological consequence: because the Hanafi school considers the 'illah as established through its effect, they prioritize istihsan (which is qiyas khafi, a hidden analogy) over qiyas when the effect of istihsan is strong. Conversely, they prioritize qiyas over istihsan when istihsan's effect is apparent but its underlying rot (فساد) is hidden; the criterion is the strength and correctness of the effect, not merely its visibility. This rule distinguishes Hanafi usul from the Shafi'i position, where ihalah (mere suitability) suffices without requiring a prior effect.

Key Terms
الْمُلَايَمَةُ (al-mulāyamah): Suitability or appropriateness of a description (wasf) to the ruling; it is a necessary but insufficient condition for an 'illah.
الْعَدَالَةُ (al-ʿadālah): In this context, it means the proven effect (al-athar) of the description in another instance, established by nass or ijma, confirming its validity as an 'illah.
الْأَثَرُ (al-athar): The effect or trace; here, it is synonymous with 'adalah and refers to the manifestation of the description's legal impact in a specific case.
الْإِسْتِحْسَانُ (al-istiḥsān): A method of juristic preference, defined here as qiyas khafi (hidden analogy), which may be preferred over explicit qiyas when its effect is strong.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, after establishing mulayamah (suitability) of a description, what additional condition is required for it to be a valid 'illah?
A) Ihalah (mere suitability)
B) 'Adalah (effect proven by nass or ijma in another instance)
C) Qiyas khafi (hidden analogy)
D) Ijma of the companions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a valid 'illah requires both mulayamah (suitability) and 'adalah (effect proven elsewhere); the latter determines priority between qiyas and istihsan.

The Requirement of 'Adala for the 'Illa in Qiyas
Explaining the 'adala condition for 'illa in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of 'adala for an 'illa and apply it to determine whether an attribute can serve as the 'illa in a given qiyas.

Core Idea
An 'illa is valid only if its effect has already been manifested in another case by nass or ijma.

This passage introduces a key condition for the validity of an 'illa (causal attribute) in qiyas according to the Hanafi school: 'adala. It contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who does not require prior manifestation. The Hanafi view is supported by an analogy to witness testimony and illustrated with the example of minority (sighar) as the 'illa for guardianship in marriage. Understanding this condition is essential for properly extending rulings to new cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Find the two opposing views on whether an 'illa requires prior manifestation of its effect. The Hanafi position mandates 'adala; the Shafi'i view does not.
2
Understand the Hanafi evidence from analogy
Examine the analogy to a witness: just as a witness needs both capacity (ahliyya) and integrity ('adala), an 'illa needs both suitability (muwafaqa) and proven effectiveness ('adala). Without 'adala, the attribute may be rejected.
3
Analyze the example of minority
Follow how the text uses ijma to establish that minority is the 'illa for guardianship over property. Then it extends this to guardianship over the person (marriage) because the effect (incapacity) is manifest in both cases.
This demonstrates how 'adala is established: the effect appeared in one ruling (property) by ijma, so minority becomes a valid 'illa for a similar ruling.
4
Apply the condition to a hypothetical
Consider a new attribute not yet proven effective by nass or ijma. According to Hanafi usul, it cannot be used as an 'illa. Contrast with the Shafi'i view where it could be used if the mujtahid is convinced.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علیہ میں علت کا تعین کر دینا، مجتہد کے دل میں کسی چیز کے علت ہونے کا خیال پیدا ہو جانا اس کے علت بننے کے لئے کافی ہے، عدالت شرط نہیں ہے یعنی امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ اس علت کا اثر کسی اور جگہ ظاہر ہو چکا ہو اور ہمارے نزدیک موافقت کے بعد عدالت بھی ضروری ہے، یعنی اس علت کا اثر کسی اور جگہ ظاہر ہو چکا ہو، بغیر عدالت کے وصف پر عمل واجب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ موافقت کے پائے جانے کے باوجود وہ وصف شارع کی طرف سے مردود ہونے کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے گواہ اس میں دو چیزیں ضروری ہیں (۱) اہلیت وصلاحیت (۲) عدالت (دیانت)، گواہ میں پہلی شرط ہے اہلیت و صلاحیت یعنی عاقل، بالغ، آزاد وغیرہ، اور عدالت نہیں ہے تو قاضی اس کی گواہی کو رد کر سکتا ہے، کیونکہ عدالت نہیں ہے وہ فاسق ہے۔ لہذا قبل العدالۃ وصف جامع میں عمل واجب نہیں ہے۔ فيتعرف صحته - وصف میں عدالت کا پتہ اس طرح چلے گا کہ نص یا اجتماع سے اس وصف کا اثر کسی اور جگہ بھی ظاہر ہوا ہے، تو اس وصف میں عدالت ثابت ہو جائے گی، لہذا عمل واجب ہوگا جیسے مال کی ولایت میں صغر کا اثر ہے یعنی صغر کی وجہ سے مالی تصرف کا حق شریعت نے ولی کو دیدیا، کیونکہ بچہ بوجہ صغر مالی تصرف سے عاجز ہے، اس لئے ولی کو حق تصرف اور حق ولایت شریعت نے دیا یہ مسئلہ اجماع سے ثابت ہے، اور صغر کی وجہ سے جیسے مالی تصرف سے عجز ہے ایسے ہی صغیر اپنے نفس میں تصرف سے بھی عاجز ہے، لہذا اس علت صغر کی وجہ سے ولایت فی النفس یعنی ولایت نکاح بھی ثابت ہو جائے گی، پس ولایت نکاح کے لئے ہم نے صغر کو علت بنایا کیونکہ یہ ایسی علت ہے جس کا اثر اور جگہ ظاہر ہو چکا ہے، چونکہ اجماع سے اس کا ولایت مال میں علت ہونا ثابت ہو چکا ہے۔ وهو نظير صدق الشاهد - وصف کی صحت معلوم ہوگی اس کے اثر کے ظاہر ہونے سے، اس کی نظیر یہ ہے جیسے گواہ، اس کی اہلیت ثابت ہونے کے بعد اس کا صدق و عدل اس کے دینی اثر کے ظاہر ہونے سے معلوم ہوگا، اس طرح کہ وہ معاصی اور کبائر سے بچتا ہے، اب اس کی شہادت قبول کرنا واجب ہے، اسی طرح وصف کے لئے حکم کی علت بننے میں اس کی صلاحیت ثابت ہونے کے بعد اس کی عدالت تاثیر سے معلوم ہوگی یعنی اس کا اثر کسی جگہ میں نص اور اجماع سے ظاہر ہو چکا ہو، پھر وصف پر عمل واجب ہوگا یعنی اس کو حکم کی علت بنایا جائے گا۔
Determining the 'illa: It is sufficient for a mujtahid that the idea of something being the 'illa occurs in his heart; 'adala (validity) is not a condition, i.e., according to Imam al-Shafi'i it is not necessary that the effect of this 'illa has appeared elsewhere. But according to us, after muwafaqa (agreement with the ruling), 'adala is also necessary, i.e., the effect of this 'illa must have appeared elsewhere. Without 'adala, acting upon the attribute is not obligatory, because despite the presence of muwafaqa, that attribute may be rejected by the Lawgiver. Its example is like a witness: two things are necessary: (1) ahliyya wa salāḥiyya (capacity and suitability), (2) 'adāla (integrity). In a witness, the first condition is ahliyya wa salāḥiyya, i.e., sane, adult, free, etc. If 'adāla is not present, the judge may reject his testimony because he is a fāsiq. Therefore, before 'adāla, acting upon a comprehensive attribute is not obligatory. The recognition of its validity: The 'adāla of an attribute is known by the fact that the effect of that attribute has appeared elsewhere by nass or ijma. Then 'adāla is established for that attribute, so acting is obligatory. For example, in guardianship over property, the effect of minority (sighar) is that the right of financial disposal is given by the Shari'ah to the guardian, because the child, due to minority, is incapable of financial disposal. Therefore, the Shari'ah gave the right of disposal and guardianship to the guardian; this issue is established by ijma. And just as there is incapacity in financial disposal due to minority, similarly the minor is incapable of disposal over his own person. Therefore, due to this 'illa of minority, guardianship over the person (wilayat al-nafs), i.e., guardianship in marriage, is also established. So for guardianship in marriage, we made minority the 'illa because this 'illa's effect has appeared elsewhere, and it has been established by ijma that it is the 'illa in guardianship over property. And it is analogous to the truthfulness of a witness: the validity of an attribute is known by the appearance of its effect. Its analogy is like a witness: after his capacity is established, his truthfulness and integrity are known by the appearance of his religious effect, i.e., he avoids sins and major sins, so accepting his testimony is obligatory. Similarly, for an attribute to be the 'illa of a ruling, after its suitability is established, its 'adāla is known by its effectiveness, i.e., its effect has appeared somewhere by nass and ijma. Then acting upon the attribute is obligatory, i.e., it is made the 'illa of the ruling.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage explains a key condition for the validity of an 'illa (causal attribute) in qiyas according to the Hanafi school. The condition is 'adala: the 'illa must have already produced its effect in another case, established by explicit text (nass) or consensus (ijma). The passage begins by contrasting the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who does not require prior manifestation. The author then illustrates with the example of a witness: just as a witness needs both legal capacity (ahliyya) and integrity ('adala), an 'illa needs both suitability (as a plausible attribute) and proven effectiveness. The proof of effectiveness is that the attribute has been recognized as effective in another ruling by nass or ijma. The example of guardianship (wilaya) over property due to minority (sighar) is given: it is established by ijma that minority is the 'illa for guardianship over property. Therefore, by extension, minority is also the 'illa for guardianship over the person (marriage guardianship), because the effect (incapacity) is present in both. This demonstrates how 'adala is established. The passage concludes by comparing this to how a witness's truthfulness is known by his religious conduct: avoidance of sins confirms his integrity, making his testimony acceptable. Similarly, an attribute's 'adala is confirmed by its effective impact in another ruling.

Key Terms
عدالت ('adāla): The condition that an 'illa has already produced its effect in another case, established by nass or ijma.
علت ('illa): The cause or attribute that is the basis for extending a ruling in qiyas.
موافقت (muwāfaqa): The agreement of the 'illa with the ruling in the original case (asl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for an 'illa to be valid besides muwafaqa?
A) It must be mentioned explicitly in the Quran.
B) It must have been used by a companion.
C) It must have its effect manifested elsewhere by nass or ijma.
D) It must be agreed upon by all mujtahids.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that an 'illa's effectiveness be proven by its prior manifestation in another case through nass or ijma, ensuring that qiyas is grounded in established Shari'ah recognition.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Istihsan and Takhsis al-Illah: The Hanafi Rebuttal
Refuting that istihsan constitutes takhsis al-illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school argues that istihsan does not constitute takhsis al-illah and evaluate the opposing view using the example of the forgetful fasting person.

Core Idea
Istihsan removes the cause itself; it does not just block its effect.

This passage tackles a critical usul al-fiqh dispute: is istihsan a form of takhsis al-illah (specification of the cause)? The author, a Hanafi commentator, firmly answers no. He argues that when stronger evidence (nass, ijma', necessity, or a stronger qiyas) contradicts an apparent analogy, the weaker analogy's cause does not simply become blocked; it ceases to exist. This distinction is fundamental to Hanafi legal theory and has practical consequences, as illustrated by the case of a forgetful fasting person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the majority Hanafi view that takhsis al-illah is invalid. Then state the opposing view (some Hanafis, Mu'tazila, Malik, Ahmad) that a cause can exist without its ruling due to a preventer.
The objector claims istihsan is an example of takhsis.
2
Understand the objector's claim
The objector argues that when istihsan (hidden analogy) opposes qiyas jali (obvious analogy), you leave the qiyas jali, so its cause is present but blocked by istihsan — that is takhsis al-illah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the cause of the weak qiyas does not remain because the condition for its validity (not conflicting with stronger evidence) is missing. The stronger evidence (nass, ijma', necessity, or stronger qiyas) negates the cause itself, not merely its effect.
Key: for Hanafis, a cause must be effective; if blocked, it was never a true cause.
4
Apply the forgetful fasting person example
A fasting person who forgetfully eats: apparent cause is consumption, but the fast remains valid. Those who accept takhsis say the cause exists but is overridden by the hadith. Hanafis say the act is attributed to the Lawgiver, so it is not a legal consumption — the cause is absent.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis rule the fast valid; those who allow takhsis rule it invalid. This shows the importance of the theoretical debate.

گیا، کیونکہ روزہ کا رکن (امساک) فوت گیا، اس پر اعتراض ہو گا ناسی کا کہ بھول کر اگر
The ruling of this ta'lil is prevented there due to a preventer, which is the athar. And we said: The ruling is absent due to the absence of this cause, because the act of the forgetful person is attributed to the Lawgiver, so the meaning of offense is dropped from him, and the act becomes pardoned. Thus the fast remains due to the remaining of its pillar, not due to a preventer with the loss of its pillar. So what they made a proof of specification, we made it a proof of absence. And this is the foundation of this chapter, so memorize it and master it, for in it is much fiqh and great relief. Translation: Then istihsan is not from the category of takhsis al-illal, because the description is not made a cause in the face of nass, ijma', and necessity. Because necessity has ijma', and ijma' is like the Book and Sunnah. Similarly, when istihsan opposes qiyas jali, istihsan necessitates the absence of qiyas. Thus the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause, not due to a preventer despite the cause being established. And similarly we say in all effective causes. And its explanation is in our statement about the fasting person: when water is poured into his throat, his fast becomes invalid due to the loss of the pillar of fasting, and the forgetful person's objection arises. Then those who permit takhsis al-illal said that the ruling of this ta'lil is prevented due to a preventer, which is the hadith. And we said that the ruling is absent due to the absence of this cause, because the act of the forgetful person is attributed to the Lawgiver, so the meaning of offense is dropped from him, and the act is pardoned. Thus the fast remains due to the remaining of its pillar, not due to a preventer despite the loss of its pillar. So what they made a proof of specification, we made it a proof of absence. And this (making the proof of specification into a proof of absence) is the foundation of this chapter. So memorize it and master it, for in it is much fiqh and great relief. Explanation: The author (may Allah bless him) is raising a disputatious issue, whose title is takhsis al-illah, i.e., the departure of the ruling from the cause. Can it happen that a cause is present but the ruling is not found due to a preventer? Some Hanafi mashayikh, most Mutazila, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad believe in it. They say: Legal causes are signs for rulings, like a cloud is a sign of rain. So just as it is possible that a cloud exists but rain does not, similarly it is possible that a cause is present but due to a preventer the ruling is not found. The majority of Hanafis do not permit takhsis. They say: The departure of the ruling without a preventer is obviously invalid; even with a preventer it is invalid, because legal causes are proofs and signs of rulings. Therefore, wherever the cause is, it will establish the ruling and be its proof. If the ruling departs from the cause, there would be contradiction: the cause requires the ruling to be established, while the departure requires it not to be established, and both cannot happen together. This is called contradiction. So it is established that even with a preventer, departure is invalid. The objector says: You leave qiyas jali due to istihsan (qiyas khafi). This is takhsis al-illah, because qiyas jali is present and you leave it, acting on istihsan. Thus the cause in qiyas jali is left due to a preventer (istihsan coming in opposition). This is called takhsis al-illah. The author answers that istihsan is not from the category of takhsis al-illal, i.e., it is not that due to istihsan, specification occurred in qiyas jali. Because when nass, ijma', or necessity comes in opposition to the qiyas, the cause of the qiyas does not remain, because for the validity of qiyas, a condition is that it not be in opposition to nass. When nass opposes, the qiyas is not valid, so its cause does not remain. And nass, ijma', and necessity are all of the same rank because necessity is at the rank of ijma', and ijma' is like the Book and Sunnah. Therefore, just as qiyas is not valid in opposition to nass, similarly it is not valid in opposition to ijma' and necessity, so its cause does not remain, thus the objection of takhsis al-illah does not arise. The objector says: I understand your point regarding these three things: qiyas does not remain in opposition to nass, ijma', and necessity. But if istihsan comes in opposition to qiyas jali, here you would have to accept takhsis al-illah, because here two qiyases conflict. The author clarifies this in the next phrase: "Wa kadha idha aradahu" - Similarly, when istihsan opposes qiyas jali, the non-existence of qiyas jali is established, meaning qiyas jali does not remain, because istihsan (qiyas khafi) is stronger in effect, so it is given preference, and in its opposition qiyas jali does not remain, nor does its cause remain. Thus the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause, not that we say the cause remains but due to a preventer the ruling is not found. The conclusion is that istihsan is not from the category of takhsis al-illah in any respect. Sahib al-Husami says: What we said about istihsan and qiyas - that the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause - we say the same about all effective causes: wherever there is departure of the ruling, it is due to the absence of the cause. And its explanation: He is presenting an example for the aforementioned dispute: If water is forcibly poured into the throat of a fasting person, his fast is broken because the pillar of fasting (abstention) is lost. An objection arises from the forgetful person: if he (forgets and eats)...
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul al-fiqh dispute regarding takhsis al-illah (specification of the effective cause) and its relationship with istihsan. The author, a Hanafi commentator on Al-Husami, refutes the claim that istihsan constitutes a form of takhsis al-illah. The central argument is that when istihsan (hidden analogy) contradicts qiyas jali (obvious analogy), the qiyas jali's cause is not merely overridden by a preventer; rather, the cause itself ceases to exist because the condition for the validity of the qiyas (that it not be opposed by stronger evidence) is violated. Thus, the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause, not due to a preventer with the cause present. This is a key Hanafi position distinguishing their methodology from those who permit takhsis al-illah (such as some Hanafi scholars, Mu'tazila, Malik, Ahmad). The author provides a concrete example: a fasting person who has water forcibly poured down his throat. The apparent cause (introduction of water into the throat) would normally invalidate the fast, but if the person is forgetful (nasi), the fast remains valid according to the Hanafi view. Those who allow takhsis al-illah argue that the cause (drinking) is present but the ruling (invalidity) is prevented by the hadith excusing forgetfulness. The Hanafis respond that the act of the forgetful person is attributed to the Lawgiver (i.e., it is excused), so the act ceases to be a 'drinking' in the legal sense; thus the cause is absent, and the fast remains due to the remaining pillar. The author emphasizes that this principle—that departure of a ruling is always due to absence of cause, not a preventer—is the foundation of this chapter and contains much fiqh and great relief for solving legal problems.

Key Terms
تخصیص علت (takhsis al-illah): The occurrence of the cause (illa) without its ruling (hukm) due to a preventer (mani').
استحسان (istihsan): Preferring a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) over an obvious analogy (qiyas jali) due to a stronger evidence or necessity.
علة (illa): The effective cause or ratio legis in qiyas, which is a descriptive attribute connected to the ruling by divine law.
مانع (mani'): A preventer that blocks the effect of the cause while the cause itself remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view in this passage, when istihsan opposes qiyas jali, why is the ruling of qiyas jali absent?
A) Because the cause of qiyas jali is present but overridden by a preventer (istihsan).
B) Because the cause of qiyas jali ceases to exist due to the stronger effect of istihsan.
C) Because qiyas jali is invalid in all cases where istihsan exists.
D) Because the ruling of qiyas jali is excused for the sake of necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that a ruling's absence is always due to the absence of its cause (not a preventer) is fundamental to preserving the coherence of qiyas and refuting claims that istihsan involves takhsis al-illah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Necessity of Ta'diyah (Transitivity) in Qiyas
Stating the Hanafi position that qiyas requires the cause to be transitive, contra al-Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ta'diyah, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi response to evaluate the practical difference.

Core Idea
A cause without transitivity is legally useless: it neither yields certain knowledge nor obligates action beyond the text.

In this passage, the author establishes that the ruling (hukm) of qiyas is transitivity - transferring the ruling from the original case to new cases where no text exists. The Hanafi position insists that causal reasoning (ta'lil) necessarily requires transitivity; otherwise it serves no legal purpose. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, validates ta'lil even without transitivity, arguing that it can still specify the original ruling. We will dissect both arguments and see why the Hanafis consider transitivity essential.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on ta'diyah
Identify what the text says: 'ta'diyah is a necessary ruling for ta'lil according to us.' Understand that for Hanafis, the very purpose of ta'lil is to extend the ruling to new cases.
The Urdu explanation clarifies that qiyas operates on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), not certainty.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i permits ta'lil without transitivity, even using an attribute like 'eightness.' His reasoning: ta'lil is a legal proof, so it must obligate action (ijab) just like other proofs. The indication that a description is a cause does not require transitivity; transitivity is an additional meaning.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: a legal proof must necessitate knowledge or action. A non-transitive cause does not give certain knowledge (by consensus), nor does it obligate action in the textually prescribed case because the text itself already does. Therefore, the only remaining benefit is transitivity.
The text argues: 'text is above ta'lil' - so cutting the ruling from the text is invalid.
4
Respond to the Shafi'i specification argument
The Shafi'i might say that a non-transitive cause specifies the ruling for the original case. The Hanafi response: specification is achieved simply by not performing ta'lil. Moreover, a non-transitive cause does not prevent using a transitive one, so this benefit is illusory.
This is the decisive refutation presented in the text.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference: Hanafis require the cause in qiyas to be transitive; Shafi'is allow non-transitive causes. For example, if the cause for prohibiting wine is 'intoxication', a Hanafi would extend it to all intoxicants, while a Shafi'i might restrict it to wine alone if the cause is considered non-transitive.
The text mentions 'eightness' as an example of a non-transitive attribute.

Source Text

ترجمہ: اور بہر حال قیاس کا حکم پس نص کے حکم کو متعدی کرنا ہے اس فرع کی طرف جس میں نص نہ ہو ، تا کہ اس میں احتمال خطا کے ساتھ غالب رائے سے حکم ثابت ہو جائے ، پس ہمارے نزدیک تعدیہ تعلیل کے لئے ایک لازمی حکم ہے، امام شافعی کے نزدیک تعلیل صحیح ہے بغیر تعدیہ کے، یہاں تک کہ انہوں نے خمینیت کے ساتھ تعلیل کو جائز قرار دیا ہے، اور اس بات سے استدلال کیا ہے کہ یہ تعلیل جب دلائلِ شرعیہ کی جنس سے ہے تو واجب ہے کہ اس تعلیل کے ساتھ حکم کا اثبات متعلق ہو، جیسا کہ تمام دلائل شرعیہ، کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ وصف کے علت ہونے کی دلیل اس کے متعدی ہونے کا تقاضا نہیں کرتی ہے ، بلکہ تعدیہ وصف میں ایک معنی کی وجہ سے پہچانا جائے گا ، اور ہمارے قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دلیل شرعی کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ علم یا عمل کو واجب کرے ، اور یہ تعلیل علم یقینی کو واجب نہیں کرتی بغیر اختلاف کے، اور نہ یہ منصوص علیہ میں عمل کو واجب کرتی ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ ( وجوب عمل ) نص سے ثابت ہے، اور نص تعلیل سے بڑھ کر ہے تو وجوب حکم کو نص سے منقطع کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا، پس تعلیل کے لئے تعدیہ کے علاوہ کوئی حکم باقی نہیں رہا، پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ تعلیل ایسی علت کے ساتھ جو متعدی نہیں ہے نص کے ساتھ حکم نص کو خاص کرنے کا فائدہ دیتی ہے، تو ہم جواب دیں گے کہ یہ اختصاص ترک تعلیل سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے، علاوہ اس بات کے تعلیل ایسی علت کے ساتھ جو متعدی نہیں ہے، نہیں روکتی ہے تعلیل کو ایسی علت کے ساتھ جو متعدی ہے، پس یہ فائدہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح:- مصنف سے قیاس کا حکم بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ قیاس کا حکم تعدیہ ہے یعنی اس کا حکم ایسی فرع کی طرف متعدی کرنا جس میں نص یا اجماع وغیرہ ایسی کوئی دلیل نہ ہو جو قیاس سے بڑھ کر ہو، کیونکہ قیاس کی شرطوں میں ہے کہ اس کے مقابل میں کوئی قومی دلیل نہ ہو، پھر اصل سے فرع کی طرف جو حکم متعدی ہوگا وہ غالب رائے سے ہوگا ، غالب رائے اس لئے کہا کہ قیاس اولیۂ ظنیہ میں سے ہے قطعیہ میں سے نہیں ہے، اگر چہ قیاس پر عمل قطعی ویقینی طور پر واجب
(Fayd Subhani) And as for its ruling, it is the transference of the ruling of the text to that which has no text, so that it may be established in it by predominant opinion with the possibility of error. Thus transitivity is a necessary ruling for ta'lil according to us. And according to al-Shafi'i, ta'lil is valid without transitivity, to the extent that he permitted ta'lil with 'eightness'. He argued that since this ta'lil is of the genus of legal proofs, it is necessary that obligation be attached to it like all other proofs. Do you not see that the indication of a description being a cause does not necessitate its transitivity; rather, that is known by a meaning in the description. And the proof of our statement is that a legal proof must necessarily necessitate knowledge or action. And this ta'lil does not necessitate certain knowledge, without disagreement, nor does it necessitate action in the textually prescribed case, because that (obligation of action) is established by the text, and the text is above ta'lil; so separating it from the text is not valid. Thus no ruling remains for ta'lil except transitivity. If it is said: 'Ta'lil with a non-transitive cause benefits the specification of the ruling of the text to it,' we reply: This specification is achieved by abandoning ta'lil. Moreover, ta'lil with a non-transitive cause does not prevent ta'lil with a transitive cause; thus this benefit is invalid.
Translation: And in any case, the ruling of qiyas is to transfer the ruling of the text to the branch in which there is no text, so that the ruling may be established in it by predominant opinion with the possibility of error. So according to us, transitivity is a necessary ruling for ta'lil. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, ta'lil is valid without transitivity; even he permitted ta'lil with 'eightness'. He argued that since this ta'lil is of the genus of legal proofs, it is necessary that the affirmation of the ruling be attached to it, like all legal proofs. Do you not see that the indication of a description being a cause does not require its transitivity; rather, transitivity is known by a meaning in the description. The proof of our statement is that a legal proof must necessarily cause knowledge or action. And this ta'lil does not cause certain knowledge, without disagreement, nor does it cause action in the textually prescribed case, because that (obligation of action) is established by the text, and the text is superior to ta'lil; so it is not valid to separate the obligation of the ruling from the text. Thus no ruling remains for ta'lil except transitivity. If it is objected that ta'lil with a non-transitive cause benefits the specification of the ruling of the text to that case, we reply: This specification is achieved by abandoning ta'lil. Moreover, ta'lil with a non-transitive cause does not prevent ta'lil with a transitive cause; thus this benefit is invalid.
Explanation: The author is stating the ruling of qiyas: that the ruling of qiyas is transitivity, i.e., to transfer its ruling to a branch in which there is no text or consensus or any other proof that is stronger than qiyas, because among the conditions of qiyas is that no stronger proof opposes it. Then the ruling transferred from the original to the branch will be by predominant opinion. He said 'predominant opinion' because qiyas is among presumptive evidences, not definitive, although acting upon qiyas is definitively and certainly obligatory.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between Hanafis and the Shafi'i school regarding the nature of ta'lil (causal reasoning) in qiyas. The Hanafi position, as stated, holds that ta'lil necessarily requires transitivity (ta'diyah)—meaning the cause must be applicable to new cases beyond the original text. Without transitivity, ta'lil serves no judicial purpose because it does not produce new knowledge (since it is not certain) nor does it mandate action in the textually prescribed case (since the text already does that). Imam al-Shafi'i, by contrast, allows ta'lil even with a non-transitive cause, arguing that any legal proof must obligate action; ta'lil, being a proof, obligates action regarding the textually prescribed case itself, thereby specifying it. The Hanafi response, as presented, refutes this: specification is already achieved by simply not performing ta'lil; a non-transitive cause does not prevent using a transitive one, so it offers no unique benefit. The Arabic text, with its Urdu translation and explanation (tashrih), concludes that qiyas's ruling is transitivity, and this is a necessary characteristic for the cause. All examples and reasoning are within the Hanafi usul framework.

Key Terms
تعدیۃ (ta'diyah): The transitivity of the cause to new cases beyond the original text.
تعلیل (ta'lil): The act of using a cause (illa) to explain or extend a ruling.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, why is transitivity necessary for ta'lil?
A) Because ta'lil produces certain knowledge about new cases.
B) Because without transitivity, ta'lil does not obligate certain knowledge or action in the textually prescribed case, so it would be useless.
C) Because Imam al-Shafi'i required it.
D) Because the text explicitly states that all causes must be transitive.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is valid only if the cause is transitive; a non-transitive cause offers no legal benefit.

Why Qiyas Requires a Transitive 'Illah
Hanafi argument against non-transitive 'illah in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires transitivity ('illah muta'addiyah) for valid qiyas and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Without transitivity, ta'lil is futile — a cause that applies only to the original case serves no legal purpose.

In this passage, the author defends the Hanafi requirement that causal reasoning (ta'lil) in qiyas must extend the ruling to new cases. You will see why Hanafis argue that a non-transitive 'illah (qasirah) is legally useless, and how the Shafi'i school differs. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish valid from invalid qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structural claim
Read the first sentence: 'A legal proof must necessitate knowledge or action.' This is the premise. Then see how the author applies it to ta'lil: this ta'lil (non-transitive) produces neither, so its only remaining function is ta'diyah.
The premise is a principle of usul: proofs yield either ilm (certain knowledge) or amal (obligation to act).
2
Trace the Hanafi proof
Follow the argument: Non-transitive ta'lil does not yield ilm (it is zanni) nor does it necessitate action (the text already obligates). Therefore it is futile (abath) unless it provides ta'diyah.
The text asserts that the text (nass) is above (higher authority than) ta'lil, so ta'lil cannot add obligation.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i claim: ta'lil with a non-transitive 'illah benefits by specifying the ruling to the original case. Identify this claim in the text: 'if it is said: ta'lil with what does not extend yields the benefit of specifying the ruling of the text to it'.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi responds with two points: (1) specification is already achieved by simply not performing ta'lil; (2) a non-transitive ta'lil does not prevent a transitive one, so the claimed benefit is null.
The rebuttal undermines the Shafi'i justification by showing it is either redundant or ineffective.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply this to a real case: riba in gold and silver (nuqud). Hanafis require the 'illah (thamaniyyah) to be transitive to other currencies; Shafi'is may confine it. Thus, the ruling on riba in modern fiat money differs.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: same 'illah, different scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قُوْلِنَا أَنَّ دَلِيْلَ الشَّرْعِ لَابُدَانْ يُؤْجِبَ عِلْماً أَوْعَمَلًا وَهَذَا لَا يُؤْجِبْ عِلْمًا بِلَا خِلَافٍ وَلَا يُوجِبْ عَمَلًا فِى الْمَنْصُوصِ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّهُ ثَابِتُ بِالنَّضِ وَالنَّص فَوْقَ التَّعْلِيْلِ فَلَا يَصِحُ قَطْعُهُ عَنْهُ فَلَمْ يَبْقَ لِلتَّعْلِيلِ حُكْمُ سِوَى التَّعْدِيَةِ فَإِنْ قِيْلَ التَّعْلِيلُ بِمَا لَا يَتَعَدَّى يُفِيْدُ اِخْتَصَاصَ حُكْم النَّضِ بِهِ قُلْنَا هَذَا يَحْصُلُ بِتَرْكِ التَّعْلِيلِ عَلَى أَنَّ التَّعْلِيْلَ بِمَالَا يَتَعَدَّى لَا يَمْنَعُ التَّعْلِيْلَ بِمَا يَتَعَدَّى فَتَبْطُلُ هَذِهِ الْفَائِدَةُ
Our statement: That a legal proof must necessarily necessitate knowledge or action. And this (ta'lil) does not necessitate knowledge without dispute, nor does it necessitate action concerning the textually specified (mansus 'alayh) because that (the obligation of action) is established by the text, and the text is above ta'lil. So it is not valid to separate it from the text. Therefore, no ruling remains for ta'lil except transitivity (ta'diyah). If it is said: Ta'lil with what does not extend yields the benefit of specifying the ruling of the text to it, we say: This is achieved by abandoning ta'lil. Moreover, ta'lil with what does not extend does not prevent ta'lil with what extends. So this benefit becomes null.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools concerning the nature of qiyas and ta'lil (causal reasoning). The Hanafi position, as stated, is that the sole legitimate function of ta'lil is transitivity (ta'diyah)—extending the ruling from the original case (asl) to a new case (far') where no explicit text exists. Without ta'diyah, ta'lil is invalid. The Shafi'i school, represented by Imam al-Shafi'i, holds that ta'lil is valid even with a non-transitive 'illah (qasirah), as seen in their treatment of riba in gold and silver (nuqud) where the 'illah of thamaniyyah (currency medium) is confined to those items. The Hanafi proof is rational: a shar'i proof must either produce certain knowledge (ilm) or necessitate action (amal). This ta'lil produces neither—it does not produce ilm because it is zanni, and it does not necessitate action because the obligation of action is already established by the text, which is superior. Thus, without ta'diyah, the ta'lil would be futile (abath). The Shafi'i counterargument that ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah benefits by specifying the ruling to the text is rejected by the Hanafis on two grounds: first, that specification is already achieved by simply not performing ta'lil; second, such ta'lil does not preclude a transitive ta'lil, nullifying that claimed benefit. The commentary clarifies that Hanafis treat ta'lil and qiyas as synonymous, whereas Shafi'is consider ta'lil a broader category that includes qiyas with transitive 'illah.

Key Terms
تعليل (ta'lil): Establishing a cause ('illah) for a legal ruling; for Hanafis, it is synonymous with qiyas and requires ta'diyah.
تعدية (ta'diyah): Extending the ruling from the original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on shared 'illah.
علة قاصرة ('illah qasirah): A non-transitive cause that is confined to the original case and does not apply to other cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sole remaining function of ta'lil when it does not produce certain knowledge or necessitate action?
A) To specify the ruling to the original case
B) To extend the ruling to new cases (ta'diyah)
C) To confirm the text
D) To provide a rational explanation

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, the sole valid function of ta'lil is transitivity (ta'diyah); without it, causal reasoning has no legal force.

Ta'diyah in Ta'lil: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Usul dispute: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on ta'diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the Hanafi requirement of ta'diyah in ta'lil, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of 'illah qasirah.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, ta'lil without ta'diyah is futile — the only benefit of a cause is transitivity.

This lesson presents a foundational dispute in Usul al-Fiqh: does legal causation (ta'lil) require the ruling to extend to other cases? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ sharply on this point, with the Hanafis insisting that a non-transitive cause ('illah qasirah) is invalid. The debate centers on whether ta'lil can have any benefit without transitivity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Hanafis equate ta'lil with qiyas and require ta'diyah (transitivity) for validity. Without it, the ta'lil is invalid.
Hanafis: ta'lil = qiyas; both require transitivity.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Recognize that Shafi'is distinguish between ta'lil and qiyas: ta'lil is broader and can be based on a non-transitive 'illah (qasirah). They do not require ta'diyah for ta'lil.
Shafi'is accept 'illah qasirah as valid for ta'lil.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the Hanafi argument: a shar'i proof must produce either certain knowledge (yaqin) or obligatory action (wajib). Ta'lil is zanni and the obligation comes from the text anyway, so its only benefit is transitivity. Without ta'diyah, ta'lil is futile (abath).
Key: 'ta'lil does not produce certainty or obligation; only transitivity gives it benefit.'
4
Analyze the Shafi'i response
The Shafi'is argue that other shar'i proofs can be particular without transitivity, so ta'lil can also be particular. The validity of an 'illah depends on its intrinsic suitability (muwafaqah and 'adalah), not on ta'diyah.
Shafi'is see ta'diyah as an additional feature, not a condition.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis counter that the text already shows the ruling is specific to the original case, so a non-transitive ta'lil adds nothing. Moreover, if a transitive 'illah exists alongside a non-transitive one, the mujtahid would use the transitive one, nullifying any benefit of the non-transitive one. Thus ta'diyah is necessary.
Practical consequence: in riba, Hanafis use 'illah of value and genus (transitive), while Shafi'is use dain (gold/silver, non-transitive).

Al-Faiz al-Hijazi. Commentary in Urdu of Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. ... (then the Urdu text explaining the dispute). Finally: 'Therefore, ta'diyah is necessary for ta'lil.'
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on ta'lil (causation in legal reasoning) and its dispute with the Shafi'i school. The Hanafis hold that ta'lil (which they equate with qiyas) requires ta'diyah—the transitivity of the ruling from the original case to the branch. Without ta'diyah, the ta'lil is invalid. The Shafi'is, however, distinguish between ta'lil and qiyas: ta'lil is broader and can be based on a 'illah qasirah (a non-transitive cause) that only applies to the original case. They argue that legal proofs can be particular, so ta'diyah is not a condition. The Hanafis counter that a shar'i proof must yield either certain knowledge or obligatory action; ta'lil does neither, so its only benefit is transitivity. An objection that even a non-transitive ta'lil shows the ruling is specific to the text is refuted: the text itself already indicates that. Thus ta'diyah alone justifies ta'lil.

Key Terms
تعلیل (ta'lil): The act of assigning a cause ('illah) for a ruling; according to Hanafis, it is synonymous with qiyas.
تعدیہ (ta'diyah): Transitivity of the ruling from the original case (asl) to the branch (far') via the 'illah.
علت قاصرہ ('illah qasirah): A non-transitive cause that only applies to the original case and does not extend to other cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis require transitivity (ta'diyah) in ta'lil?
A) Because without transitivity, the ruling cannot be applied to any new case.
B) Because ta'lil does not produce certainty or obligatory action, so its only benefit is extending the ruling beyond the original text.
C) Because Shafi'is rejected transitivity, so Hanafis insisted on it out of opposition.
D) Because the Quran commands Muslims to seek the general benefit of rulings.

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, ta'lil without ta'diyah is futile; the only benefit of a cause is transitivity.

Types of 'Illal and Methods of Daf: Tardiyyah and Mu'aththirah
Introducing division of 'illal and four methods of daf' for tardiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an 'illah as tardiyyah or mu'aththirah, and apply the four methods of daf' for the tardiyyah type, especially al-qawl bi-mujab.

Core Idea
A formal 'illah (tardiyyah) can be refuted by four methods; the strongest is al-qawl bi-mujab which concedes the opponent's ground but turns it to your advantage.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, identifying the type of 'illah is crucial for constructing or refuting analogies. As per Al-Husami, 'illal are divided into two categories: tardiyyah (formal) and mu'aththirah (effective). This lesson explains the nature of each and provides four methods to refute a formal 'illah, with a focused exploration of the first method—al-qawl bi-mujab—using the classic example of intention in fasting Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of 'illah
Recognize that tardiyyah is merely concomitant and lacks an apparent effective attribute (wasf munasib), while mu'aththirah has a clear effective quality that can be the basis of istinbat.
Think of tardiyyah as a formal cause that accompanies the ruling but does not explain why the ruling is there.
2
Memorize the four methods of daf' for tardiyyah
List them from the text: (1) al-qawl bi-mujabil 'illah, (2) al-mumana'ah, (3) bayan fasad al-wad', (4) al-munaqadah. Know the Arabic terms and their meanings.
These methods target the 'illah itself, not the asl or far'.
3
Unpack al-qawl bi-mujab
This method accepts the opponent's 'illah and its logical consequence but shows that the consequence actually supports your position or does not harm it. It is a powerful concession-based rebuttal.
It requires careful analysis of what the 'illah necessarily entails.
4
Apply the method to the fasting example
The opponent argues that an obligatory fast requires specific intention (ta'yin). Using al-qawl bi-mujab, the Hanafi accepts that but argues that in Ramadan, an absolute intention (itlaq) is effectively a specific intention because the month is already certain. Thus, the opponent's own condition is met.
This shows how the Hanafi school can uphold its view while conceding the premise.
