العلة
ثُمَّ الْمُمَانَعَةُ ثُمَّ بَيَانُ فَسَادِ الْوَضْع ثُمَ الْمُنَاقَضَةُ لَمَّا الْقَوْلُ بِمُوْجَبِ فَالْتِرَامُ مَا يُلْزِمَهُ الْمُعَلَّلَ بِتَعْلِيلِهِ وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ قَوْلِهِمْ فِي صَوْمِ رَمْضَانَ أَنَّهُ صَوْمُ فَرْضِ فَلَا يَتَأَذَى إِلَّا بِتَعْيِينِ النّيَةِ فَيُقَالُ لَهُمْ عِنْدَ نَالَا يَصِحُ إِلَّا بِتَعْبِيْنِ النَّيَّةِ
69
وَإِنَّمَا نُجَوزهُ بِاطْلَاقِ النِّيَةِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ تَعْيِينْ
ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال دفع قیاس تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ علتوں کی دوقسمیں ہیں، طردیہ، مؤثرہ ، اور ان دونوں قسموں میں
And when we come to its refutation (daf'), we say: The 'illal (causes) are of two types: tardiyyah (formal) and mu'aththirah (effective). For each of the two divisions there are methods of refutation. As for the methods of refuting the formal 'illal, they are four: (1) al-qawl bi-mujabil 'illah (accepting the consequence of the 'illah), (2) al-mumana'ah (denial), (3) bayan fasad al-wad' (showing the invalidity of the postulate), and (4) al-munaqadah (contradiction). As for al-qawl bi-mujab, it is to accept what the opponent's ta'lil leads to (i.e., conceding the point but drawing a different conclusion). Example: their statement concerning the fast of Ramadan that 'it is an obligatory fast, so it is not affected except by specifying the intention (ta'yin al-niyyah).' Then it is said to them: 'As for [i.e., according to you?], it is not valid except with specifying the intention, but we permit it with an absolute intention (itlaq al-niyyah) considering it as specification (ta'yin).'
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage introduces a classification of 'illal (causes) in legal reasoning, and the methods of refuting them. The 'illal are divided into two types: tardiyyah (formal/terminal) and mu'aththirah (effective). Tardiyyah 'illah is one that does not have a clear effective quality but is merely formal. For refuting such 'illal, there are four methods: (1) al-qawl bi-mujabil 'illah: accepting the opponent's 'illah but showing that it leads to a consequence that does not harm your position, or that the consequence is already conceded. (2) al-mumana'ah: denying the existence of the 'illah or its description. (3) bayan fasad al-wad': showing that the 'illah is incorrectly constructed or invalid. (4) al-munaqadah: showing that the 'illah leads to a contradiction. The text gives an example: in the case of fasting in Ramadan, the opponent claims that an obligatory fast requires a specific intention (ta'yin al-niyyah) to be valid. The Hanafi response using al-qawl bi-mujab is to accept that specification is needed, but then argue that an absolute intention (itlaq) in Ramadan actually constitutes specification by default because the month is already specified by the calendar. Thus the opponent's own criterion is satisfied.

Key Terms
علة طردية ('illah tardiyyah): A formal cause that accompanies the ruling but does not have an apparent effective quality; it is used in formal analogies.
دفع القياس (daf' al-qiyas): Methods of refuting an analogy by attacking the 'illah or its application.
القول بموجب العلة (al-qawl bi-mujab al-'illah): Accepting the opponent's 'illah but showing that the conclusion does not harm your position, or that the opponent's own conditions lead to your conclusion.
الممانعة (al-mumana'ah): Denying the existence or description of the 'illah in the original case or the branch.
فساد الوضع (fasad al-wad'): Showing that the opponent's 'illah is incorrectly constructed or that the attribute is not properly tied to the ruling.
المناقضة (al-munaqadah): Showing that the 'illah leads to a contradictory ruling either in the same case or in another accepted case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many methods are there for refuting a formal 'illah (tardiyyah)?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The four methods of daf' for tardiyyah 'illah—especially al-qawl bi-mujab—are essential tools in Hanafi usul for neutralizing formal objections.

Necessity of Ta'diyah in Ta'lil
Analyzing the necessity of ta'diyah in causal reasoning for qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of ta'diyah in ta'lil and explain why the Hanafi school considers it necessary, using the objection-response structure from the source.

Core Idea
A non-transitive cause adds nothing to the text; only ta'diyah makes ta'lil beneficial in qiyas.

In this passage, the Hanafi position on causal reasoning in qiyas is defended against a key objection. The objector argues that even a non-transitive cause has value in confirming specificity. The Hanafi response dismantles this claim, showing that the text itself already establishes specificity, and therefore the only meaningful function of ta'lil is to extend the ruling to new cases. This lesson walks through each part of the argument to clarify why ta'diyah is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
State the objector's claim that a non-transitive cause ('illah qasira) is sufficient for ta'lil because it confirms the ruling's specificity.
The objector focuses on specification as a benefit.
2
Trace the Hanafi First Response
Explain why the text's own form already indicates specificity, making ta'lil without ta'diyah redundant.
The text's sighah (form) itself shows the ruling is restricted to the stated case.
3
Trace the Hanafi Second Response
Understand the argument that even if a non-transitive cause is permissible, the mujtahid can also use a transitive cause, which would remove specificity and extend the ruling.
This second response covers the possibility of alternative causes.
4
Conclude on Necessity
Synthesize that ta'lil without ta'diyah provides no additional benefit, so ta'diyah is necessary.
The only real benefit of ta'lil is transitivity.

فرع کی طرف حکم کو متعدی کرنا تاکہ تعلیل کا باطل ہونا لازم نہ آئے ، اس لئے تعدیہ کو لازم قرار دیا۔ فان قيل التعلیل : معترض کہتا ہے کہ تعلیل میں اگر تعدیہ نہ بھی ہو، بلکہ تعلیل علت قاصرہ سے یعنی علت غیر متعدیہ سے ہو، تو تعلیل سے یہ فائدہ تو ضرور حاصل ہو جائے گا کہ نص کا حکم اسی نص کے ساتھ خاص ہے، تو نص کے حکم کا نص کے ساتھ خاص ہونا یہ تعلیل سے معلوم ہوا، تو اتنا فائدہ کافی ہے، خواہ مخواہ تعدیہ کے چکر میں پڑ کر کیوں وقت ضائع کرتے ہیں؟ مصنف عالیہ نے ایک جواب تو یہ دیا کہ اختصاص کا جو فائدہ آپ بتارہے ہیں وہ تو بغیر تعلیل کے بھی حاصل ہے، اس لئے کہ نص خود اپنے صیغہ کی وجہ سے اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ حکم صرف منصوص علیہ میں ثابت ہے، اس کے علاوہ میں ثابت نہیں ہے اور تعلیل سے اس میں عموم کا فائدہ ہوتا ہے، جس سے حکم دوسری طرف متعدی ہوتا ہے، اگر الله اس تعدیہ کونہ مانو گے تو تعلیل بیکار ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ اختصاص تو پہلے سے ہی موجود ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ اصل میں ایسے دو وصفوں کا جمع ہونا جائز ہے جو متعدی ہوں ، ایک کا تعدیہ قوی اور دوسرے کا ہلکا ہو ، اسی طرح یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ اصل میں ایسے دو وصف جمع ہوں ، جن میں ایک متعدی اور دوسرا غیر متعدی ہو، جب بات یوں ہے تو علت غیر متعدیہ کے ساتھ تحلیل مجتہد کو علت متعدیہ کے ساتھ تعلیل سے نہیں روکے گی یعنی مجتہد جیسے علت غیر متعدیہ کے ساتھ تعلیل پیش کر سکتا ہے، ( جس میں اختصاص ہو سکتا ہے ) ایسے ہی علت متعدیہ کے ساتھ بھی تعلیل پیش کر سکتا ہے، جب علت متعدیہ کے ساتھ وہ تعلیل کرے گا تو یہ حکم اور جگہ متعدی ہوگا تو حکم کا اصل کے ساتھ خاص رہنے کا فائدہ کہاں رہے گا ، باطل ہو جائے گا، پس آخر میں اسی بات پر آنا پڑے گا کہ تعلیل میں تعدیہ کے علاوہ کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے، لہذا تعلیل کے لئے تعد یہ لازم ہے۔
Making the ruling transitive to the branch so that the invalidity of the causation does not become necessary, therefore transitivity was deemed necessary. If it is said: 'The objector says that if transitivity is not present in causation, but rather causation is with a non-transitive cause, then from causation this benefit will definitely be obtained: that the ruling of the text is specific to that text. So the ruling of the text being specific to the text is known from causation, so this benefit is sufficient. Why waste time unnecessarily getting involved in the issue of transitivity?' The noble author gave one answer: that the benefit of specification you mention is obtained without causation, because the text itself by its form indicates that the ruling is established only for the specified case, not for others, and causation provides the benefit of generality, by which the ruling becomes transitive to other cases. If you do not accept this transitivity, causation becomes useless, because specification already exists. The second answer is that it is permissible for two descriptions to be combined in the original, both of which are transitive, one with strong transitivity and the other with weak transitivity. Similarly, it is permissible for two descriptions to be combined in the original, one transitive and the other non-transitive. When this is the case, the mujtahid's analysis with a non-transitive cause will not prevent him from using a transitive cause for causation. That is, just as the mujtahid can present a causation with a non-transitive cause (which can have specification), similarly he can present a causation with a transitive cause. When he does causation with a transitive cause, this ruling will become transitive to other places, so where will the benefit of the ruling remaining specific to the original remain? It will become invalid. So eventually one must come to the conclusion that there is no benefit in causation besides transitivity. Therefore, transitivity is necessary for causation.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of an objection and response regarding the necessity of ta'diyah (transitivity) in ta'lil (causal reasoning) for qiyas. The author argues that ta'lil without ta'diyah is useless. An objector claims that even a non-transitive cause provides the benefit of confirming that the ruling is specific to the text. The author gives two responses: first, that the text itself already indicates specificity through its own form, so the only additional benefit of ta'lil is generalization and transitivity. Second, even if a non-transitive cause is acceptable in principle, using a transitive cause removes the ruling's specificity and makes it applicable elsewhere, which is the true purpose of ta'lil. All explanations and examples are based on Hanafi usul al-fiqh, focusing on the role of 'illah in qiyas.

Key Terms
تعلیل (ta'lil): Causal reasoning in qiyas; assigning a cause for a ruling.
تعدیہ (ta'diyah): Transitivity of the cause; extending the ruling to other cases.
علت قاصرہ ('illah qasira): A non-transitive cause that does not extend beyond the original case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main benefit of ta'lil (causation) in qiyas?
A) To confirm that the ruling is specific to the original case.
B) To extend the ruling to other cases through transitivity.
C) To establish the weakness of the opponent's argument.
D) To prove the existence of a cause without any effect.

Key Takeaway
Transitivity (ta'diyah) is essential for ta'lil because without it, causal reasoning provides no benefit beyond what the text already states.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Types of 'Illah and Methods of Refuting Qiyas
Memorization anchor: types of 'illah and refutation methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'illat tardiyya and 'illat mu'aththira and list the four Hanafi methods for refuting formal causes.

Core Idea
Hanafi usul accepts only effective causes; formal causes are refuted by four established methods.

In this passage, the author of Al-Husami introduces the classification of causes in qiyas and provides the Hanafi toolkit for refuting arguments based on formal causes. This is a core memorization anchor for students of usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of 'illah
Define 'illat tardiyya (formal cause) and 'illat mu'aththira (effective cause). Note that formal causes lack proven effectiveness (ta'thir).
Formal cause: ruling revolves with existence/non-existence of cause. Effective cause: influence proven by nass or ijma'.
2
State the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
Hanafis accept only effective causes; Shafi'is accept formal causes as valid for qiyas.
This difference leads to distinct methods of refutation.
3
List the four methods of refuting formal causes
Memorize: qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, mumana'ah, fasad al-wad', munaqadah.
These are the tools to dismantle an opponent's formal cause argument.
4
Apply the first method to the Ramadan fast example
Show how Hanafis accept the Shafi'i's cause (obligation) but argue that absolute intention is a form of specification, thus the ruling (validity with absolute intention) differs.
This illustrates qawl bi-mujab al-'illah in action.

حال علل کر دیہ کو دفع کرنے کے طریقے چار ہیں، قول بموجب العلة پھر ممانعت ، پھر فساد وضع کا بیان، پھر مناقضہ ۔ بہر حال قول بموجب العالیہ تو وہ اس حکم کا التزام ہے جس کو معلل اپنی تعلیل سے لازم کرتا ہے، اور یہ شوافع کے قول کے مثل ہے رمضان کے روزہ میں، کہ یہ صوم رمضان ) فرض روزہ ہے پس ادا نہیں ہو گا مگر نیت کی تعیین سے ، تو شوافع سے کہا جائے گا کہ ہمارے نزدیک ( بھی ) بغیر تعیین نیت کے روز پیچ نہیں جاسکتا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ علت کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) طردیہ (۲) مؤثرہ ، علت طرد یہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ حکم اس علت کے وجود اور عدم کے ساتھ دائر ہو، اور بعض کے نزدیک صرف وجود کے ساتھ دائر ہو یعنی علت ہو تو حکم ہو اور نہ ہو تو حکم بھی نہ ہو، اور بعض کے نزدیک علت ہو تو حکم کا وجود ہو اور علت نہ ہو تو وہ حکم کے وجود و عدم کا کوئی فیصلہ نہیں کرتے ، علت طرد یہ میں تاثیر کو نہیں دیکھا جاتا ، شوافع اس سے استدلال کرتے ہیں ، اور ہمارے نزدیک اس سے استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے۔۔ ہمارے نزدیک علت مؤثرہ سے استدلال ہوتا ہے، یعنی ایسی علت جس کی تاثیر نص یا اجماع سے دوسری جگہ ظاہر ہو چکی ہو، جس کی تفصیل اور اقسام اربعہ ہم ماقبل میں ذکر کر چکے۔ بہر حال امام شافعی علت طردیہ سے استدلال کرتے ہیں، اور ہم علت مؤثرہ سے استدلال کرتے ہیں ، تو اس باب میں وہ ہم پر کچھ اعتراضات کرتے ہیں، اور ہم جواب دیتے ہیں، اور ہم علت طرد یہ پر کچھ ایسے اعتراض کرتے ہیں جن سے شوافع علت مؤثرہ کے ماننے پر مجبور ہوں ، ہم شوافع پر جو اعتراضات کرتے ہیں جن سے علت طر د یہ کا دفع ہوتا ہے اس کی چار قسمیں ہیں ، (۱) قول بموجب العلہ (۲) ممانعت (۳) فساد وضع (۴) مناقضہ ۔ قول بموجب العلہ یہ ہے کہ فریق مخالف نے جو علت بیان کی ہے، اس کو تسلیم کر کے ہم ایسا نکتہ چھوڑیں کہ علت تو وہی رہے اور حکم مختلف ہو جائے ، بالفاظ دیگر معلن اپنی علت سے جو الزام دے رہا ہے اس کو قبول کر کے حکم کو اس کے خلاف ثابت کیا جائے۔ جیسے شوافع کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کا روزہ بغیر تعیین نیت کے صحیح نہیں ہوتا ہے، یہ استدلال شوافع نے علت طردیہ سے کیا ہے، اس طرح کہ رمضان کا روزہ فرض ہے اور جہاں فرضیت ہوگی وہاں تعیین نیت ضروری ہے جیسے فرض نماز ، قضا اور کفارہ کا روزہ ، ان میں تعیین نیت ضروری ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک رمضان کے روزہ کے لئے مطلق نیست کافی ہے۔ تو ہم نے شوافع کی علت کو تسلیم کر لیا کہ ہمارے نزدیک بھی فرض بغیر تعیین نیت کے صحیح نہیں ہے، لیکن ہم مطلق نیست سے جواز کے قائل اس لئے ہیں کہ تعیین
And when it comes to refutation, we say: causes are of two types: formal (tardiyya) and effective (mu'aththira). For each of the two types, there are several kinds of refutation. The methods of refuting formal causes are four: acceptance of the mandate of the cause, then prevention, then demonstration of the corruption of the positing, then contradiction. As for acceptance of the mandate: it is the acknowledgement of what the one giving the cause necessitates by his causation. That is like their statement regarding the fast of Ramadan: 'It is an obligatory fast, so it is only valid with specification of intention.' Then they are told: in our view, it is also not valid without specification of intention, and we permit it with absolute intention on the basis that absolute intention is itself specification. Explanation: The author is explaining the refutation of qiyas, i.e., how the opponent's qiyas can be refuted. He says: Causes are of two types: (1) Formal (tardiyya) (2) Effective (mu'aththira). Formal cause is that the ruling revolves around the existence and non-existence of the cause; according to some, it revolves only around existence—i.e., if the cause exists, the ruling exists; if not, the ruling does not exist. According to others, if the cause exists, the ruling exists; if it does not, they make no judgment about the ruling's existence or non-existence. In formal cause, effectiveness is not considered. The Shafi'is use it for argumentation, but in our view, argumentation with it is not correct. In our view, argumentation is with effective cause, i.e., a cause whose effectiveness has been shown elsewhere by text or consensus, the details and four types of which we have mentioned previously. In any case, Imam al-Shafi'i argues with formal causes, but we argue with effective causes. In this chapter, they raise some objections against us, and we answer. We raise such objections against formal causes that the Shafi'is are compelled to accept effective causes. The objections we raise against the Shafi'is by which formal causes are refuted are of four types: (1) Acceptance of the mandate of the cause (qawl bi-mujab al-'illah); (2) Prevention (mumana'ah); (3) Demonstration of the corruption of the positing (fasad al-wad'); (4) Contradiction (munaqadah). Acceptance of the mandate of the cause is that we accept the cause presented by the opponent, but then we introduce a point such that the cause remains the same but the ruling becomes different. In other words, we accept the claim that the opponent makes with his cause and then prove the ruling contrary to it. For example, the Shafi'is say that the fast of Ramadan is not valid without specification of intention. This argumentation of the Shafi'is is with a formal cause, as follows: The fast of Ramadan is obligatory, and wherever obligation exists, specification of intention is necessary, like obligatory prayer, and the fast of qada' and kaffarah require specification of intention. In our view, for the fast of Ramadan, absolute intention is sufficient. So we accepted the Shafi'i's cause: that in our view too, an obligatory act is not valid without specification of intention, but we hold that absolute intention is permissible because specification...
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational usul al-fiqh rule about types of 'illah (cause) in qiyas and methods of refuting the opponent's qiyas. The author distinguishes between 'illat tardiyya (formal cause) and 'illat mu'aththira (effective cause). The Hanafi position is that only effective causes—those whose ta'thir (influence) is established by nass or ijma'—are valid for qiyas. The Shafi'i school uses formal causes, which Hanafis reject. To refute arguments based on formal causes, four methods are given: (1) qawl bi-mujab al-'illah (accepting the cause but showing the ruling differs), (2) mumana'ah (denying that the cause exists in the original or branch), (3) fasad al-wad' (showing the cause is improperly constructed), and (4) munaqadah (showing a contradiction in the opponent's reasoning). The example of Ramadan fast and intention illustrates the first method: the Hanafis accept that obligatory acts require intention, but argue that absolute intention is a form of specification, thus the ruling stands. All explanations are within the Hanafi usul framework, emphasizing the hierarchy of evidence and the conditions for valid qiyas.

Key Terms
علة طردية (illat tardiyya): A formal cause that is merely concomitant with the ruling, showing no effective influence.
علة مؤثرة (illat mu'aththira): An effective cause whose influence is proven by nass or ijma'.
قول بموجب العلة (qawl bi-mujab al-'illah): A method of refutation where the opponent's cause is accepted but the ruling is shown to be different.
ممانعة (mumana'ah): Denial of the opponent's claim that the cause is present in the original or branch.
فساد الوضع (fasad al-wad'): Demonstrating that the cause is incorrectly constructed or does not fit the ruling.
مناقضة (munaqadah): Showing contradiction in the opponent's argument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of 'illah is accepted for qiyas according to the Hanafi school as per this passage?
A) 'Illat tardiyya
B) 'Illat mu'aththira
C) Both are accepted
D) Neither is accepted

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, only effective causes ('illat mu'aththira) are valid for qiyas; formal causes are refuted by four specific methods.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Methods of Refuting Analogy: Qawl bi-Mujab al-‘Illah and Mumana‘ah
Explaining two Hanafi methods to refute an opponent's qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two methods of refuting qiyas (qawl bi-mujab al-‘illah and mumana‘ah) and apply them to Hanafi-Shafi'i disputes.

Core Idea
In usul al-fiqh, you can defeat an analogy by accepting its cause but changing the ruling, or by denying a premise.

The Hanafi school has developed sophisticated methods to refute analogical arguments (qiyas) advanced by opponents, particularly the Shafi'is. This lesson introduces two key methods: qawl bi-mujab al-‘illah (accepting the cause but proving a different ruling) and mumana‘ah (denial of a premise). Using the classic debates on Ramadan fasting and expiation, you will learn how these tools preserve the integrity of Hanafi positions while engaging seriously with opposing proofs.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish tardiyah vs mu'aththirah cause
Recognize that the Shafi'is often use a tardiyah cause (mere accompaniment) while Hanafis require a mu'aththirah cause (proven efficacy). This sets the stage for refutation.
The passage explains the two types of 'illah early on.
2
Understand qawl bi-mujab al-'illah
Learn that this method accepts the opponent's cause but introduces a nuance that changes the ruling while keeping the cause intact.
Key: you do not deny the cause; you accept it and then distinguish.
3
Apply to the Ramadan fast example
Work through the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute: Shafi'i says obligatory acts need specified intention; Hanafi accepts but says shari'ah specification suffices, so absolute intention works.
This is the classic illustration in the text.
4
Learn the four types of mumana'ah
Mumana'ah is denial of a premise. The four types are: denial of the attribute itself, its suitability for the ruling, the ruling itself, or the attribution of the ruling to the attribute.
Each type targets a different part of the opponent's argument.
5
Apply mumana'ah to the expiation example
The Shafi'i claimed that sexual intercourse is the cause of expiation; Hanafis deny that attribute (mumana'ah fi nafs al-wasf) and instead assert deliberate breaking as the cause.
This shows the first type of mumana'ah in action.

۲۸۲
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
سے ہر ایک پر چند طرح کے اعتراضات ہیں، اور بہر حال علل کر دیہ کو دفع کرنے کے طریقے چار ہیں، قول بموجب العلة پھر ممانعت ، پھر فساد وضع کا بیان، پھر مناقضہ ۔ بہر حال قول بموجب العالیہ تو وہ اس حکم کا التزام ہے جس کو معلل اپنی تعلیل سے لازم کرتا ہے، اور یہ شوافع کے قول کے مثل ہے رمضان کے روزہ میں، کہ یہ صوم رمضان ) فرض روزہ ہے پس ادا نہیں ہو گا مگر نیت کی تعیین سے ، تو شوافع سے کہا جائے گا کہ ہمارے نزدیک ( بھی ) بغیر تعیین نیت کے روز پیچ نہیں ہوگا، اور ہم اس کو اطلاق نیت کے ساتھ جائز قرار دیتے ہیں اس بنا پر کہ اطلاق نیت ( بھی ) تعیین ہے۔ تشریح:- مصنف ، دفع قیاس کو بیان فرمارہے ہیں، یعنی یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ مخالف کے قیاس کو کیسے دفع کیا جاسکتا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ علت کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) طردیہ (۲) مؤثرہ ، علت طرد یہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ حکم اس علت کے وجود اور عدم کے ساتھ دائر ہو، اور بعض کے نزدیک صرف وجود کے ساتھ دائر ہو یعنی علت ہو تو حکم ہو اور نہ ہو تو حکم بھی نہ ہو، اور بعض کے نزدیک علت ہو تو حکم کا وجود ہو اور علت نہ ہو تو وہ حکم کے وجود و عدم کا کوئی فیصلہ نہیں کرتے ، علت طرد یہ میں تاثیر کو نہیں دیکھا جاتا ، شوافع اس سے استدلال کرتے ہیں ، اور ہمارے نزدیک اس سے استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے۔۔ ہمارے نزدیک علت مؤثرہ سے استدلال ہوتا ہے، یعنی ایسی علت جس کی تاثیر نص یا اجماع سے دوسری جگہ ظاہر ہو چکی ہو، جس کی تفصیل اور اقسام اربعہ ہم ماقبل میں ذکر کر چکے۔ بہر حال امام شافعی علت طردیہ سے استدلال کرتے ہیں، اور ہم علت مؤثرہ سے استدلال کرتے ہیں ، تو اس باب میں وہ ہم پر کچھ اعتراضات کرتے ہیں، اور ہم جواب دیتے ہیں، اور ہم علت طرد یہ پر کچھ ایسے اعتراض کرتے ہیں جن سے شوافع علت مؤثرہ کے ماننے پر مجبور ہوں ، ہم شوافع پر جو اعتراضات کرتے ہیں جن سے علت طر د یہ کا دفع ہوتا ہے اس کی چار قسمیں ہیں ، (۱) قول بموجب العلہ (۲) ممانعت (۳) فساد وضع (۴) مناقضہ ۔ قول بموجب العلہ یہ ہے کہ فریق مخالف نے جو علت بیان کی ہے، اس کو تسلیم کر کے ہم ایسا نکتہ چھوڑیں کہ علت تو وہی رہے اور حکم مختلف ہو جائے ، بالفاظ دیگر معلن اپنی علت سے جو الزام دے رہا ہے اس کو قبول کر کے حکم کو اس کے خلاف ثابت کیا جائے۔ جیسے شوافع کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کا روزہ بغیر تعیین نیت کے صحیح نہیں ہوتا ہے، یہ استدلال شوافع نے علت طردیہ سے کیا ہے، اس طرح کہ رمضان کا روزہ فرض ہے اور جہاں فرضیت ہوگی وہاں تعیین نیت ضروری ہے جیسے فرض نماز ، قضا اور کفارہ کا روزہ ، ان میں تعیین نیت ضروری ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک رمضان کے روزہ کے لئے مطلق نیست کافی ہے۔ تو ہم نے شوافع کی علت کو تسلیم کر لیا کہ ہمارے نزدیک بھی فرض بغیر تعیین نیت کے صحیح نہیں ہے، لیکن ہم مطلق نیست سے جواز کے قائل اس لئے ہیں کہ تعیین دو طرح کی ہیں، ایک یہ کہ بندہ خود تعیین کرے جیسے نذر کا روزہ اور دوم یہ کہ شریعت تعیین کرے، رمضان کے روزے میں شریعت کی تعیین موجود ہے، لہذا مطلق نیت سے بھی رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا ۔۔ تو یہاں ہم نے فریق مخالف کی علت کو تسلیم کر کے حکم اس کے خلاف ثابت کیا، مطلق نیت سے روزہ کا ادا ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو ہم نے شوافع کے اس استدلال کو دفع کر دیا، اس کا نام ہے قول بموجب العلۃ ۔
وَأَمَّا الْمُمَانَعَةُ فَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامِ مُمَانَعَةٌ فِي نَفْسِ الْوَصْفِ وَفِي صَلَاحِهِ لِلْحُكْمِ وَفِي نَفْسِ الْحُكْمِ وَفِي نِسْبَتِهِ إِلَى الْوَصْفِ ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال ممانعت پس وہ چار قسم پر ہے، نفس وصف کا انکار کر دینا ، وصف کا حکم کے لئے صالح ہونے سے انکار کر دینا نفس حکم کا انکار کر دینا ، وصف کی طرف حکم کے منسوب ہونے کا انکار کرنا۔ تشریح : - علت طرد یہ کو دفع کرنے کا دوسرا طریقہ ممانعت ہے، ممانعت اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ معترض مغلک کی دلیل کے تمام مقدمات کو یا بعض متعین اجزا کو قبول کرنے سے انکار کر دے۔ ممانعت کی چار قسمیں ہیں ، (۱) نفس وصف کا انکار کرنا (۲) وصف کا صالح الحکم ہونے کا انکار کرنا (۳) نفس حکم کا انکار کرنا (۴) حکم کے وصف کی طرف منسوب ہونے کا انکار کرنا۔ پہلی قسم : ممانعت في نفس الوصف یہ ہے کہ معتل نے جس وصف کو علت قرار دیا ہے، معترض اس وصف کو علت ماننے سے انکار کر دے۔ جیسے امام شافعی سے کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کا روزہ اگر جماع سے توڑا ہے تو کفارہ واجب ہے اور اگر کھانے پینے سے توڑا ہے تو کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے، تو کفارہ کا سبب انہوں نے جماع کو قرار دیا۔ اس پر ہم احناف کہتے ہیں کہ جماع کو کفارہ کی علت ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے ، بلکہ عمداً افطار ( روزہ توڑنا) کفارہ کی علت ہے، اور عمداً افطار کھانے پینے سے بھی ہوتا ہے، لہذا کھانے پینے سے بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا، جماع اگر علت ہوتا تو بھول کر جماع سے بھی کفارہ واجب ہوتا حالانکہ بھول کر جماع سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ غرض معلل نے جس وصف کو حکم کی علت قرار دیا معترض نے اس علت کو توڑ دیا۔ دوسری قسم: یہ ہے کہ معترض معلل کے وصف کو تو تسلیم کرے لیکن یہ تسلیم نہ کرے کہ اس وصف میں حکم کو ثابت کرنے کی صلاحیت ہے، جیسے امام شافعی اللہ نے باکرہ پر ولایت کو ثابت کرنے کی علت بکارت کو قرار دیا، اور دلیل یہ دی کہ باکرہ مردوں کے ساتھ زندگی گزارنے کا تجربہ نہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے نکاح کے مصالح سے ناواقف ہے، اس لئے باکرہ پر ولایت ثابت ہوگی۔ اس پر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وصف بکارت تو تسلیم ہے لیکن اس میں حکم کی علت
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi 282 Commentary Urdu of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. There are several types of objections to each, and in any case the methods to refute [the opponent's] causal reasoning are four: qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, then mumana'ah, then fasad al-wad', then munaqadah. In any case, qawl bi-mujab al-'illah is that one accepts the ruling which the proponent of the cause [mu'allil] demands by his causal explanation, and it is similar to the saying of the Shafi'is regarding the fast of Ramadan: that this fast of Ramadan is an obligatory fast, so it will not be performed except with specification (ta'yin) of intention. Then it will be said to the Shafi'is: 'In our view (also) the fast will not be valid without specification of intention, but we permit it with absolute (mutlaq) intention, on the basis that absolute intention is (also) specification.' Explanation: The author is explaining the refutation of analogy, i.e., he is explaining how the opponent's analogy can be refuted. So he said that the cause ('illah) is of two types: (1) tardiyah, (2) mu'aththirah. The tardiyah cause is that the ruling revolves around the existence and non-existence of this cause; according to some, it revolves only around its existence, i.e., if the cause is present then the ruling is present, and if it is absent then the ruling is also absent; and according to some, if the cause is present then the ruling exists, and if the cause is absent then they do not decide anything about the existence or non-existence of the ruling. In a tardiyah cause, efficacy (ta'thir) is not considered. The Shafi'is use it as proof, and in our view it is not valid to use it as proof. In our view, proof is based on the mu'aththirah cause, i.e., a cause whose efficacy has been shown elsewhere by text or consensus, whose details and four types we have mentioned previously. In any case, Imam al-Shafi'i uses the tardiyah cause as proof, and we use the mu'aththirah cause as proof. So in this chapter they make some objections against us, and we give answers. And we make some objections against the tardiyah cause that compel the Shafi'is to accept the mu'aththirah cause. The objections we make against the Shafi'is by which the tardiyah cause is refuted are of four types: (1) qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, (2) mumana'ah, (3) fasad al-wad', (4) munaqadah. Qawl bi-mujab al-'illah is that the opponent states a cause, and we accept it but then introduce a point such that the cause remains the same but the ruling becomes different; in other words, we accept the implication (ilzam) that the mu'allil is demanding by his cause and then prove the ruling contrary to it. For example, the Shafi'is say that the fast of Ramadan is not valid without specification of intention; they have used the tardiyah cause as proof, in that the fast of Ramadan is obligatory, and wherever there is obligation, specification of intention is necessary, like obligatory prayer, and the fasts of qada and kaffarah; in these, specification of intention is necessary. In our view, absolute intention is sufficient for the fast of Ramadan. So we have accepted the Shafi'is' cause: in our view too, an obligation is not valid without specification of intention, but we hold permissibility with absolute intention because specification is of two types: one is that the servant himself specifies, like the fast of a vow, and the second is that the shari'ah specifies; in the fast of Ramadan, the shari'ah's specification exists, so the fast of Ramadan will be performed even with absolute intention. So here we accepted the opponent's cause and proved the ruling contrary to it; we proved the validity of the fast with absolute intention, thus we refuted the Shafi'is' argument. This is called qawl bi-mujab al-'illah. And as for mumana'ah, it is of four types: mumana'ah concerning the attribute (wasf) itself, concerning its suitability (salahiyyah) for the ruling, concerning the ruling itself, and concerning its attribution (nisbah) to the attribute. Explanation: The second method to refute the tardiyah cause is mumana'ah. Mumana'ah is that the objector (mu'tarid) refuses to accept all the premises of the opponent's proof or some specific parts. Mumana'ah has four types: (1) denial of the attribute itself, (2) denial that the attribute is suitable for the ruling, (3) denial of the ruling itself, (4) denial of the attribution of the ruling to the attribute. The first type: mumana'ah fi nafs al-wasf is that the mu'allil has considered a certain attribute as the cause; the objector refuses to accept that attribute as the cause. For example, the Shafi'is say that if the fast of Ramadan is broken by sexual intercourse, expiation (kaffarah) is obligatory, and if it is broken by eating or drinking, expiation is not obligatory. So they made sexual intercourse the cause of expiation. We Hanafis say: we do not accept sexual intercourse as the cause of expiation; rather, deliberate breaking of the fast (ta'ammud iftar) is the cause of expiation, and deliberate breaking occurs through eating and drinking as well, so expiation will be obligatory from eating and drinking too. If sexual intercourse were the cause, then expiation would also be obligatory if one forgets and has intercourse, but expiation is not obligatory in that case. In short, the attribute that the mu'allil made the cause of the ruling, the objector refuted it. The second type: the objector accepts the attribute of the mu'allil but does not accept that this attribute has the capacity to establish the ruling. For example, Imam al-Shafi'i made virginity (bukarah) the cause for establishing guardianship (wilayah) over a virgin, giving the proof that a virgin, due to lack of experience of living with men, is unaware of the interests of marriage, so guardianship over a virgin is established. We say: the attribute of virginity is accepted, but it does not have the capacity to be the cause of the ruling.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of how a Hanafi jurist can refute an opponent's analogy (qiyas) in usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between two types of causes ('illah): tardiyah (a cause that merely accompanies the ruling) and mu'aththirah (a cause whose efficacy is independently verified). The Shafi'is are described as relying on the tardiyah cause, while the Hanafis insist on the mu'aththirah cause. The text then lists four methods to refute the tardiyah cause: qawl bi-mujab al-'illah (accepting the cause but proving a different ruling), mumana'ah (denial of premises), fasad al-wad' (corruption of the basis), and munaqadah (contradiction). The passage elaborates on the first two methods with concrete examples. In qawl bi-mujab al-'illah, the Hanafi accepts the Shafi'i assertion that obligatory acts require specified intention, but argues that the fast of Ramadan has specification by the shari'ah itself, so absolute intention suffices. Thus the ruling is changed while the cause is conserved. In mumana'ah, the objector denies one of four elements: the attribute itself (e.g., rejecting that sexual intercourse is the cause of expiation—Hanafis hold that deliberate breaking is the cause), the attribute's suitability for the ruling (e.g., accepting virginity but denying it necessitates guardianship), the ruling itself, or the attribution of the ruling to the attribute. The examples are drawn from classic Hanafi-Shafi'i disputes on fasting and marriage guardianship, illustrating how these methodological tools are used in substantive legal argumentation.

Key Terms
العلة الطردية (al-‘illah al-ṭardiyyah): A cause that merely accompanies the ruling in existence and non-existence, without proven efficacy
العلة المؤثرة (al-‘illah al-mu’aththirah): A cause whose efficacy (ta’thir) is established by text or consensus in another case
قول بموجب العلة (qawl bi-mūjab al-‘illah): Accepting the opponent's cause but proving a different ruling, thus refuting the analogy
الممانعة (al-mumāna‘ah): Denial of one of the premises in the opponent's proof; four subtypes

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi method of refuting analogy called qawl bi-mujab al-‘illah, what does the Hanafi do with the opponent's proposed cause (al-‘illah)?
A) Denies the cause entirely
B) Accepts the cause but proves a different ruling
C) Denies the ruling but accepts the cause
D) Accepts both the cause and the ruling

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of qawl bi-mujab al-‘illah allows a jurist to accept an opponent's causal reasoning while still arriving at a different ruling by identifying a legally relevant distinction.
